The Tathwib and Iqamah Phrases
Explains the addition of tathwib and iqamah phrase with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the additional phrases in the fajr adhan and iqamah, explain their proofs, and apply the Hanafi ruling that they are a confirmed sunnah specific to these calls.

Core Idea
Prayer is better than sleep' is a confirmed sunnah for fajr; 'The prayer has begun' is for iqamah.

In this lesson, we examine the specific phrases added to the adhan of fajr and to the iqamah. These are not random innovations but are based on explicit prophetic instruction and angelic practice. Understanding their rulings and rationale deepens our appreciation of the sunnah and helps avoid common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional phrases
Locate the two phrases: for fajr adhan, 'as-salatu khairun min an-naum' (prayer is better than sleep) repeated twice; for iqamah, 'qad qamati as-salah' (the prayer has begun) repeated twice.
The tathwib is specific to fajr; the iqamah phrase is universal.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof: the Prophet ordered Bilal to say the tathwib in fajr; the angel demonstrated the iqamah phrase.
These are ahad hadith but with clear indication of sunnah.
3
Analyze the wisdom
Understand why fajr is specified: it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so the reminder is especially needed.
Sleep can be a form of worship if intended for obedience, but prayer's reward is superior.
4
Consider the unresolved issue
Note the hesitation about whether to say the tathwib in the adhan for a missed fajr prayer.
The text leaves this as a point of hesitation; it is not definitively settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويزيد) المؤذن (بعد فلاح الفجر) قوله (الصلاة) خير من النوم) يكررها (مرتين) لأنّ النبي أمر به بلالاً رضي الله عنه، وخص به الفجر لأنه وقت نوم وغفلة) (و) يزيد (بعد فلاح الإقامة قد قامت الصلاة ويكررها مرتين) كما فعله الملك. قوله : (الصلاة خير من النوم) إنما كان النوم مشاركاً للصلاة في الخيرية لأنه قد يكون عبادة إذا كان وسيلة إلى تحصيل طاعة، أو ترك معصية، ولكونه راحة في الدنيا والصلاة راحة في الآخرة وراحة الآخرة أفضل. قاله في الشرح : وهل يأتي به في أذان الفائتة محل توقف
And the mu'adhdhin adds after the announcement of fajr the saying: 'Prayer is better than sleep' and repeats it twice, because the Prophet ordered Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) to do so, and it is specific to fajr because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness. And he adds after the announcement of iqamah: 'The prayer has indeed been established' and repeats it twice, as the angel did. His saying: 'Prayer is better than sleep' — sleep is only considered to share in goodness because it can be a form of worship if it is a means to attaining obedience or abandoning sin, and because it is rest in this world while prayer is rest in the Hereafter, and the rest of the Hereafter is superior. It is stated in the commentary: As to whether he says it in the adhan for a missed prayer, that is a point of hesitation.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that in the adhan for fajr prayer, the mu'adhdhin adds the phrase 'as-salatu khairun min an-naum' (Prayer is better than sleep) twice after saying 'hayya ala al-falah'. This is based on the Prophet's order to Bilal. It is specific to fajr because it is a time when people are asleep and may neglect prayer. Similarly, in the iqamah, after saying 'hayya ala al-falah', the mu'adhdhin adds 'qad qamati as-salah' (The prayer has indeed been established) twice, following the practice of the angel who taught the adhan. The commentary explains that sleep can be good as it may lead to worship, but prayer's benefit is superior. There is a question about whether to say 'as-salatu khairun min an-naum' in the adhan for a missed fajr prayer; the text leaves this unresolved.

Key Terms
التثويب (at-tathwib): The phrase 'as-salatu khairun min an-naum' said in the fajr adhan.
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qamati as-salah): The phrase said in the iqamah after 'hayya ala al-falah' to indicate that the prayer is about to begin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which adhan is the phrase 'as-salatu khairun min an-naum' added?
A) All five daily prayers.
B) Only the fajr adhan.
C) Only the maghrib adhan.
D) Only the jumu'ah adhan.

Key Takeaway
The tathwib and iqamah phrase are confirmed sunnahs based on prophetic and angelic practice, specific to fajr and iqamah respectively.

Pace in Adhan and Iqamah: Tarsil and Hadr
Explains recommended pace for adhan and iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended pace for adhan and iqamah in the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Adhan is recited slowly (tarsil), iqamah quickly (hadr) — reversing the pace is makruh.

In this lesson, we examine the specific Sunnah practices regarding the pace of adhan and iqamah. The Hanafi school holds that the adhan should be delivered with deliberate slowness, pausing between phrases, while the iqamah should be recited quickly. This distinction is based on prophetic practice and commands in the Sunnah. We will explore the textual evidence and the implications of reversing the pace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
What are the two acts being discussed? For adhan, what pace is recommended? For iqamah, what pace is recommended?
Note the terms tarsil (slow) and hadr (fast).
2
Locate the dalil
What is the proof cited for these recommendations? The passage says 'because both are commanded in the sunnah.' Identify the type of evidence.
This is a reference to the Prophet's practice and commands.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does the command in the sunnah indicate the specific pace? The passage mentions the pause between phrases for adhan and the quickness for iqamah.
The command indicates a recommended action, not an obligatory one.
4
Note the consequence of reversal
What happens if the mu'adhdhin does the opposite (fast adhan, slow iqamah)? The passage states it is disliked (makruh). Also note the discussion on repeating the call if the proper pace is missed.
This is a makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويتمهل) يترسل (في الآذان) بالفصل بسكتة بين كل كلمتين (ويسرع) أي يحدر في الإقامة) للأمر بهما في السنة. قوله : (بين) كل كلمتين أي جملتين إلا في التكبير الأول، فإن السكتة تكون بعد تكبيرتين قوله : (أي يحذر من باب نصر، ولو عكس بأن حدر بالأذان، وترسل بالإقامة كره قال في الفتح وهو الحق .اهـ. والسنة أن يعاد الأذان لفوات تمام المقصود منه كما في القهستاني، وكذا الإقامة كما في الخانية، وهذا على سبيل الأفضلية كما في النهر، وقيل : لا تعاد الإقامة لترك الحدر لعدم مشروعية تكرارها وصحح
And he takes his time (tarasul) in the adhan by pausing between every two phrases, and he hurries, i.e. speed (hadr) in the iqamah, because both are commanded in the sunnah. His saying: 'between' every two phrases, i.e. two sentences, except in the first takbir, for the pause is after two takbirs. His saying: 'i.e. yahdir' from the verb hadara (to be quick). And if he were to reverse by being quick in the adhan and slow in the iqamah, it is disliked. It is stated in al-Fath and it is the truth. And it is sunnah to repeat the adhan if the completion of its purpose is missed, as in al-Qahastani, and likewise the iqamah as in al-Khaniyyah, and this is on the basis of preference as in al-Nahr. And it is said: the iqamah is not repeated for omitting hadr due to the impermissibility of its repetition, and this is corrected.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended pace in adhan and iqamah. The adhan should be recited slowly (tarsil) with distinct pauses between phrases, except that the first takbir is paused after two takbirs. The iqamah should be recited quickly (hadr). If the mu'adhdhin does the opposite (hasty adhan, slow iqamah), it is disliked (makruh). The commentary also mentions that if the slowness or quickness is not achieved properly, it is recommended to repeat the adhan or iqamah to fulfill the sunnah, though some scholars argue against repeating the iqamah.

Key Terms
ترسل (tarsil): Reciting the adhan slowly with pauses between phrases.
حدر (hadr): Reciting the iqamah quickly without prolongation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended pace for reciting the iqamah in the Hanafi school?
A) Slowly with pauses between phrases.
B) Quickly without prolongation.
C) The same as the adhan.
D) In a melodious tone.

Key Takeaway
The adhan must be recited slowly (tarsil) and the iqamah quickly (hadr); reversal is disliked, and ikhtilaf exists on repetition if the pace is missed.

Validity of Adhan in Non-Arabic Languages
States that adhan is not valid if recited in a language other than Arabic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that adhan in a non-Arabic language is invalid and identify the condition that Arabic is required for validity.

Core Idea
Adhan is only valid in Arabic — any other language invalidates the call.

The adhan is a sacred call to prayer transmitted from the Prophet ﷺ in Arabic. This lesson focuses on the explicit ruling from Maraqi al-Falah that adhan recited in any language other than Arabic is not valid, even if the reciter knows it is an adhan. The commentary extends this rule to the iqamah by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage speaks about the adhan. The ruling is that it is not satisfactory (la yujzi) if recited in Persian (or any non-Arabic language). That means the adhan is invalid and must be repeated.
The ruling applies whether the reciter knows the meaning or not.
2
Identify the condition
The implicit condition is that the adhan must be in Arabic. Non-Arabic recitation violates this condition, rendering the adhan void.
3
Identify the reason (dalil)
The text gives the reason: 'because it has come in the sunnah.' The adhan is a worship act defined by the Sunnah, which is in Arabic.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Extend to iqamah
The commentator states that the same ruling applies to iqamah by analogy (qiyas) because the same cause ('illah) applies: both are calls to prayer transmitted in Arabic.
This extension is based on the shared 'illah of being a worship act defined by Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا يجزي الأذان (بالفارسية) المراد غير العربي وإن علم أنه أذان في الأظهر) لو روده السنة. قوله : (ولا يجزي الأذان بالفارسية) الظاهر ان الإقامة مثله للعلة المذكورة.
And the adhan is not acceptable in Persian (meaning non-Arabic), even if one knows that it is an adhan, in the most apparent view, because it has come in the sunnah. His saying: 'And the adhan is not acceptable in Persian' — apparently the iqamah is like it for the mentioned reason.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: the adhan is not valid if recited in any language other than Arabic, even if the reciter knows it is an adhan. The reason is that the adhan is a form of worship that must be performed as transmitted in the sunnah, which is in Arabic. The commentary extends this ruling to the iqamah by analogy, as the same cause applies.

Key Terms
يجزي (yujzi): To be sufficient or valid; here it means the adhan is not legally valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is an adhan recited in Persian (non-Arabic) valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, as long as the reciter knows it is an adhan.
B) No, it is not valid and must be repeated in Arabic.
C) Yes, if all listeners understand Persian.
D) It is valid but disliked.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is invalid if recited in any language other than Arabic, because it is a fixed Sunnah act transmitted in Arabic.

Recommended Qualities of the Mu'adhdhin
Lists the recommended qualities for a mu'adhdhin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended qualities of a mu'adhdhin and determine the legal ruling when some are omitted.

Core Idea
A mu'adhdhin should be pious, knowledgeable, in wudu, and face qibla, but omissions do not invalidate the adhan.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the recommended (mustahabb) conditions for the mu'adhdhin. While not obligatory, these practices enhance the adhan's spiritual merit. The text also addresses special cases like riding during travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm level
The text uses 'yustahab' (it is recommended). Determine that these qualities are mustahabb, not fard or wajib.
Mustahabb acts bring reward but no sin for leaving.
2
List the recommended qualities
State each quality: righteousness (taqwa), knowledge of sunnah in adhan, knowledge of prayer times, being in wudu, and facing the qibla.
All are recommended, not required for validity.
3
Note the exception for riding
In travel (safar linguistic), it is permissible to give adhan while riding if necessary. In settled areas, it is disliked (makruh tanzih).
The term 'safar' here is linguistic, not the legal travel.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
If a recommended quality is omitted, the adhan remains valid but is considered makruh tanzih (slightly disliked).
The purpose of the adhan is still achieved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويستحب أن يكون المؤذن صالحاً) أي متقياً لأنه أمين في الدين (عالماً بالسنة) في الأذان (و) عالماً بدخول (أوقات الصلاة) لتصحيح العبادة (و) أن يكون على وضوء) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء مستقبل القبلة) كما فعله الملك النازل (إلا) أن يكون راكباً) لضرورة سفر ووحل ويكره في الحضر راكباً في ظاهر الرواية. قوله : (بالسنة في (الأذان كتربيع التكبير والترسل قوله : (مستقبل القبلة) والإقامة مثله، ولو تركه جاز لحصول المقصود وكره تنزيهاً قوله : (الضرورة سفر الظاهر أن المراد به اللغوي دون الشرعي لمقابلته بالحضر ويدل له أنهم أباحوا التنفل راكباً خارج المصر مطلقاً فالأذان أولى أفاده بعض الأفاضل
And it is recommended that the mu'adhdhin be righteous, i.e. pious, because he is a trustee of the religion; knowledgeable of the sunnah regarding the adhan; knowledgeable of the entering of the prayer times to correct the worship; and that he be in a state of wudu due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Let none call the adhan except one in wudu, facing the qibla' as the descending angel did, except if he is riding due to necessity of travel and mud, and it is disliked in a settled area to be riding in the apparent narration. His saying: 'knowledgeable of the sunnah regarding the adhan like the fourfold repetition of takbir and slowness.' His saying: 'facing the qibla' and the iqamah is like it. And if he leaves it, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked tanzihan. His saying: 'necessity of travel' — apparently what is meant is the linguistic meaning, not the legal one, because it is contrasted with settled area. This indicates that they allowed voluntary prayer while riding outside the city absolutely, so adhan is more worthy. Some virtuous ones conveyed this.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended (mustahabb) conditions for the mu'adhdhin. He should be righteous (pious) because he is a trustee of the religion, knowledgeable of the sunnah practices of adhan (like the four takbirs and slowness), and aware of prayer times to ensure correctness. He should perform wudu and face the qibla, as based on a hadith. However, if he is traveling and riding due to necessity (like mud), it is permissible to perform adhan while riding, though it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to do so in a settled area. The commentary clarifies that the term 'safar' here is linguistic, not the legal travel, and that voluntary prayer while riding is allowed outside the city, so adhan is even more permissible.

Key Terms
متقياً (muttaqiyan): A person who is pious and fearful of Allah, fulfilling His rights.
مستقبل القبلة (mustaqbil al-qiblah): Facing the qibla during adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a mu'adhdhin giving adhan while riding in a city without necessity?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzih).
C) It is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
The recommended qualities for a mu'adhdhin enhance the adhan but are not required for validity; omitting them is permissible but makruh tanzih.

Recommended Actions in Adhan: Fingers in Ears and Turning
Explains two recommended actions in adhan and their evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions for the mu'adhdhin during adhan and identify the evidence and scholarly difference on turning.

Core Idea
Placing fingers in ears and turning right for 'as-salah' and left for 'al-falah' are recommended sunnah actions, not obligations.

The adhan is a call to prayer accompanied by certain recommended practices. This lesson examines two such actions: placing the fingers in the ears and turning the face right and left. While some might assume these are obligatory, the Hanafi school teaches they are sunnah mu'akkadah based on specific hadith and scholarly reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actions and Their Ruling
The passage identifies two recommended actions: placing the tips of the index fingers in the ears and turning the face to the right when saying 'hayya ala as-salah' and to the left for 'hayya ala al-falah'. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
The text explicitly says 'yustahabb' (it is recommended).
2
Locate the Dalil
The first action is based on the Prophet's instruction to Bilal: 'Place your two fingers in your ears, for it raises your voice.' The second action is based on the practice (sunnah) of the adhan, as authenticated by al-Zayla'i.
Note that the text also mentions a virtue narration about the reward of the mu'adhdhin, but the main dalil is the direct instruction to Bilal.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's command to Bilal is a dalil for recommendation (istihbab) because it is an instruction for a specific action to improve the adhan, but it was not part of the original adhan from the angel (as the commentary notes). Thus it falls under sunnah, not fard.
The commentary clarifies: 'This is not an original sunnah, since it was not in the adhan of the descending angel.' Hence it is a secondary sunnah for emphasis.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Turning
There is a difference among Hanafi scholars: the accepted view (authenticated by al-Zayla'i) is to turn right for 'as-salah' and left for 'al-falah', while another opinion says to turn with both phrases in both directions. Al-Kamal and al-Nahr argue that specifying right and left is arbitrary, but the mufta bihi follows al-Zayla'i's authentication.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, the mu'adhdhin turns right for the first phrase and left for the second.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is to turn right for 'as-salah' and left for 'al-falah'. This is based on al-Zayla'i's authentication (sahhahahu) as cited in the text. Also, when alone, the correct view is that he still turns, contrary to al-Halwani's opinion that no turning is needed for oneself.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يستحب أن يجعل إصبعيه في أذنيه لقوله ل لبلال رضي الله عنه : اجعل إصبعيك في أذنيك فإنه أرفع الصوتك وقال : لا . يسمع مدى صوت المؤذن جن ولا إنس ولا شيء إلا شهد له يوم القيامة ويستغفر له كل رطب ويابس سمعه (و) يستحب أن يحول وجهه يميناً بالصلاة ويساراً بالفلاح) ولو كان وحده في الصحيح لأنه سنة الأذان (ويستدير في صومعته) بأن يخرج رأسه من الكوة اليمني، ويقول ما يقول، ثم يذهب إلى الكوة اليسرى، ويفعل كذلك كما في الدرر من غير استدبار للقبلة، لأنه مكروه كما في الفتح، والصومعة المنارة، وهي في الأصل متعبد الراهب ذكره العيني، ويحوّل في الإقامة إذا كان المكان متسعاً، الأقوال كما في النهر واختلف في أذان المغرب، والظاهر أنه يؤذن في مكان عال أيضاً كما في السراج، ويكره أن يؤذن في المسجد كما في القهستاني عن النظم، فإن لم يكن ثمة مكان. قوله : (ويستحب أن يجعل أصبعيه) أي السبابتين والمراد أنملتهما، وهو ليس بسنة أصلية، إذ لم يكن في أذان الملك النازل من السماء ولم يشرع لأصل الإعلام، بل للمبالغة فيه وان جعل يديه على أذنيه فحسن قوله : (لا يسمع مدى صوت المؤذن المدى كالفتى الغاية، وهذا شروع في بيان فضل فاعله وهو علة لقول المصنف، وأن يجعل الخ المفيد رفع الصوت بالأذان في النسائي له مثل أجر من صلى معه اهـ ويخرج من قبره يؤذن والمؤذنون أطول الناس أعناقاً يوم القيامة أي أكثر الناس رجاء ، وقيل : أكثر الناس اتباعاً لأنه يتبعهم كل من يصلي بأذانهم يقال : جاءني عنق من الناس، أي جماعة، وقيل: تطول أعناقهم فلا يلحقهم العرق يوم القيامة، وضبط بكسر الهمزة والمعنى أنهم أشد الناس إسراعاً في السير، أن المؤذن يجلس يوم القيامة على كثيب من المسك وأنه لا يهوله الفزع الأكبر، وفي أنه أذن في سفر بنفسه، وأقام وصلى الظهر قوله : (يمينا بالصلاة الخ) صححه الزيلعي ، وقيل : يحوّل بهما جميعاً في الجهتين. قال الكمال: وهو الأوجه. قال في النهر : لأنه خطاب للقوم فيواجههم به واختصاص اليمين بالصلاة واليسار بالفلاح تحكم، بلا دليل قوله : ولو كان وحده في الصحيح وقال الحلواني : إن أذن لنفسه لا يحوّل لأنه لا حاجة إليه. قوله : (لأنه سنة (الأذان ولو لمولود أو لخوف قوله : (ويستدير في صومعته) بأن يخرج رأسه من الكوة اليمني، ويقول ما يقول، ثم يذهب إلى الكوة اليسرى، ويفعل كذلك كما في الدرر من غير استدبار للقبلة، لأنه مكروه كما في الفتح، والصومعة المنارة، وهي في الأصل متعبد الراهب ذكره العيني، ويحوّل في الإقامة إذا كان المكان متسعاً، الأقوال كما في النهر واختلف في أذان المغرب، والظاهر أنه يؤذن في مكان عال أيضاً كما في السراج، ويكره أن يؤذن في المسجد كما في القهستاني عن النظم، فإن لم يكن ثمة مكان
And it is recommended that he place his two fingers in his ears due to his saying to Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Place your two fingers in your ears, for it raises your voice.' And he said: 'No jinn or human or anything hears the extent of the mu'adhdhin's voice except that it will testify for him on the Day of Judgment and every wet and dry thing that hears him will seek forgiveness for him.' And it is recommended that he turn his face to the right for 'as-salah' and to the left for 'al-falah', even if he is alone, according to the correct view, because it is a sunnah of the adhan. And he turns around in his minaret by bringing his head out of the right window and saying what he says, then going to the left window and doing likewise, as in al-Durar, without turning his back to the qibla because it is disliked as in al-Fath. And the minaret is called 'saum'ah', which originally means a monk's cell, as mentioned by al-Ayni. And he turns in the iqamah if the place is spacious, according to various opinions as in al-Nahr. And there is a difference of opinion regarding the maghrib adhan; the apparent view is that he calls it from a high place as well, as in al-Siraj. And it is disliked to call the adhan inside the mosque, as in al-Qahastani from al-Nuzum, if there is no other place. His saying: 'And it is recommended that he place his two fingers' i.e. the index fingers, meaning the tips of them. And this is not an original sunnah, since it was not in the adhan of the descending angel from the heaven, and it was not legislated for the original purpose of announcement, but rather for emphasis. And if he places his hands over his ears, it is good. His saying: 'No one hears the extent...' The extent (mada) is like 'al-ghayah' (the limit). And this begins explaining the virtue of the doer, and it is the reason for the author's statement: 'And that he place...' which leads to raising the voice in adhan. In al-Nasa'i, he has the like of the reward of those who prayed with him. And he will come out of his grave calling the adhan. And the mu'adhdhins will have the longest necks on the Day of Judgment, i.e., the most hopeful people, or it is said: the most followed because everyone who prays with their adhan follows them. It is said: 'came to me a neck of people' i.e., a group. And it is said: their necks will be elongated so that sweat will not reach them on the Day of Judgment. And it is pronounced with a kasrah on the hamza, meaning they are the fastest people in walking. And that the mu'adhdhin will sit on a musk hill on the Day of Judgment and that he will not be frightened by the greatest terror. And that he called the adhan himself on a journey, established the iqamah, and prayed zuhr. His saying: 'to the right for 'as-salah' etc.' was authenticated by al-Zayla'i. And it is said: he turns with both phrases in both directions. Al-Kamal said: that is more appropriate. Al-Nahr stated: because it is an address to the people, so he faces them with it, and specifying the right for 'as-salah' and the left for 'al-falah' is arbitrary, without evidence. His saying: 'even if he is alone' according to the correct view. Al-Halwani said: if he calls for himself, he does not turn because there is no need. His saying: 'because it is a sunnah of the adhan' even if for a newborn or for fear. His saying: 'and he turns around in his minaret' by bringing his head out of the right window and saying what he says, then going to the left window and doing likewise, as in al-Durar, without turning his back to the qibla because it is disliked as in al-Fath. And the minaret is 'saum'ah', originally a monk's cell, mentioned by al-Ayni. And he turns in the iqamah if the place is spacious, according to various opinions as in al-Nahr. And there is disagreement regarding the maghrib adhan; the apparent view is that he calls it from a high place also, as in al-Siraj. And it is disliked to call the adhan inside the mosque, as in al-Qahastani from al-Nuzum, if there is no other place.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage discusses three recommended actions for the mu'adhdhin: (1) placing the tips of his index fingers in his ears to raise his voice, based on the Prophet's instruction to Bilal and the reported virtues of the mu'adhdhin; (2) turning his face to the right when saying 'hayya ala as-salah' and to the left when saying 'hayya ala al-falah,' even if alone, because it is a sunnah of the adhan, though some scholars argue that if alone he need not turn; (3) turning around (from one window to another) in the minaret to face different directions, without turning his back to the qibla. The commentary discusses various opinions, including that the turning is done in the iqamah if the place is spacious, and whether the maghrib adhan should be from a high place. It also notes that calling the adhan inside the mosque is disliked. The commentary also delves into the virtues of the mu'adhdhin, including hadith about their reward on the Day of Judgment.

Key Terms
صومعة (saum'ah): A minaret, originally a monk's cell, used for calling adhan from a height.
كوة (kuwwah): A window or aperture in the minaret from which the mu'adhdhin calls out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended ruling for placing the index fingers in the ears during adhan?
A) Wajib, because the Prophet commanded it.
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah, based on the hadith of Bilal.
C) Mubah, no specific reward.
D) Makruh, as it distracts from the adhan.

Key Takeaway
Placing fingers in ears and turning during adhan are recommended sunnah actions, not obligations, and the relied-upon practice is to turn right for 'as-salah' and left for 'al-falah'.

Recommended Acts of the Mu'adhdhin (Sunan al-Adhan)
Hashiya commentary on the sunan of the mu'adhdhin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) of the mu'adhdhin and identify which conditions are recommended for a valid adhan according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The mu'adhdhin's sunan perfect the adhan but are not obligatory: righteousness, wudu, facing qibla, fingers in ears, turning face at key phrases.

This lesson examines the recommended practices (sunan) for the mu'adhdhin as detailed in al-Tahtawi's Hashiya. While these actions are not obligatory, they complete the adhan and bring great reward. Understanding the distinction between sunna and condition is key to correct fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin
List the attributes the text suggests for the caller: being righteous, knowledgeable of Sunnah and prayer times, and being in a state of wudu and facing qibla.
These are sunnan, not shurut of validity.
2
List the specific physical sunan during adhan
Note the actions: placing index fingers in ears, turning face to the right for 'Hayya ala as-salah' and left for 'Hayya ala al-falah', and turning in the minaret without back to qibla.
The hadith for placing fingers promises great reward.
3
Note the exceptions and disliked acts
Identify when the sunan can be omitted: riding due to necessity, and the disliked nature of adhan inside the mosque or riding in town.
Exceptions do not make adhan invalid.
4
Determine the authority and weight of these rulings
Recognize that the rulings come from zahir al-riwaya and authoritative texts like al-Durar, al-Fath, and al-Nahr.
The sound opinion (as-sahih) is that turning face is sunna even when alone.
5
Apply the distinction between sunna and condition
Understand that omitting a sunna does not invalidate the adhan, while missing a condition (if any) would. The text does not list shurut for validity.
All acts mentioned are sunna, not fard or wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة بلسان عربي في أذان الملك النازل (ويستحب أن يكون المؤذن صالحاً) أي متقياً لأنه أمين في الدين (عالماً بالسنة) في الأذان (و) عالماً بدخول (أوقات الصلاة) لتصحيح العبادة (و) أن يكون على وضوء) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء مستقبل القبلة) كما فعله الملك النازل (إلا) أن يكون راكباً) لضرورة سفر ووحل ويكره في الحضر راكباً في ظاهر الرواية (و) يستحب أن يجعل إصبعيه في أذنيه لقوله لبلال رضي الله عنه : اجعل إصبعيك في أذنيك فإنه أرفع الصوتك وقال : لا . يسمع مدى صوت المؤذن جن ولا إنس ولا شيء إلا شهد له يوم القيامة ويستغفر له كل رطب ويابس سمعه (و) يستحب أن يحول وجهه يميناً بالصلاة ويساراً بالفلاح) ولو كان وحده في الصحيح لأنه سنة الأذان (ويستدير في صومعته) بأن يخرج رأسه من الكوة اليمني، ويقول ما يقول، ثم يذهب إلى الكوة اليسرى، ويفعل كذلك كما في الدرر من غير استدبار للقبلة، لأنه مكروه كما في الفتح، والصومعة المنارة، وهي في الأصل متعبد الراهب ذكره العيني، ويحوّل في الإقامة إذا كان المكان متسعاً، الأقوال كما في النهر واختلف في أذان المغرب، والظاهر أنه يؤذن في مكان عال أيضاً كما في السراج، ويكره أن يؤذن في المسجد كما في القهستاني عن النظم، فإن لم يكن ثمة مكان مرتفع للأذان يؤذن في فناء المسجد كما في الفتح.
The Book of Prayer. In Arabic for the adhan of the descending angel. (And it is recommended that the mu'adhdhin be righteous) meaning pious, because he is a trustee in religion, (knowledgeable of the Sunnah) concerning the adhan, (and) knowledgeable of the entry of (prayer times) to correct the worship, (and that he be in ablution) because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'None should give the adhan except one in ablution, facing the qibla' as the descending angel did. (Except) if he is riding, due to necessity of travel and mud, and it is disliked in the town while riding according to the apparent transmission. (And) it is recommended that he put his two fingers in his ears because of his saying to Bilal, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Place your fingers in your ears, for it raises your voice.' And he said: 'No jinn or human or anything hears the voice of the mu'adhdhin except that it bears witness for him on the Day of Resurrection and seeks forgiveness for him, every moist and dry thing that hears it.' (And) it is recommended that he turns his face to the right for 'as-salah' and to the left for 'al-falah', even if he is alone according to the sound opinion, because it is a sunna of the adhan. (And he turns around in his minaret) by putting his head out of the right niche and saying what he says, then going to the left niche and doing likewise, as in al-Durar, without turning his back to the qibla, because it is disliked as in al-Fath. The minaret (sawma'a) is the light tower, originally a monk's cell, mentioned by al-Ayni. He turns in the iqama if the place is spacious; there are different sayings as in al-Nahr. And there is disagreement about the adhan for Maghrib; apparently he gives adhan from a high place as well, as in al-Siraj. And it is disliked to give adhan inside the mosque, as in al-Qahistani from al-Nuzam. If there is no high place for the adhan, he gives adhan in the courtyard of the mosque, as in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the recommended acts (sunan) related to the mu'adhdhin (the caller to prayer). The text begins by stating the recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin: he should be righteous and trustworthy, knowledgeable of the Sunnah regarding the adhan, and aware of the prayer times to ensure correct worship. It is also recommended that he be in a state of wudu (ablution) and face the qibla, as the angel did when giving the adhan descending from heaven. An exception is made for a rider in case of travel necessity or muddy conditions; in such cases, facing qibla is not required, but riding while in town is disliked according to the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya). The mu'adhdhin is recommended to place his index fingers in his ears to raise his voice, based on a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed Bilal to do so, with a promise of great reward: every hearer testifies for him and seeks forgiveness. The mu'adhdhin should also turn his face to the right when saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and to the left when saying 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', even if alone, as this is a sunna of the adhan. Regarding turning in the minaret (sawma'a), the mu'adhdhin should move his head from the right niche to the left without turning his back to the qibla. The commentary clarifies that some allow turning in iqama as well if space permits. It is disliked to give adhan inside the mosque; if no high place is available, he may do so in the courtyard. These rulings are derived from the Hanafi school's authoritative texts such as al-Durar, al-Fath, and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
مؤذن (mu'adhdhin): The person who calls the adhan, required to be trustworthy and knowledgeable.
إصبعين (isba'ayn): The two index fingers placed in the ears during adhan to amplify the voice.
تحويل الوجه (tahwil al-wajh): Turning the face to the right for 'as-salah' and left for 'al-falah'.
صومعة (sawma'a): Minaret or high place where adhan is given; originally a monk's cell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is sunna according to the sound opinion.
C) It is only recommended when there is a congregation.
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The sunan of the mu'adhdhin perfect the adhan but are not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the call to prayer.

Separation Between Adhan and Iqama, Tathwib, and Prohibition of Tatrib
Hashiya commentary on adhan practices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended separation between adhan and iqama, explain the Hanafi position on tathwib, and identify the prohibition of tatrib.

Core Idea
Separation is recommended; tathwib in all times is the soundest view; tatrib that changes words is haram.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies three interrelated aspects of the adhan: the recommended gap before iqama, the practice of tathwib (second call), and the prohibition of melodious chanting that distorts the text. These rulings ensure the adhan remains a clear summons to prayer, free from alteration and resembling sinful behavior.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on separation (fasl)
Find the statement about the gap between adhan and iqama. Note that connection is disliked and the separation is recommended. Observe the specific amount for Maghrib: a pause equivalent to three short verses or three steps.
The amount is a guideline, not a precise measure.
2
Understand the practice of tathwib
Locate the rule that tathwib is after the adhan in all times according to the soundest view. Note that local custom may dictate the exact wording, and flexibility is allowed as long as the purpose of notification is achieved.
This view is from the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin).
3
Recognize the prohibition of tatrib
Identify the explicit prohibition of melodiously chanting the adhan or Quran if it alters words or letters. Understand the rationale: it resembles the actions of transgressors.
Tatrib is defined as changing the words or pronunciation, not mere beautification.
4
Apply the rulings to real-life adhan
Envision a mu'adhdhin following the Hanafi school: he pauses briefly between adhan and iqama, says 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm' after the Fajr adhan, and avoids any melodic alteration.
The pause for Maghrib is particularly brief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويفصل بين الأذان والإقامة) لكراهة وصلهما (بقدر ما يحضر القوم الملازمون (للصلاة للأمر به (مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب و) يفصل بينهما (في المغرب بسكتة) هي (قدر قراءة ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة (أو) قدر (ثلاث خطوات) أو أربع (ويثوب) بعد الأذان في جميع الأوقات لظهور التواني في الأمور الدينية في الأصح وتثويب كل بلد بحسب ما تعارفه أهلها (كقوله) أي المؤذن (بعد الأذان الصلاة) قوله: (وهو التطريب) أي التغني به بحيث يؤدي إلى تغيير كلمات الأذان، وكيفياتها بالحركات والسكنات، ونقص بعض حروفها، أو زيادة فيها فلا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن، ولا يحل سماعه لأن فيه تشبهاً بفعل الفسقة في حال فسقهم فإنهم يترنمون اهـ
His statement: (And he separates between the adhan and iqama) because it is disliked to join them, (to the extent that the people who are regular for the prayer may attend) due to the command to do so, (while observing the recommended time). And he separates (in Maghrib with a pause) which is (the length of reciting three short verses or one long verse, or the length of three or four steps). (And he makes tathwib) after the adhan in all times, due to the appearance of laziness in religious matters, according to the soundest view. And tathwib of each locality is according to what its people are accustomed to, (like his saying) i.e., the mu'adhdhin (after the adhan: the prayer). His statement: (And it is tatrib) meaning melodiously singing it such that it leads to changing the words of the adhan, their qualities in movements and pauses, omission of some letters, or addition, so it is not permissible therein nor in the recitation of the Quran, nor is it permissible to listen to it, because it resembles the action of transgressors in their state of transgression, for they intone melodiously. End.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage continues the Hashiya commentary on the recommended practices related to the adhan. It addresses three main issues: 1) the separation (fasl) between adhan and iqama, 2) tathwib (the second call after adhan, especially for Fajr), and 3) the prohibition of tatrib (melodic chanting). The text states that it is recommended to have a gap between the adhan and the iqama to allow people to prepare for prayer. The gap should be sufficient for those regular in prayer to attend, while ensuring that the prayer is not delayed beyond the recommended time. For Maghrib, a brief pause is sufficient – the length of reciting three short verses or one long verse, or three to four steps. This is based on the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructing Bilal to leave a breath between adhan and iqama. Tathwib, which is the phrase 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep) or similar, is recommended after the adhan in all prayers according to the later scholars (mutakhkhirin), especially in times of religious laxity. The manner of tathwib follows local custom, even if by clearing the throat, as the goal is notification. Finally, tatrib – singing the adhan melodiously in a way that alters its words or letters – is strictly forbidden (haram), as it distorts the sacred text and resembles the behavior of sinners. This prohibition applies also to Quran recitation and listening.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): The recommended gap between adhan and iqama to allow people to prepare for prayer.
تثويب (tathwib): The second call after the adhan, usually 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm' for Fajr, but here applied in all times according to custom.
تطريب (tatrib): Singing the adhan melodiously in a way that alters its wording or pronunciation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible (jahiz) but disliked.
B) Forbidden (haram) in adhan and Quran recitation.
C) Recommended only for Fajr.
D) Permissible if done with good intention.

Key Takeaway
Separation is recommended, tathwib in all times is the soundest Hanafi view, and tatrib that alters the adhan is forbidden.

The Ruling on Separating Adhan and Iqama
Hashiya on the ruling and evidence for separating adhan and iqama

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating adhan and iqama, identify the primary evidence, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Separating adhan and iqama is sunnah, not wajib; joining them is makruh by consensus.

The adhan announces the prayer time, and the iqama signals the immediate start. The Hanafi school teaches that a short interval between them is recommended, not required. This lesson examines the proof, the wisdom behind the separation, and a subtle difference of opinion within the school regarding its exact manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the separation between adhan and iqama. The matn states 'he separates' which implies a recommendation.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet (ﷺ) commanded Bilal: 'Place between your adhan and your iqama a breath.' Analyze the hadith's transmission and meaning.
The hadith is ahad, giving zann, so the command is interpreted as recommendation.
3
Understand the purpose
The separation allows people to prepare for prayer – finishing wudu or food leisurely. The adhan's purpose is to inform, and connecting them negates that purpose.
This teleological reasoning supports the sunnah ruling.
4
Note the consensus on dislike of joining
The text states 'by consensus' that connecting the adhan and iqama is disliked (makruh) in every prayer.
This establishes a clear prohibition (not haram but makruh).
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on manner
Abu Hanifa allowed separation by three steps or reciting three short verses; the Sahibayn preferred a light sitting. Al-Halwani clarified the difference is about preference, not permissibility.
Both views are valid; the mufta bihi is to separate, with the manner being flexible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويفصل بين الأذان والإقامة) لقوله لبلال: اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك نفساً حتى يقضي المتوضيء حاجته في مهل، وحتى يفرغ الأكل من أكل طعامه في مهل اهـ والنفس بفتحتين واحد الأنفاس وهو ما يخرج من الحي حال التنفس، ولأن المقصود بالأذان إعلام الناس بدخول الوقت ليتهيؤا للصلاة بالطهارة، فيحضروا المسجد وبالوصل ينتفي هذا المقصود قوله: (لكراهة وصلهما) في كل صلاة إجماعاً. قوله: (بقدر ما يحضر الملازمون) إلا إذا علم بضعيف مستعجل فإنه ينتظره، ولا ينتظر رئيس المحلة كما في الفتح، وما في المبتغى أن تأخير الإقامة، وتطويل القراءة لإدراك بعض الناس حرام جداً معناه إذا كان لأجل الدنيا تأخيراً وتطويلاً يشق على الناس لأنه إهانة لأحكام الشرع، والحاصل أن التأخير اليسير للإعانة على الخير غير مكروه، ولا بأس أن ينتظر الإمام إنتظاراً وسطاً كما في المضمرات. قوله: (مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب) فلا يجوز التأخير عنه إلى المكروه مطلقاً. قوله: (أو) قدر ثلاث خطوات هذه رواية عن الإمام وهذه الأحوال متقاربة وعندهما يفصل بينهما بجلسة خفيفة بقدر ما تتمكن مقعدته، ويستقر كل عضو في مفصله كما في الفصل بين الخطبتين والخلاف كما قال الحلواني في الأفضلية لا في الجواز.
His statement: (And he separates between the adhan and the iqama) due to his statement to Bilal: 'Place between your adhan and your iqama a breath so that the one performing wudu may complete his need leisurely, and the one eating may finish his food leisurely.' An-nafas (breath) with two fatha's is the singular of anfas, and it is what comes out from a living being during breathing. And because the purpose of the adhan is to inform people of the entry of the time so that they may prepare for prayer with purification, and thus attend the mosque, and by connecting them this purpose is negated. His statement: (Because of the dislike of connecting them) in every prayer by consensus. His statement: (To the extent that the regular attenders may come) except if one knows of a weak person in a hurry, then he waits for him, but he does not wait for the chief of the quarter as in al-Fath. What is in al-Muntagha that delaying the iqama and prolonging the recitation to catch up some people is severely forbidden, its meaning is if it is for worldly reasons as a delay and prolongation that burdens people because it is a disrespect to the rulings of Shari'ah. The conclusion is that a slight delay to aid in good is not disliked, and there is no harm if the imam waits a moderate amount as in al-Mudmarat. His statement: (While observing the recommended time) so it is not permissible to delay from it to the disliked time absolutely. His statement: (Or) the amount of three steps – this is a narration from the Imam, and these conditions are close. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he separates between them with a light sitting to the extent that his buttocks are seated and every limb settles in its joint as in the separation between the two sermons. The difference, as al-Halwani said, is in preference, not permissibility.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from the hashya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the ruling of separating the adhan from the iqama. The passage type is a ruling with proof, where the commentator explains the matn's statement 'And he separates between the adhan and the iqama'. The primary proof is the Prophet's command to Bilal to place a 'nafas' (breath) between them, which is understood to be a sufficient interval for people to finish wudu or food leisurely. The commentator clarifies that 'nafas' means a breath, and the purpose of the separation is to allow people to prepare for prayer, as the adhan is meant to inform them of the time. He then states that connecting the adhan and iqama is disliked by consensus in every prayer. Regarding the amount of separation, the text says it should be enough for regular attenders to come, but exceptions exist for a weak person in a hurry. Delaying the iqama unnecessarily for worldly reasons is severely forbidden, but a slight delay to aid in good is not disliked. The imam may wait a moderate amount. The separation must not delay beyond the recommended time for prayer. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to a narration from Abu Hanifa, the separation can be three steps or reciting three short verses; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it should be a light sitting similar to the separation between the two sermons of Jumu'ah. Al-Halwani notes that this difference is about preference, not permissibility.

Key Terms
النفس (an-nafas): A breath; the time interval of one breath, as defined in the text: 'the singular of anfas, what comes out from a living being during breathing'.
الملازمون (al-mulāzimūn): Those who regularly attend the mosque for prayers; the regular congregants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the recommended way to separate between adhan and iqama?
A) Three steps
B) Reciting three short verses
C) A light sitting
D) Waiting for a breath

Key Takeaway
Separating adhan and iqama with a sufficient interval is sunnah; joining is makruh, and the manner of separation varies within the Hanafi school but all agree on the principle.

Ruling of Tathwib: Sunnah in All Times?
Hashiya explaining the ruling and dispute on tathwib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwib after the adhan and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Tathwib is sunnah in all prayers according to later Hanafis, based on communal approval.

This passage from the hashya addresses the second call after adhan (tathwib). The commentator clarifies its ruling, noting a difference between the early authorities and the later scholars who deemed it commendable in all times. Understanding this dispute helps you see how the school evolves through istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Define Tathwib
Start by understanding what tathwib means both linguistically and legally. The hashya gives both definitions.
Linguistically: return to notification. Legally: specific call after adhan.
2
Identify the Ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah
Note that the early texts restrict tathwib to Fajr; the Sahibayn consider it makruh in other prayers.
This is the opinion recorded in the six core books.
3
Examine the Later Scholars' Opinion
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) adopted the view that tathwib is commendable in all times, citing Ibn Mas'ud's statement as evidence.
This is an example of istihsan based on communal practice.
4
Understand the Tarjih
Which opinion is mufta bihi? The later scholars' view prevails because of the principle 'ma ra'ahu al-muslimoon hasanan'.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويثوب الخ) هو لغة مطلق العود إلى الإعلام بعد الإعلام وشرعاً هو العود إلى الإعلام المخصوص قوله: (بعد الأذان على الأصح لا بعد الإقامة كما هو اختيار علماء الكوفة. قوله: (في جميع الأوقات) استحسنه المتأخرون، وقد روى أحمد في السنن والبزار وغيرهما بإسناد حسن موقوفاً على ابن مسعود ما رآه المسلمون حسناً. فهو عند الله حسن، ولم يكن في زمنه، ولا في زمن أصحابه إلا ما أمر به بلال أن يجعله في أذان الفجر. قوله: (في الأصح) ويكره عندهما في غير الفجر لأنه وقت نوم وغفلة، بخلاف غيره. قوله: (بحسب ما تعارفه أهلها ولو بالتنحنح لأن المقصود الإعلام كما في النهر عن المجتبى. قوله: (كقوله) أي المؤذن قيد بكون المثوب، هو المؤذن لأنه لا ينبغي لأحد أن يقول لمن فوقه في العلم والجاه حان وقت الصلاة سوى المؤذن لأنه إستفضال لنفسه. قوله: (قوموا إلى الصلاة) أي أو قوموا قوله : (وهو التطريب) أي التغني به بحيث يؤدي إلى تغيير كلمات الأذان، وكيفياتها بالحركات والسكنات، ونقص بعض حروفها، أو زيادة فيها فلا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن، ولا يحل سماعه لأن فيه تشبهاً بفعل الفسقة في حال فسقهم فإنهم يترنمون اهـ من
فيه ۱۹۹ كتاب الصلاة
الصلاة يا (مصلين قوموا إلى الصلاة ويكره التلحين وهو التطريب والخطأ في الإعراب وأما تحسين الصوت بدونه فهو مطلوب
His statement: (And he makes tathwib, etc.) – linguistically it is absolute return to notification after notification, and legally it is the return to the specific notification. His statement: (After the adhan on the correct view, not after the iqama as is the choice of the scholars of Kufa. His statement: (In all times) – the later scholars considered it good, and Ahmad in al-Sunan, al-Bazzar and others narrated with a good chain as a mawquf from Ibn Mas'ud: 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' And it was not in his time nor in the time of his companions except what he commanded Bilal to place in the adhan of Fajr. His statement: (On the correct view) – and according to them (the Sahibayn) it is disliked in other than Fajr because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, unlike other times. His statement: (According to the customary practice of its people, even if by clearing the throat, because the purpose is notification as in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba. His statement: (Like his statement) – i.e., the mu'adhdhin is restricted by being the one making tathwib; it is not fitting for anyone to say to one superior in knowledge or status 'the time of prayer has come' except the mu'adhdhin, because it is self-promotion. His statement: (Rise for prayer) – i.e., or rise. His statement: (And it is talheen) – i.e., singing it in a way that leads to changing the words of the adhan, their forms in movements and pauses, omitting some of its letters or adding to them, so it is not permissible in it nor in the recitation of the Quran, nor is it permissible to listen to it because it resembles the action of transgressors in their state of transgression, for they sing. ... In it: 199 Kitab al-Salah  'Prayer, O worshippers, rise to prayer' and it is disliked to make talheen, which is talteen and grammatical mistakes. As for improving the voice without that, it is desirable.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from the hashya explains the ruling of tathwib (the second call after the adhan, usually saying 'as-salatu khairun min an-nawm' in Fajr or 'as-salatu as-salatu' or 'qad qamat as-salah' etc.). The commentator defines tathwib linguistically and legally, and states the correct position is that tathwib is after the adhan, not after the iqama. It is considered commendable in all times according to later scholars, based on the principle that whatever Muslims consider good is good with Allah. However, it was not practiced in the time of the Prophet or his companions except in the Fajr adhan. According to the Sahibayn, tathwib is disliked in other than Fajr. The method of tathwib should follow local custom, even if by clearing the throat. The person making tathwib should be the mu'adhdhin himself, as it is not appropriate for others to announce the time. The wording includes 'qad qamat as-salah' or 'qumuu ila as-salah'. The text then discusses talheen (melodic chanting) which is severely disliked; it involves changing the words of the adhan or Quran through singing, and listening to it is also unlawful because it resembles the actions of transgressors. However, simply beautifying the voice without such changes is recommended.

Key Terms
التثويب (at-tathwīb): The return to notification after the adhan, specifically the call of 'as-salatu khairun min an-nawm' or similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi scholars, in which prayers is tathwib (the second call) considered commendable?
A) Only Fajr
B) All prayers
C) Only Maghrib
D) Only Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
Tathwib in all prayers is a valid practice in the Hanafi school, supported by istihsan and the principle of communal good.

Talheen in Adhan: Prohibition and Distinction
Hashiya explaining the prohibition of melodic adhan and the recommendation of good voice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited talheen and recommended beautification of voice in adhan.

Core Idea
Melodic chanting that changes the words of adhan is prohibited; beautifying the voice without distortion is recommended.

This section of the hashya addresses the issue of singing the adhan. It draws a clear line between acceptable voice modulation and prohibited singing that alters the text. Understanding this distinction protects the sanctity of the adhan.

Guided Path
1
Define Talheen and Tatrib
Note that talheen and tatrib are used interchangeably in the text. They refer to melodic chanting that changes letters or adds sounds.
2
State the Ruling
The text says 'لا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن' - it is not permissible in adhan or Quran recitation.
The ruling is haram.
3
Identify the Reason
The prohibition is because it resembles the actions of sinners (tashabbuh bi af'al al-fasiqeen).
4
Distinguish from Recommended Voice Beautification
The text adds that improving the voice without talheen is desirable (mahlub).

Source Text

Rulings on Disliked and Invalid Adhan Callers
Hashiya on the dislike and invalidity of adhan from certain persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the adhan of a person with minor or major impurity, a child, a woman, a fasiq, and a sitting person, and identify the evidence and reasoning behind each ruling.

Core Idea
The adhan of an impure person is disliked; of a child without discernment is invalid; of a woman and fasiq is disliked.

The adhan is a sacred call to prayer, but its validity and desirability depend on the state of the caller. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies which callers are considered problematic, providing nuanced rulings based on hadith and rational considerations. Understanding these distinctions ensures that the adhan fulfills its purpose of clear notification and spiritual dignity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories
List all the types of callers mentioned: muhdith (minor impurity), junub (major impurity), child (without discernment), madman, idiot, drunkard, woman, fasiq, and sitting person.
Each category has a specific ruling and reasoning.
2
Determine the Ruling for Each
For each category, identify whether the adhan is makruh (disliked) or invalid (la adhan). Note that for some there is an internal ikhtilaf.
The child without discernment is explicitly 'no adhan' invalid; others are disliked.
3
Examine the Evidence for Muhdith
The text cites the hadith 'La yu'adhdhin illa mutawaddi'' and explains why the narration that considers it makruh is followed despite a contrary report.
This demonstrates the principle of preferring a narration that aligns with the hadith text.
4
Analyze the Reasoning for Woman and Fasiq
For the woman, the reasons are: raising voice impairs notification, lowering fails, and her voice is 'awrah. For the fasiq, his report is not accepted and he is not trustworthy.
These are rational (ma'qul) considerations supplementing textual evidence.
5
Understand the Implications for Fatwa
Recognize that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is that these adhans are disliked, but some may be invalid. Apply this in practice.
The ruling of dislike does not necessarily void the adhan, but it is preferred to repeat it in some cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (إقامة المحدث، وأذانه) لما روينا ولما من الدعاء لما لا يجيب بنفسه واتبعت هذه الرواية لموافقتها نص الحديث وإن صحح عدم كراهة أذان المحدث (و) يكره أذان الجنب رواية واحدة كإقامته (و) يكره، بل لا أذان (صبي لا يعقل) وقيل والذي يعقل أيضاً لما روينا ومجنون) ومعتوه (وسكران) لفسقه وعدم تمييزه بالحقيقة (و) أذان (امرأة) لأنها إن فخضت صوتها أخلت بالإعلام وإن أخفـته لم يحصل الإعلام ولأنه عورة (و) أذان (فاسق) لأن خبره لا يقبل ولا يؤمن التهمة (و) أذان (قاعد)
And it is disliked (the iqama of a person in minor ritual impurity, and his adhan) because of what we have narrated, and because it is a supplication from one who does not answer it himself. And this narration was followed because it agrees with the text of the hadith, although the correction that the adhan of a person in minor impurity is not disliked (is also reported). And it is disliked, rather no adhan (of a child without discernment) – and it is said even one with discernment – because of what we have narrated. And (a madman) and (an idiot) and (a drunkard) because of his transgression and his lack of true discernment. And (the adhan of a woman) because if she raises her voice she impairs notification, and if she lowers it notification is not achieved, and because it is 'awrah. And (the adhan of a transgressor) because his report is not accepted and one is not safe from suspicion. And (the adhan of a sitting person).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage lists persons whose adhan is disliked or invalid. The text states that the iqama and adhan of a person in minor impurity (muhdith) is disliked, based on a hadith that only a person in wudu should give adhan. However, there is a report that it is not disliked; the first opinion is followed because it agrees with the hadith text. Similarly, the adhan of a junub (major impurity) is disliked by unanimous narration, and even more so than a muhdith. The adhan of a child without discernment is invalid, and even a discerning child's adhan is said to be disliked by some. The adhan of a madman, idiot, and drunkard is disliked due to lack of discernment. A woman's adhan is disliked because she either raises her voice and impairs the notification, or lowers it so it is not heard; also her voice is considered 'awrah. The adhan of a fasiq (open sinner) is disliked because his report is not accepted and there is suspicion. Finally, the adhan of a sitting person is also mentioned. The hashya adds that the ruling of dislike may imply invalidity in some contexts, as with the child.

Key Terms
المحدث (al-muḥdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (without wudu).
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (requiring ghusl).
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): An open sinner who commits major sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because her voice is forbidden to be heard
B) Because she cannot raise her voice sufficiently
C) Because raising her voice impairs notification and lowering it fails to inform, and her voice is 'awrah
D) Because she is not allowed to enter the mosque

Key Takeaway
The adhan of an impure, fasiq, or female caller is disliked; the adhan of a child without discernment is invalid.

Speaking During Adhan and Iqamah: Ruling and Repetition
Ruling on speaking during adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speaking during adhan and iqamah, identify exceptions, and apply the preferred view on repetition.

Core Idea
Speaking during adhan reduces reward but does not invalidate; repetition required only for substantial speech.

The adhan is a sacred call to prayer, and maintaining its reverence is essential. Hanafi scholars have detailed what actions diminish its perfection. This lesson examines the rulings on speaking during adhan and iqamah, including the nuances of what requires repeating the call, based on the commentary from Hashiya al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The passage states that speaking during adhan is makruh (disliked) because it disrupts the sanctity of the dhikr. Note that it does not invalidate the adhan.
2
Recognize exceptions and conditions
Clearing the throat (tanahnuh) without excuse is also makruh, but if there is a valid reason like phlegm, it is permissible. The commentator clarifies that disliked actions are only problematic when not excused.
3
Distinguish between disliked and invalidating speech
Returning a greeting during adhan is prohibited (the adhan should not be interrupted even for that). However, speech does not break the adhan; it only reduces the reward. The adhan remains valid.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on repetition
There are three views: (1) never repeat, (2) repeat only with much speech (the preferred view), (3) repeat with any speech. The commentator favors the second view, citing al-Bahr and al-Khulasa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that if the speech is considerable (much speech), the adhan should be repeated; one or two words are considered little and do not require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويكره الكلام في خلال الأذان) لأنه ذكر معظم كالخطبة والكلام يخل بالتعظيم ويغير النظم المسنون. وفي المضمرات، ويكره التنحنح عند الإقامة، والأذان لأنه بدعة قال في : كذا البرهان الحلبي : أطلقوه، ولا يخفى أن المراد إذا لم يكن لعذر كبلغم يمنعه عن الكلام أو تحسين الصوت، ومن المكروهات الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في ابتداء الإقامة لأنه بدعة ولو وقف. في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال لا يعيد إلا إذا طالت الوقفة كما في القنية . قوله : ولو) برد السلام) ولا يرده في الحال، ولا بعد الفراغ، ولا في نفسه على المعتمد، وكذا القارىء والمصلي والخطيب وأجمعوا على عدم الوجوب على متغوط ومكشوف عورة مطلقاً لأن السلام عليهما حرام، وكذا يجب على قاض ومدرس ولا يجب رد سلام السائل كما في القرماني عن القنية، قوله: بالكلام فيه) أي مطلقاً وقيل لا يعاد مطلقاً ثالثها يعاد بالكلام الكثير دون اليسير، وهو الأشبه كما . في البحر عن الخلاصة، والكلمة والكلمتان كما يسير في القهستاني .
His saying: 'And speaking during the adhan is disliked' because it is a great dhikr like the sermon, and speech disrupts reverence and changes the prescribed order. And in al-Mudmarat: it is disliked to clear the throat during iqamah and adhan because it is an innovation. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: they said it unconditionally, but it is clear that it is meant when there is no excuse like phlegm preventing speech or beautifying the voice. Among disliked things is sending blessings on the Prophet at the beginning of the iqamah because it is an innovation, even if he stops during the adhan for clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat unless the pause is long, as in al-Qunyah. His saying: 'even if [speaking] is to return the greeting' and he does not return it immediately, nor after finishing, nor in himself according to the relied-upon view; likewise the reciter, the one in prayer, and the preacher; and they agreed on the non-obligation upon one who is defecating or has exposed 'awrah absolutely because greeting them is haram; and likewise it is obligatory upon a judge and teacher, and returning the greeting of a questioner is not obligatory, as in al-Qurmani from al-Qunyah. His saying: 'with speech in it' i.e. absolutely, and it is said it is not repeated absolutely; a third view: it is repeated with much speech, not little, which is more appropriate as in al-Bahr from al-Khulasa; and one or two words are considered little in al-Qahistani.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on speaking during the adhan and iqamah. It is disliked (makruh) because the adhan is a form of remembrance (dhikr) and speaking interrupts its sanctity. The commentator elaborates that even clearing the throat without excuse is disliked and considered an innovation. However, if there is a valid excuse such as phlegm, it is permissible. Also included is the rule of not returning a greeting during the adhan, neither immediately nor later, nor even in one's mind according to the relied-upon view. The same applies to a reciter, one in prayer, and a preacher. However, greeting one who is defecating or has exposed 'awrah is haram, so returning it is not obligatory. The passage also discusses whether the adhan should be repeated after speaking. There are three views: (1) not repeated at all, (2) repeated only with much speech (the preferred view), (3) repeated with any speech. The commentary leans towards repetition only when the speech is substantial, with one or two words considered insignificant.

Key Terms
التنحنح (al-tanahnuh): Clearing the throat intentionally without excuse.
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Continuity without pause; speaking breaks the continuity.
البدعة (al-bid'ah): An innovation in religion; clearing throat without excuse is considered a bid'ah in the context of adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the ruling on clearing the throat (tanahnuh) during adhan?
A) Permissible unconditionally
B) Disliked (makruh) unless there is an excuse
C) Invalidates the adhan
D) Recommended to clear throat

Key Takeaway
Speaking during adhan is makruh, not invalidating; the need to repeat depends on the quantity of speech—only considerable speech triggers repetition.

Dislike of Adhan for Zuhr on Friday in the City
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for zuhr on Friday for those who missed jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that adhan and iqamah for zuhr on Friday in a city are makruh tanzihi and identify the condition (city vs. village) that governs the ruling.

Core Idea
Adhan for zuhr on Friday in the city is makruh to avoid confusion with the jumu'ah adhan.

On Friday, the public adhan is for jumu'ah prayer. When someone misses jumu'ah and must pray zuhr instead, calling another adhan for zuhr can confuse others and imply that jumu'ah was not performed. This passage clarifies that in cities (misr), this practice is disliked (makruh tanzihi), while in villages where jumu'ah is not held, the normal zuhr adhan remains permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under consideration is performing adhan and iqamah for the zuhr prayer on Friday, specifically for those who missed the jumu'ah congregation.
The ruling applies to the adhan (call to prayer) and iqamah (commencement call) together.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi school holds that this act is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), meaning it is not sinful but contrary to the better practice.
The dislike arises because the adhan for jumu'ah has already served the purpose, and a second adhan may cause confusion.
3
Identify the condition
The dislikedness is specific to cities (misr) where jumu'ah is established. In villages without jumu'ah, the zuhr prayer is prayed normally with adhan and iqamah.
The term 'misr' refers to a major town or city where jumu'ah is valid.
4
Note the exception for missed prayers
This ruling does not apply to making up any missed prayer (faa'itah) on other days; for those, adhan and iqamah are sunnah, as will be covered later.
The passage makes a distinction to avoid conflating the Friday situation with general missed prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويكرهان) أي الأذان والإقامة الظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر) لمن فاتتهم الجمعة كجماعتهم مثل المسجونين (ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم لأن الأذان والإقامة من سنن الصلاة لا الوقت، والقضاء يحكي الأداء قال في الشرح والإطلاق يشمل القضاء في المسجد، والبيت ولكن في المجتبى معزياً إلى الحلواني، أن سنة القضاء في البيوت دون المساجد فإن فيه تشويشاً وتغليظاً اه قال صاحب البحر وإذا كانوا صرحوا بأن الفائتة لا تقضى في المسجد لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في إخراج الصلاة عن وقتها فالإخفاء بالأذان لها أولى
His saying: 'And both are disliked' i.e., the adhan and iqamah for zuhr on Friday in the city for those who missed jumu'ah, like their congregation such as prisoners. And [it is recommended] to call adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah because adhan and iqamah are sunnahs of the prayer, not of the time, and making up mimics performance. He said in the commentary: the absolute includes making up in the mosque and home, but in al-Mujtaba, ascribed to al-Halwani, that the sunnah of making up is in homes not mosques, for indeed it causes disturbance and severity. The author of al-Bahr said: when they explicitly stated that the missed prayer is not made up in the mosque because it shows laziness in taking the prayer out of its time, then hiding the adhan for it is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, for those who miss the Friday prayer (jumu'ah) in a city (misr), it is disliked to perform adhan and iqamah for the zuhr prayer they pray instead. This is because the public adhan on Friday is for jumu'ah, and doing another adhan for zuhr may cause confusion. However, this applies only inside the city; in villages, there is no jumu'ah so zuhr adhan is normal. Second, for missed prayers (fawa'it), it is sunnah to call adhan and iqamah when making them up, because these are sunnahs of the prayer itself. However, the commentator notes that it is better to make up prayers at home rather than in the mosque to avoid the appearance of laziness. Making up with adhan in the mosque might disturb others and suggest neglect, so one should preferably perform it quietly at home.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A major city where jumu'ah is held; the ruling applies to cities, not villages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because adhan is only for jumu'ah on Friday.
B) To avoid confusion and because the public adhan already served.
C) Because it is invalid to pray zuhr on Friday.
D) Because they should pray at home.

Key Takeaway
Adhan for zuhr on Friday in the city is makruh tanzihi due to possible confusion with the jumu'ah adhan.

Adhan for Missed Prayers: Sunnah but Recommended at Home
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers (fawa'it) and recommendation to do so at home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that adhan and iqamah are sunnah when making up missed prayers (fawa'it) and explain the preference for doing so at home rather than in the mosque.

Core Idea
Adhan for missed prayers is sunnah, but better done at home to avoid the appearance of laziness.

When a person has missed a prayer and must make it up (qada), the Hanafi school teaches that calling adhan and iqamah is a sunnah of the prayer itself, not of the time. However, the later scholars refine that it is more virtuous to perform this adhan at home rather than in the mosque, to avoid giving the impression that one is negligent about prayer times. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is performing adhan and iqamah when making up a missed prayer (faa'itah) – whether one missed prayer or many.
This applies to any obligatory prayer that was missed.
2
State the general ruling
It is sunnah (recommended) to call adhan and iqamah for missed prayers, because adhan is a sunnah of the prayer itself, not of the time (the prayer's prescribed window).
This is based on the principle that 'qada mimics ada' – the make-up imitates the original performance.
3
Identify the refinement
Although valid in the mosque, the preferred (afdal) practice is to make up missed prayers at home and to call adhan there. This avoids disturbance and the appearance of being lazy about praying on time.
The commentary cites al-Halwani and al-Bahr for this refinement.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason for the refinement is twofold: (a) praying missed prayers in the mosque may lead others to think one is careless about timeliness, and (b) calling adhan in the mosque for a make-up could cause confusion about the actual congregational prayer.
This is an example of Hanafi fiqh balancing the general sunnah with contextual considerations (talatuf).

Source Text

However, the commentator notes that it is better to make up prayers at home rather than in the mosque to avoid the appearance of laziness. Making up with adhan in the mosque might disturb others and suggest neglect, so one should preferably perform it quietly at home.
