Disliked Forms of Adhan and Ruling on Speech During It
Listing disliked adhans and ruling on speaking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the disliked forms of adhan and iqamah, and apply the Hanafi ruling on speaking during the adhan, including the recommendation to repeat for much speech.

Core Idea
Speech during adhan is makruh tanzih, but repetition is recommended for lengthy talk.

The adhan and iqamah are sacred calls that demand full reverence. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies which forms are disliked and how speech affects their validity, balancing sunnah practice with practical concessions. It also provides the relied-upon view on repeating the adhan after speech.

Guided Path
1
Classify the disliked adhans
Identify the three types of disliked adhan mentioned: from a sinner (fasiq), from a seated person (except when alone), and the iqamah without standing. Understand the reasons: the fasiq's testimony is unreliable, the seated posture contradicts the angel's example, and standing for iqamah is sunnah.
The dislike is tanzihi (close to permissible), not tahrimi.
2
Analyze the ruling on speech
The text states that speech during adhan is makruh, even replying to salam. The dalil is qiyas to the khutbah: both are great acts of dhikr, where speech undermines veneration and breaks the prescribed order.
Clearing the throat without excuse is also disliked as an innovation.
3
Evaluate the consequence of speech
There are three views: (1) repeat the adhan absolutely, (2) do not repeat, (3) repeat only if speech is much (more than two words). The relied view is the third, as it balances reverence and ease.
Much speech is defined as more than two words; one or two words are considered little.
4
Apply to iqamah
Speech during iqamah is also disliked because it breaks the sunnah of continuity (muwalah). However, unlike adhan, the iqamah is not repeated if speech occurs; repetition is only recommended for adhan.
Standing is required for iqamah absolutely.
5
Examine exceptions and details
Pausing due to cough or phlegm does not require repetition unless the pause is long. Sending salutations at the start of iqamah is disliked as an innovation. Replying to salam is not permitted immediately, even in the heart, for the mu'adhdhin, reciter, and khatib.
The relied view: the mu'adhdhin does not reply to salam during adhan, nor after finishing, nor in the heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رفعته إرتكبت معصية لأنه عورة (و) أذان (فاسق) لأنّ خبره لا يقبل في الديانات (و) أذان (قاعد) لمخالفة صفة الملك النازل إلا لنفسه (و) يكره الكلام في خلال الأذان ولو برد السلام (و) يكره الكلام في (الإقامة) لتفويت سنة الموالاة (ويستحب إعادته) أي الأذان بالكلام فيه لأنّ تكراره مشروع كما في الجمعة دون الإقامة. قوله: (إلا لنفسه لعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام وأما الإقامة فتكره بلا قيام مطلقاً. قوله: (ويكره الكلام في خلال الأذان) لأنه ذكر معظم كالخطبة والكلام يخل بالتعظيم ويغير النظم المسنون. وفي المضمرات، ويكره التنحنح عند الإقامة، والأذان لأنه بدعة قال في: كذا البرهان الحلبي: أطلقوه، ولا يخفى أن المراد إذا لم يكن لعذر كبلغم يمنعه عن الكلام أو تحسين الصوت، ومن المكروهات الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في ابتداء الإقامة لأنه بدعة ولو وقف. في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال لا يعيد إلا إذا طالت الوقفة كما في القنية. قوله: ولو) برد السلام) ولا يرده في الحال، ولا بعد الفراغ، ولا في نفسه على المعتمد، وكذا القارىء والمصلي والخطيب وأجمعوا على عدم الوجوب على متغوط ومكشوف عورة مطلقاً لأن السلام عليهما حرام، وكذا يجب على قاض ومدرس ولا يجب رد سلام السائل كما في القرماني عن القنية. قوله: بالكلام فيه) أي مطلقاً وقيل لا يعاد مطلقاً ثالثها يعاد بالكلام الكثير دون اليسير، وهو الأشبه كما. في البحر عن الخلاصة، والكلمة والكلمتان كما يسير في القهستاني.
He who raises it (garment) commits sin because it is 'awrah. (And) the adhan of a sinner, because his report is not accepted in religious matters. (And) the adhan of a seated person, contrary to the description of the descending angel, except for himself. (And) speech is disliked during the adhan, even replying to salām. (And) speech is disliked during the iqāmah because it loses the sunnah of continuity. (And) it is recommended to repeat the adhan due to speech therein, because its repetition is prescribed as on Friday, not the iqāmah. His statement: (except for himself) due to no need for notification; as for iqāmah, it is disliked without standing absolutely. His statement: (and speech is disliked during the adhan) because it is a great dhikr like the sermon, and speech detracts from veneration and changes the prescribed order. In al-Mudmarāt: clearing the throat is disliked during iqāmah and adhan because it is an innovation. Al-Burhān al-Halabi said: they stated it absolutely; it is understood that this is when there is no excuse like phlegm preventing speech or improving the voice. Among disliked acts is sending salutations upon the Prophet at the start of iqāmah, as it is an innovation. If he pauses in the adhan due to clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat unless the pause is long. His statement: (even) replying to salām. He does not reply immediately, nor after finishing, nor in his heart according to the relied view, likewise the reciter, the praying person, and the khatīb. They all agreed that it is not obligatory for one who is defecating or with exposed 'awrah absolutely, because greeting them is forbidden. It is obligatory for a judge and teacher; it is not obligatory to reply to a questioner. His statement: (due to speech therein) i.e., absolutely; some say it is not repeated absolutely; a third view: it is repeated for much speech, not little, which is most likely as in al-Bahr from al-Khulāṣah. One or two words are considered little.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiyah addresses several disliked aspects of the adhan and iqāmah. First, the adhan of a sinner (fāsiq) is disliked because his testimony is not accepted in religious matters, indicating a lack of reliability. Second, the adhan of a seated person is disliked because it contradicts the practice of the descending angel (the mu'adhdhin's ideal), except when the mu'adhdhin is alone, as there is no need for broad announcement. The iqāmah is disliked without standing in all cases. Third, speaking during the adhan is disliked, as it is a great remembrance comparable to the khutbah; speech disrupts veneration and the prescribed order. Even replying to salām is not allowed during the adhan. Similarly, speech during iqāmah is disliked because it breaks the sunnah of continuity (muwālāh). If one speaks during the adhan, it is recommended to repeat the adhan from the beginning, as repetition is prescribed in cases like Friday; the iqāmah is not repeated. Clearing the throat or sending salutations at the beginning of iqāmah are disliked innovations unless there is an excuse. A pause for coughing does not require repetition unless lengthy. Regarding replying to salām, the commentator notes the relied view: one does not reply immediately nor later, even in the heart, and this applies to the reciter, the praying person, and the khatīb. It is not obligatory for one defecating or with exposed 'awrah, but it is obligatory for a judge and teacher. The passage also discusses the extent of speech that necessitates repetition: three views exist—absolute repetition, none, and repetition only for much speech (more than two words) according to the strongest view.

Key Terms
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer, a sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and the Friday prayer.
إقامة (iqāmah): The second call immediately before the prayer, consisting of similar phrases with an added 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh'.
مكروه (makrūh): A disliked act; in Hanafi fiqh, it is tanzīhan (lesser dislike) unless specified as taḥrīman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The adhan is not repeated regardless of speech.
C) The adhan is repeated only for much speech (more than two words).
D) The adhan is repeated only if the speech is related to the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Speech during adhan is disliked but not invalidating; repetition is recommended only for lengthy speech (more than two words), balancing reverence with practicality.

Adhan and Iqamah for Missed Prayers: Rulings and Prophetic Evidence
Rulings on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers and identify the Prophetic evidence used to derive it.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah for every missed prayer, confirmed by the Prophet's practice on the Day of al-Aḥzāb.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on whether adhan and iqamah are required when making up missed prayers (fawā'it). The passage draws on two key events from the Prophet's life: the night of al-Ta'rīs and the Day of al-Aḥzāb. Understanding these rulings prevents common mistakes, such as assuming adhan is only for prayers performed in their proper time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (adhan and iqamah for missed prayers) and the hukm level (sunnah mu'akkadah).
The ruling applies to every missed prayer, not just the first.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Prophetic actions cited: the missed Fajr after al-Ta'rīs and the four missed prayers on the Day of al-Aḥzāb.
These are aḥādīth (mursal and mutawātir in meaning).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the Prophet's actions prove the sunnah: by performing adhan and iqamah for each missed prayer, he established it as part of the make-up.
The principle: 'al-qaḍā' yaḥkī al-adā' – the make-up imitates the performance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement: some narrations indicate only iqamah is needed for subsequent prayers, but the majority hold both adhan and iqamah for each.
Also note cross-madhhab: Shafi'is may not require adhan after the first.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is to perform adhan and iqamah for every missed prayer, based on the 'narration of increase' and the Day of al-Aḥzāb account.
This is the position of zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكرهان) أي الأذان والإقامة الظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر) لمن فاتتهم الجمعة كجماعتهم مثل المسجونين (ويؤذن للفائتة وراكب إلا المسافر لضرورة السير ويعلم حكم أذان المضطجع بالأولى نهر. تنبيه: إذا كان المقيم غير الإمام أتمها في موضع البداءة وإن كان إماماً فعن أبي يوسف يتمها في موضعه، وخيره الفقيه مطلقاً به في الخلاصة، وصحح ما روي عن أبي يوسف. قوله: (في المصر) قيد به لأن أهل السواد لا يكره لهم ذلك لأنه لا جمعة على أهله كما في البحر من باب الجمعة وقول السيد أن القرية كالمصر إذا كان لها مسجد فيه أذان، وإقامة وإن لم يكن لها مسجد فكالمسافر وعزاه إلى البحر ليس في محله لأن صاحب البحر ذكر ما نقله السيد في شرح قول الكنز وكره تركهما لمسافر لا لمصل في بيته في المصر. قوله: (لمن فاتتهم الجمعة سواء كان لعذر أم لا قبل صلاة الجمعة، أو بعدها بجماعة أم لا. قوله: (ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم لأن الأذان والإقامة من سنن الصلاة لا الوقت، والقضاء يحكي الأداء قال في الشرح والإطلاق يشمل القضاء في المسجد، والبيت ولكن في المجتبى معزياً إلى الحلواني، أن سنة القضاء في البيوت دون المساجد فإن فيه تشويشاً وتغليظاً اه قال صاحب البحر وإذا كانوا صرحوا بأن الفائتة لا تقضى في المسجد لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في إخراج الصلاة عن وقتها فالإخفاء بالأذان لها أولى. من سنن (ويقيم كما فعله النبي الله في الفجر الذي قضاه غداة ليلة التعريس (وكذا) يؤذن ويقيم لأولى الفوائت) والأكمل فعلهما في كل منها كما فعله النبي حين شغله الكفار يوم الأحزاب عن أربع صلوات الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء فقضاهن مرتباً على الولاء وأمر بلالاً أن يؤذن، ويقيم لكل واحدة منهن وكره) ترك الإقامة دون الأذان في البواقي) من الفوائت فلا يكره ترك الأذان في غير الأولى (إن) اتحد مجلس القضاء) لمخالفة فعل النبي لإتفاق الروايات على أنه أتى بالإقامة في جميع التي قضاها وفي بعض الروايات بالمنع اهـ إلا إذا كان التفويت لأمر عام فلا يكره في المسجد لانتفاء العلة. قوله: (في الفجر الذي قضاه الخ) عن زيد بن أسلم قال: عرس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة بطريق مكة ووكل بلالاً أن يوقظهم للصلاة فرقد بلال ورقدوا حتى استيقظوا، وقد طلعت عليهم الشمس، وقد فزعوا فأمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركبوا حتى يخرجوا من ذلك الوادي، وقال: إن هذا واد به شیطان فركبوا حتى خرجوا من ذلك الوادي، ثم أمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن ينزلوا وأن يتوضؤوا وأمر بلالاً أن ينادي للصلاة، ويقيم فصلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالناس، وقد رأى من فزعهم، فقال: أيها الناس إن الله قبض أرواحنا ولو شاء لردها علينا في حين غير هذا فإذا رقد أحدكم عن الصلاة أو نسيها ثم فزع إليها فليصلها كما كان يصليها في وقتها، ثم التفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي بكر الصديق، فقال: إن الشيطان أتى بلالاً وهو قائم يصلي فأضجعه، ثم لم يزل يهدئه كما يهدأ الصبي حتى نام، ثم دعا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بلالا فأخبر بلال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مثل الذي أخبر به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبا بكر، فقال أبو بكر رضي الله عنه: أشهد أنك رسول الله رواه مالك في موطئه مرسلاً، والتعريس النزول آخر الليل. قوله: والأكمل فعلهما لأن الأخذ برواية الزيادة أولى خصوصاً في باب العبادات كذا في البدائع. قوله: (يوم (الأحزاب) هو يوم الخندق وكان في السنة الرابعة من الهجرة قال في الشرح. قوله: (إن اتحد مجلس القضاء) أما إن اختلف فيؤذن للأولى في المجلس الثاني أيضاً. قوله: (المخالفة فعل النبي للهو و لعل له لقوله: وكره ترك الإقامة، قوله: (وفي بعض الروايات الخ) قد علمت أن الأخذ برواية الزيادة أولى.
Both (adhan and iqamah) are disliked for Zuhr on Friday in the metropolis for those who missed Jumu'ah, like their congregation such as prisoners. And he calls the adhan for a missed prayer, and is riding except the traveler due to necessity of travel, and the ruling of the adhan of one lying down is understood from the first. A note: if the one performing iqamah is not the imam, he completes it in the place of beginning; if he is the imam, according to Abu Yusuf he completes it in his place, and the faqih gives him choice absolutely according to al-Khulāṣah, and he authenticated what is narrated from Abu Yusuf. His statement: (in the metropolis) restricted because the people of the countryside are not disliked for them that because there is no Jumu'ah upon its people as in al-Bahr from the chapter of Jumu'ah, and the saying of al-Sayyid that the village is like the metropolis if it has a mosque with adhan and iqamah, and if it has no mosque then like the traveler, and he attributed it to al-Bahr, but it is not correct because the author of al-Bahr mentioned what al-Sayyid quoted in explaining the saying of al-Kanz: 'and their leaving is disliked for a traveler not for one praying in his house in the city.' His statement: (for those who missed Jumu'ah) whether due to excuse or not, before Jumu'ah prayer or after, in congregation or not. His statement: (and he calls the adhan for the missed prayer and performs iqamah because the adhan and iqamah are from the sunnah of the prayer, not the time, and the make-up imitates the performance. He said in al-Sharh: and the absolute includes the make-up in the mosque and the house, but in al-Mujtabā attributed to al-Halwānī, that the sunnah of make-up is in houses not mosques because therein is confusion and severity. The author of al-Bahr said: and since they stated that a missed prayer is not made up in the mosque because it shows laziness in taking the prayer out of its time, so hiding the adhan for it is more appropriate. From the sunan: (and he performs iqamah as the Prophet did in Fajr that he made up on the morning of the night of al-Ta'rīs. (And likewise) he calls adhan and iqamah for the first of the missed prayers) and the perfect is to do both in every one of them as the Prophet did when the disbelievers on the Day of al-Aḥzāb occupied him from four prayers: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha, so he made them up in order consecutively and ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqamah for each one of them. And it is disliked to omit the iqamah without the adhan in the remaining missed prayers) so it is not disliked to omit the adhan in other than the first (if) the place of make-up is the same) contrary to the action of the Prophet because the reports agree that he performed iqamah in all he made up, and in some reports prohibition. Except if the missing is due to a general matter, then it is not disliked in the mosque because the cause is absent. His statement: (in Fajr that he made up) from Zayd ibn Aslam: the Messenger of Allah camped one night on the way to Makkah and appointed Bilal to wake them for prayer. Bilal slept and they slept until they woke up, and the sun had risen upon them, and they were alarmed. So the Messenger of Allah ordered them to ride until they left that valley, saying: 'This is a valley inhabited by a devil.' They rode until they left that valley, then he ordered them to dismount, perform wudu, and ordered Bilal to call the adhan and iqamah. He led the people in prayer, and seeing their alarm, he said: 'O people, Allah took our souls, and if He willed He would have returned them at another time. So if any of you sleeps over a prayer or forgets it, then when he is alarmed to it, let him pray it as he used to pray it in its time.' Then he turned to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and said: 'The devil came to Bilal while he was standing in prayer and laid him down, then kept quieting him as a child is quieted until he slept.' Then the Messenger called Bilal, and Bilal informed him similar to what the Messenger had informed Abu Bakr. Abu Bakr said: 'I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah.' Mālik narrated it in his Muwaṭṭa' as mursal. Al-Ta'rīs is descent at the end of the night. His statement: (and the perfect is to do both) because taking the narration of increase is better, especially in matters of worship, so in al-Badā'i'. His statement: (Day of al-Aḥzāb) is the Day of the Trench in the fourth year of Hijra. His statement: (if the place of make-up is the same) but if different, he calls adhan for the first in the second session as well. His statement: (contrary to the action of the Prophet...) and you know that taking the narration of increase is better.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses two main issues: the dislike of performing the Zuhr adhan and iqamah on Friday in a city for those who missed Jumu'ah, and the rulings for performing adhan and iqamah for missed prayers (fawa'it). On Friday, those who miss the Jumu'ah prayer—whether due to excuse or not—must pray Zuhr. It is disliked for them to call the adhan and iqamah in the city (misr) because it may cause confusion; however, this dislike does not apply in villages where Jumu'ah is not obligatory. For missed prayers, the principle is that adhan and iqamah are sunnah of the prayer itself, not of its time, so they are required when making up missed prayers. The Prophet's actions support this: he performed adhan and iqamah for the missed Fajr prayer after the night of al-Ta'rīs, and for each of the four prayers he made up on the Day of al-Aḥzāb. The preferred view is to call adhan and iqamah for every missed prayer, though some narrations indicate only iqamah for subsequent prayers. The commentator notes that it is better to perform them in a house rather than a mosque to avoid showing negligence. The ruling also covers positioning of the muqim (person calling iqamah) and the dislike of omitting iqamah without adhan.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-fā'itah): A missed prayer that is made up after its time; plural fawā'it.
المصر (al-miṣr): A large town or city where Jumu'ah is established; rulings may differ for rural areas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many adhan and iqamah did the Prophet perform for the four missed prayers on the Day of al-Aḥzāb?
A) One adhan and one iqamah for all four.
B) One adhan and one iqamah for the first, then only iqamah for the rest.
C) One adhan and one iqamah for each of the four prayers.
D) Only adhan without iqamah for each.

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for every missed prayer, established by the Prophet's practice on the Day of al-Aḥzāb.

Conditions for Following the Adhan (Mutāba‘ah)
Ruling statement on following the adhan with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following the adhan and identify the conditions under which it is recommended.

Core Idea
Following the adhan is only recommended when hearing a proper sunnah adhan, free from melodic alteration.

This passage from Hāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī clarifies when the act of repeating after the mu'adhdhin (mutāba‘ah) is considered a recommended sunnah. Not every adhan triggers this practice—only those that are themselves in accordance with the Sunnah. We will dissect the conditions that must be met and note the subtle differences between madhāhib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mutāba‘ah (repeating after the adhan). The Hanafi ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. This is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Determine the primary condition: the adhan must be sunnah
The adhan must be performed according to the sunnah: no melodic alteration (lahn) and within the proper time. If the adhan deviates from this, following is not recommended.
The text uses 'al-masnūn' to mean the adhan conforms to the sunnah.
3
Examine the secondary condition: actual hearing
The listener must actually hear the adhan. If not heard due to distance or deafness, the recommendation does not apply, even if one knows it is being called. Hearing part of it may suffice.
Some scholars do not require hearing every word or understanding.
4
Consider subsidiary rulings: standing and making up missed responses
It is recommended to stand when hearing the adhan, though the duration (standing throughout or sitting) is not settled. If one delays responding, he should make up the missed phrases quickly if the interval is short.
These details are from al-Bazzāziyyah and al-Fatḥ.
5
Note cross-madhhab aspects
The text cites al-Nawawi (Shāfi‘ī) and states that Hanafi principles do not reject his view. Some schools consider following the adhan as wajib, but Hanafis maintain it as mustahabb.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا سمع المسنون منه) فلو لم يسمع لبعد أو لصمم لا تشرع له المتابعة، ولو علم أنه أذان كما ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب أي وقواعدنا لا تأباه، وفي شرح الشفاء للشهاب قيل: لا يشترط سماع الكل، ولا فهمه، ومفهوم التقييد بالمسنون أنه إذا كان على غير وجه السنة لا تندب متابعته، ومفاهيم الكتب حجة. قوله: (وهو ما لا لحن فيه وأن يقع في الوقت كما في مواهب الرحمن وفي: البزازية يندب القيام عند سماع الأذان اهـ وهل يستمر إلى فراغه أم يجلس. قال في لم أره، ثم إذا لم يجب حتى فرغ من تداركه إن قصر الفصل، وفي الفتح فإن سمعهم معاً
And if one hears the sunnah (adhan) from him. If he does not hear due to distance or deafness, following is not prescribed for him, even if he knows it is an adhan, as al-Nawawi mentioned in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, meaning our principles do not reject it. In Sharh al-Shifā' for al-Shihāb, it was said: hearing all of it nor understanding it is not a condition. And the concept of restriction to 'sunnah' is that if it is not in accordance with the sunnah, following it is not recommended; and concepts of the books are a proof. His statement: (it is what has no melody and occurs in time) as in Mawāhib al-Raḥmān. In al-Bazzāziyyah: it is recommended to stand upon hearing the adhan. Question: should one continue until completion or sit? He said: I have not seen it. Then if he did not respond until he finished, he makes up for it if the separation is short. In al-Fatḥ: if he hears them together...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the recommended following (mutāba'ah) of the adhan. The key condition is hearing a sunnah adhan—one that is performed correctly (no melody, in its proper time) by a mu'adhdhin who follows the sunnah. If one does not hear the adhan due to distance or deafness, the recommendation does not apply, even if he knows it is being called. Some scholars do not require hearing every word or understanding it, but the Hanafi principle is that the listener should hear the adhan. The adhan must be free from innovations (like singing) and performed within the time. It is recommended to stand when hearing the adhan, though whether to stand throughout or sit is not resolved. If one delays responding until after the adhan, he should make up the missed responses if the interval is short. The passage ends mid-sentence about hearing them together, likely referring to multiple adhans, but the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
متابعة (mutāba'ah): The act of repeating the phrases of the adhan after the mu'adhdhin as a response.
المسنون (al-masnūn): That which conforms to the sunnah; here referring to an adhan performed correctly in time and without melodic alteration.
لحن (lahn): Melodic singing or alteration of the adhan's natural recitation, which makes it non-sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the recommendation of following the adhan according to the Hanafi school?
A) The adhan must be called by a mu'adhdhin who is in a state of wudu.
B) The listener must be standing.
C) The adhan must be a sunnah adhan (no melody, in proper time).
D) The listener must respond aloud.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, following the adhan is a recommended sunnah conditioned on hearing a proper sunnah adhan; it is not obligatory.

Salah — Prayer

Adhan and Iqamah for Missed Prayers (Al-Fawa'it)
Explaining ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers and the preferred method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers and apply the distinction between the first and subsequent prayers.

Core Idea
For missed prayers, adhan and iqamah are given for the first; iqamah alone suffices for the rest, but doing both for each is more complete.

When making up multiple missed prayers, a key question arises: should each prayer be announced with adhan and iqamah, or is once sufficient? This lesson examines the Hanafi position, derived from the Prophet’s practice on the Day of al-Ahzab and the night of al-Ta'ris, clarifying the basic ruling and the more complete (akmal) practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The act is the giving of adhan (call to prayer) and iqamah (second call) when making up missed prayers (fawa'it).
Missed prayers must be made up in order, but the adhan/iqamah ruling differs.
2
Distinguish the first missed prayer from subsequent ones
The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between the first missed prayer and all later ones. For the first, both adhan and iqamah are sunnah muakkadah. For subsequent prayers in the same sitting, iqamah alone is sunnah, and adhan is not disliked but is optional.
The minimum sunnah is to give both for the first and iqamah for the rest.
3
Examine the evidence from the Prophet's practice
Two hadiths are cited: the night of al-Ta'ris (when the Prophet made up Fajr with adhan and iqamah) and the Day of al-Ahzab (when he made up four prayers, ordering Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each). These show the permissibility and completeness of doing both for each prayer.
The Prophet’s practice is taken as proof of the sunnah, not of obligation.
4
Understand the concept of 'akmal' (more complete)
The text states 'al-akmal fa'luhuma fi kull minha' – the more complete is to do both for each missed prayer. This is a recommended practice, not required. Taking the narration with extra details (ziyada) is preferred, especially in worship.
The akmal is based on the hadith of al-Ahzab where the Prophet did both for each prayer.
5
Apply the condition: same place of making up
The ruling that iqamah alone suffices for subsequent prayers applies only if the place of making up is the same (ittihad al-majlis). If the place changes, then adhan should be given again for the first prayer in the new place.
Changing location resets the sequence; the first prayer in the new session receives both adhan and iqamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقيم كما فعله النبي الله في الفجر الذي قضاه غداة ليلة التعريس (وكذا) يؤذن ويقيم لأولى الفوائت) والأكمل فعلهما في كل منها كما فعله النبي حين شغله الكفار يوم الأحزاب عن أربع صلوات الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء فقضاهن مرتباً على الولاء وأمر بلالاً أن يؤذن، ويقيم لكل واحدة منهن وكره) ترك الإقامة دون الأذان في البواقي) من الفوائت فلا يكره ترك الأذان في غير الأولى (إن) اتحد مجلس القضاء) لمخالفة فعل النبي لإتفاق الروايات على أنه أتى بالإقامة في جميع التي قضاها وفي بعض الروايات بالمنع اهـ إلا إذا كان التفويت لأمر عام فلا يكره في المسجد لانتفاء العلة. قوله: (في الفجر الذي قضاه الخ) عن زيد بن أسلم قال : عرس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة بطريق مكة ووكل بلالاً أن يوقظهم للصلاة فرقد بلال ورقدوا حتى استيقظوا، وقد طلعت عليهم الشمس، وقد فزعوا فأمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركبوا حتى يخرجوا من ذلك الوادي، وقال: إن هذا واد به شیطان فركبوا حتى خرجوا من ذلك الوادي، ثم أمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن ينزلوا وأن يتوضؤوا وأمر بلالاً أن ينادي للصلاة، ويقيم فصلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالناس، وقد رأى من فزعهم، فقال: أيها الناس إن الله قبض أرواحنا ولو شاء لردها علينا في حين غير هذا فإذا رقد أحدكم عن الصلاة أو نسيها ثم فزع إليها فليصلها كما كان يصليها في وقتها، ثم التفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي بكر الصديق، فقال: إن الشيطان أتى بلالاً وهو قائم يصلي فأضجعه، ثم لم يزل يهدئه كما يهدأ الصبي حتى نام، ثم دعا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بلالا فأخبر بلال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مثل الذي أخبر به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبا بكر ، فقال أبو بكر رضي الله عنه : أشهد أنك رسول الله رواه مالك في موطئه مرسلاً، والتعريس النزول آخر الليل. قوله: والأكمل فعلهما لأن الأخذ برواية الزيادة أولى خصوصاً في باب العبادات كذا في البدائع . قوله : (يوم (الأحزاب) هو يوم الخندق وكان في السنة الرابعة من الهجرة قال في الشرح. قوله : ( إن اتحد مجلس القضاء) أما إن اختلف فيؤذن للأولى في المجلس الثاني أيضاً. قوله : (المخالفة فعل النبي للهو و لعل له لقوله : وكره ترك الإقامة، قوله: (وفي بعض الروايات الخ) قد علمت أن الأخذ برواية الزيادة أولى
And he gives iqamah as the Prophet did in the Fajr that he made up on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris. Likewise, one gives adhan and iqamah for the first of missed prayers, and the more complete is to do both for each of them, as the Prophet did when the disbelievers on the Day of al-Ahzab occupied him from four prayers: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. He made them up in order consecutively and ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each one. And it is disliked to leave iqamah without adhan for the remaining missed prayers, so leaving adhan is not disliked for other than the first, if the place of making up is the same, contrary to the Prophet's action because the narrations agree that he gave iqamah for all that he made up, and in some narrations there is prohibition. Except if the missing was due to a general matter, then it is not disliked in the mosque because the reason is absent. His statement: 'In the Fajr that he made up...' from Zayd ibn Aslam who said: The Messenger of Allah camped one night on the road to Makkah and appointed Bilal to wake them for prayer. Bilal slept and they slept until they woke up when the sun had risen upon them, and they were alarmed. So the Messenger of Allah ordered them to ride until they left that valley, and said: 'This is a valley with a devil.' They rode until they left that valley, then the Messenger of Allah ordered them to dismount and perform ablution, and ordered Bilal to call the adhan and give iqamah. Then the Messenger of Allah led the people in prayer, and seeing their alarm, he said: 'O people, Allah took our souls, and if He willed He would have returned them to us at a time other than this. So if any of you sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, then becomes alarmed about it, let him pray it as he would pray it in its time.' Then the Messenger of Allah turned to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and said: 'Indeed, Satan came to Bilal while he was standing praying and made him lie down, then kept soothing him as one soothes a child until he slept.' Then the Messenger of Allah called Bilal and Bilal informed him similar to what he had informed Abu Bakr. Abu Bakr said: 'I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah.' Narrated by Malik in his Muwatta as mursal. Al-Ta'ris is descending at the end of the night. His statement: 'And the more complete is to do both' because taking the narration with increase is better, especially in matters of worship. So in al-Bada'i'. His statement: 'Day of al-Ahzab' is the Day of the Trench, in the fourth year of Hijra. He said in al-Sharh. His statement: 'If the place of making up is the same' otherwise if different, he gives adhan for the first in the second place as well. His statement: 'Contrary to the Prophet's action' etc. Perhaps because he said: 'And it is disliked to leave iqamah.' His statement: 'And in some narrations...' you know that taking the narration with increase is better.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the procedure for adhan (call to prayer) and iqamah (second call) when making up missed prayers (fawa'it). The author clarifies the Hanafi position: when a person has multiple missed prayers, the sunnah is to give both adhan and iqamah for the first missed prayer only. For the subsequent missed prayers, it is sufficient to give iqamah alone, and giving adhan for them is not disliked. The more complete (akmal) practice, however, is to give both adhan and iqamah for each missed prayer, based on the action of the Prophet on the Day of al-Ahzab when he made up four prayers in order and ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each. The text then recounts the hadith of the night of al-Ta'ris (when the Prophet overslept and missed Fajr) to show that the Prophet gave both adhan and iqamah when making up that prayer. The author notes that taking the narration with additional details (ziyada) is preferable, especially in worship. The ruling is qualified: if the place of making up is the same (majlis wahid), then iqamah suffices for subsequent prayers; if the place changes, then adhan should be given again for the first prayer in the new place. The dislike of leaving iqamah applies only when the missing was due to an individual reason; if the missing was due to a general cause (e.g., sleeping through the prayer), it is not disliked to leave iqamah in the mosque. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as the base ruling is from Maraqi al-Falah, a matn of Hanafi fiqh, and the hashiya expands upon it.

Key Terms
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed prayers that are made up after their prescribed time.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, given immediately before the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving adhan for the second and subsequent missed prayers when making them up in one sitting?
A) Adhan is required for each missed prayer.
B) Adhan is disliked for subsequent missed prayers.
C) It is sufficient to give only iqamah for subsequent prayers, and adhan is not disliked but the more complete is to give both.
D) Neither adhan nor iqamah is needed for missed prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits iqamah alone for subsequent missed prayers, but doing both adhan and iqamah for each is more complete and recommended.

Answering the Adhan: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Ruling on answering adhan and its dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on verbal response to the adhan, explain the evidence, and evaluate the practical consequences of the dispute.

Core Idea
Answering the adhan verbally is recommended, not obligatory in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the ruling on verbally responding to the adhan. There is a debate within and across schools; we will explore the Hanafi view, its evidence, and the practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act is being discussed: verbal response to the adhan. What is the hukm level according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
It is recommended (mandub/sunnah), not obligatory.
2
State the Dispute
Identify the opposing view: some early Hanafi texts and scholars held it is obligatory (wajib). Note that the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools also hold it recommended.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school as well as between schools.
3
Examine the Dalil
Analyze the hadith evidence: the Prophet responded to the adhan with phrases indicating a recommended act (e.g., 'Ala al-fitra'). Also, consider the consensus that there is no sin for leaving it.
The hadith does not take the form of an imperative; it describes the Prophet's action as a recommendation.
4
Distinguish Answering by Tongue vs. Foot
Understand that answering by foot (physically going to the mosque) is obligatory for Friday prayer by consensus, but verbal response is separate and mainly recommended.
This distinction resolves the apparent conflict of obligation.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
If one does not answer verbally, no sin; if he does, reward. He may continue other activities, though stopping is better.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that there is no sin for omitting it.

His statement: 'he continues his recitation if he is in the mosque' is based on the obligation of answering by the foot, and whoever says that does not negate the recommendation of answering by the tongue. His statement: 'When there are multiple adhans, he answers the first absolutely, whether it is the mu'adhdhin of his mosque or not, because wherever there is adhan, answering it is recommended. Then it is not repeated for him in the most correct view, as mentioned by al-Shihab in his commentary on al-Shifa. His statement: 'and he does not answer in...'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of verbally answering the adhan. The author of the hashiya explains that upon hearing a proper adhan (one free from melodic distortion or chanting), the listener should stop even from reciting the Quran to verbally respond. This is described as 'better' (afdal). However, there is a difference of opinion on whether this response is obligatory (wajib) or recommended (mandub). The Hanafi school has multiple positions: some texts like al-Khaniyya, al-Khulasa, and al-Tuhfa indicate obligation, while the majority of Hanafis (and the three other schools) hold it is recommended. The author cites evidence from a hadith where the Prophet responded to the adhan with specific phrases. The text then discusses nuances: if one is walking, he should still respond; if multiple adhans are heard, one answers the first heard; the obligation to physically attend the mosque (answering by the foot) is separate from verbal response. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that verbal response is recommended (mandub), not obligatory, except in specific contexts like the adhan before the Friday sermon where it is obliged by foot. The authority weight is from later fatawa works like al-Durr, al-Jawahir, etc., indicating it is from the mutakhkhirin (later scholars).

Key Terms
المسنون (al-masnun): That which is according to the Sunnah, here referring to the adhan that is free from melodic distortion and performed correctly.
الإجابة بالقدم (al-ijabah bi al-qadam): Answering the adhan by physically going to the mosque for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, how is answering the adhan by the tongue classified?
A) Obligatory (wajib)
B) Recommended (mandub)
C) Permissible (mubah)
D) Disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that verbal response to adhan is sunnah muakkadah (recommended), not wajib, and there is no sin for omitting it.

Responding to the Adhan: The Wording for Hay'alah
Ruling on responding to adhan and the specific wording for hay'alah phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on responding to the hay'alah phrases and explain the rationale for using 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' instead of repeating the mu'adhdhin's words.

Core Idea
When the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', the Hanafi school says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' to avoid mockery and acknowledge reliance on Allah.

Responding to the adhan is a stressed sunnah. However, the exact wording depends on the school. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the two hay'alah phrases, the evidence from istihsan, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school. Understanding why the Hanafi school departs from the apparent meaning of a hadith is key to appreciating the role of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is responding to the adhan. The Hanafi school considers it a sunnah mu'akkadah (stressed sunnah). What is the overall hukm level?
Some Hanafi scholars held it to be wajib, but the relied-upon position is sunnah.
2
State the Hanafi position on hay'alah
For the two hay'alah phrases ('hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'), the Hanafi school prescribes saying 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' instead of repeating the exact words.
This applies to both phrases.
3
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The Shafi'i school (and others) hold that one should repeat the exact words of the mu'adhdhin for all phrases. Their proof is a hadith from Musnad Abi Ya'la where the Prophet instructed a person in distress to repeat the mu'adhdhin's words, including 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
The hadith is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response (istihsan)
The Hanafi school argues that repeating the exact words would be a form of mockery because the caller is issuing a command, and repeating it as if commanding oneself is inappropriate. Instead, saying 'la hawla' acknowledges one's inability and reliance on Allah. This is a use of istihsan (juristic preference) to override the apparent meaning of the hadith.
The other words of the adhan (takbir, tashahhud) are praises and can be repeated.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Practically, Hanafis say 'la hawla' during hay'alah, while Shafi'is repeat the same words. Both positions are valid sunnah practices within their respective schools, but the Hanafi school considers its position mufta bihi.
Some later scholars like the author of al-Fath suggested combining both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(الحيعلتين) الصلاة) ولو أجاب فسدت قوله : (وخطبة) أي خطبة كانت قوله: (وتعلم العلم وتعليمه) ينافيه ما قدمه قريباً من قوله وإذا كان يتكلم في الفقه، أو الأصول تجب عليه الإجابة، والظاهر أن نفي الإجابة في اختصاصهما بذلك أنه لما طلب منهم بالجملة الأولى الإقبال على الصلاة والمجيء إليها وطلب منهم بقوله حي على الفلاح الإقبال إلى الفوز والنجاة وذلك لا يكون إلا بحركة والعبد لا قدرة له على شيء ناسب أن يقول لا حول أي لا حركة، ولا إستطاعة لي على شيء مما طلب مني إلا بقوة الله تعالى، وهذا أولى من قول المؤلف لأنه لو قال : مثلهما صار كالمستهزيء. قوله : (أي لا حول لنا هو من التحول، والمضي ومنه سمي العام حولاً لمضيه، وبعده أي لا تحول ولا بعد لي عن معصية الله إلا بعصمة الله ولا قوة لي على طاعته إلا بمعونته، فالعطف للمغايرة وهذا . هو ما فسر به هاتين الجملتين، وقيل: إن الحول بالواو، وبالياء في اللغة القدرة على التصرف فعطف القوة عليه عطف مرادف قوله (الحيعلتين) تثنية حيعلة مركبة على كذا قال المنلا علي في شرح الحصن الحصين والعرب إذا كثر استعمالهم في كلمتين ضموا بعض حروف إحداهما إلى بعض الأخرى مثل البسملة، والحمدلة والسبحلة، والحوقلة والهيللة والحيعلة والإجابة بالحوقلة للحيعلة قول الثوري وأصحابنا الثلاثة، وأحمد في الأصح . عنه، ومالك في رواية وقال النخعي، والشافعي، وأحمد في رواية ومالك في رواية: يقول كما يقول المؤذن حتى يفرغ من أذانه واختار المحقق في الفتح الجمع بين الحيعلة والحوقلة عملاً بالأحاديث الواردة، وجمعا بينها ففي مسند أبي يعلى عن أبي أمامة عنه : إذا نادى المنادي للصلاة فتحت أبواب السماء، واستجيب الدعاء فمن نزل به كرب أو شدة فليتحر المنادي إذا كبر كبر، وإذا تشهد تشهد، وإذا قال: على الصلاة قال : على الصلاة، وإذا قال: على الفلاح، قال: حي على الفلاح، ثم يقول يعني بعدما يتمه متابعاً: اللهم رب هذه الدعوة الحق المستجاب لها دعوة الحق، وكلمة التقوى أحينا عليها، وأمتنا عليها، وابعثنا عليها واجعلنا من خيار أهلها محيانا هما حي على الصلاة حي على الفلاح كما ورد لأنه لو قال مثلهما صار كالمستهزىء لأن من حكى لفظ الآمر بشيء كان مستهزئاً به بخلاف باقي الكلمات لأنه ثناء والدعاء مستجاب بعد إجابته بمثل ما قال
The preferable act is to stand and respond, and if there are multiple adhans, respond to the first. One does not respond during prayer, even funeral prayer, nor during the khutbah and listening to it, nor during learning knowledge and teaching it, nor while eating, having intercourse, or relieving oneself. A junub person responds, but not a menstruating woman or a woman with postpartum bleeding because they are incapable of responding by action. The description of the response is that one says as the respondent says, so his saying is like it, i.e., like the words of the mu'adhdhin, but one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power or strength except by Allah), meaning there is no turning from sin and no ability for obedience except by Allah's grace, upon hearing the two hay'alah phrases. If one responds during prayer, it invalidates it. His saying: 'and khutbah' means any khutbah. His saying: 'and learning knowledge and teaching it' contradicts what he previously said that if one is speaking about fiqh or usul, response becomes obligatory. The apparent view is that negating response in this case applies according to both opinions. His saying: 'their inability to respond by action' means it falls by speech following the action. His saying: 'as he responds to him' indicates that one does not fulfill the sunna unless one intends the response. His saying: 'but one says hawqala' - the secret of specifying these two phrases is that when the first phrase asks to turn to prayer and come to it, and the second phrase 'hayya alal-falah' asks to turn to success and deliverance, which cannot occur without movement, and the servant has no power over anything, it is appropriate to say 'la hawla' i.e., no movement and no ability for anything requested of me except by Allah's strength. This is better than the author's statement because if he said the same, he would be like a mocker. His saying: 'i.e., no turning for us' is from tahawwul (turning) and passing, hence the year is called hawlan for its passing, and after that i.e., no turning or going away from Allah's disobedience except by Allah's protection, and no strength for His obedience except by His help. The conjunction is for differentiation. And this is the interpretation of these two phrases. It is said that 'hawl' with waw and ya means ability to act, so the conjunction of 'quwwa' is synonymous. His saying: 'the two hay'alah' dual of hay'alah, a composition as said by Mulla Ali in Sharh al-Hisn al-Hasin. When the Arabs frequently use two words, they combine some letters of one with the other, like basmalah, hamdalah, sabhala, hawqala, haylala, and hay'alah. Responding with hawqala for hay'alah is the statement of al-Thawri, our three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), and Ahmad in the more correct narration, and Malik in one narration. Al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad in another narration, and Malik in another narration said: one says just as the mu'adhdhin says until he finishes his adhan. The muhaqqiq in al-Fath chose to combine between hay'alah and hawqala, acting upon the hadith that are reported, and combining between them. For in Musnad Abi Ya'la from Abu Umama from him (the Prophet): 'When the caller calls for prayer, the doors of heaven are opened and the supplication is answered. So whoever is afflicted with distress or hardship, let him follow the caller: when he says Allahu Akbar, he says Allahu Akbar; when he says the tashahhud, he says the tashahhud; when he says 'ala al-salah, he says 'ala al-salah; when he says 'ala al-falah, he says hayya 'ala al-falah; then he says, meaning after completing it, following: O Allah, Lord of this perfect call and the established prayer, grant Muhammad the wasilah...' Then he says: 'They are hayya 'ala al-salah and hayya 'ala al-falah as reported, because if he said the same, he would be like a mocker, because one who repeats the words of an issuer of a command is mocking. Unlike the other words because they are praise, and the supplication is answered after responding with similar words.'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses the rulings regarding responding to the adhan (call to prayer). It begins by stating the preferred act: to stand and respond, and if multiple adhans are heard (e.g., from different mosques), one responds only to the first. It then lists situations where responding is not performed: during prayer (even funeral prayer), during the khutbah (sermon) and listening to it, while studying or teaching religious knowledge, while eating, having intercourse, or during relieving oneself. A person in a state of janabah (post-sexual impurity) does respond, but a menstruating or postpartum woman does not, as they cannot perform the physical act of responding (i.e., they cannot go to the mosque). The text then defines the proper response: one should repeat the mu'adhdhin's words, except for the two 'hay'alah' phrases ('hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'), where one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power nor strength except with Allah). The commentator explains the wisdom behind this exception: the hay'alah phrases call to action (coming to prayer and success), which requires movement, but a person has no ability without Allah. Therefore, saying 'la hawla' acknowledges one's incapacity and reliance on Allah. Repeating the exact words could be seen as mocking the caller, as if one is commanding himself, since the caller's words are a command to others. This is different from the other parts of the adhan (like takbir and tashahhud), which are praises of Allah, so repeating them is appropriate. The passage then notes a disagreement among early scholars: al-Thawri, the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Imam Ahmad in one narration hold that one says 'la hawla' for the hay'alah. Al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad in another narration, and Malik in another hold that one repeats the exact words throughout the entire adhan. The Hanafi position is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid mockery and to reflect one's reliance on Allah. A hadith from Musnad Abi Ya'la is cited, where the Prophet teaches a person in distress to follow the mu'adhdhin by saying the same words, including 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The Hanafi response to this is that the hadith can be interpreted as encouraging the act of response, but the actual wording is subject to istihsan. The commentator notes that some later scholars, like the author of al-Fath, combined both by saying 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' first, and then adding 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' as a separate statement. The passage concludes by stating that the supplication after the adhan is answered when one responds with similar words, even during the hay'alah, but the Hanafi school prefers the specific wording for hay'alah.

Key Terms
الحيعلتين (al-hay'alatayn): The two phrases 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan.
الحوقلة (al-hawqalah): The phrase 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'; the act of saying this phrase.
الإجابة (al-ijabah): The response to the mu'adhdhin's call by repeating or saying specific phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should one say upon hearing 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan?
A) Repeat the exact same phrases.
B) Say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'.
C) Remain silent and listen.
D) Say 'sadaqta wa bararta'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' for the hay'alah phrases in the adhan response, based on istihsan to avoid mockery.

Salah — Prayer

Responding to the Fajr Adhan: Ruling and Phrases
Ruling on Fajr adhan response and general ijabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on responding to the adhan and identify the recommended phrases for the Fajr adhan.

Core Idea
Do not repeat 'prayer is better than sleep'—affirm it with 'sadaqta wa bararta' to avoid mockery.

When the mu'adhdhin proclaims 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific response to avoid the appearance of mockery. This lesson clarifies the ruling on responding to the adhan generally and the preferred wording for this unique phrase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Responding to the adhan (ijabah) is a sunnah act. Note that some Hanafi scholars considered it wajib, but the relied-upon view is mustahabb. The passage mentions this ikhtilaf.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi; the mufta bihi is mustahabb.
2
Distinguish the Fajr adhan response
For the Fajr adhan, when the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm', the listener should not repeat the same words. Instead, he says 'sadaqta wa bararta' or 'ma sha' Allahu kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' to affirm the truth of the statement.
This avoids resemblance to mockery (tashabbuh bil-istihza').
3
Examine alternative phrases
Other scholars recommend 'sadaqta wa bil-haqqi nataqta' or 'sadaqta wa bararta' with variations in vowelization. The passage notes that combining these is permissible.
The phrase 'bararta' is derived from birr (righteousness/truthfulness).
4
Consider the iqamah response (supplementary)
Upon hearing 'qad qamati al-salah', one may say 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha'. The addition 'wa ja'alani min salihi ahliha' is reported but depends on the madhhab difference regarding when to stand for prayer.
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one should stand at 'qad qamati al-salah'; the Sahibayn say after the iqamah completes.

Source Text

(و) في أذان الفجر (قال) المجيب (صدقت وبررت) بفتح الراء الأولى وكسرها (أو) يقول ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن عند قول المؤذن في أذان الفجر (الصلاة خير من النوم تحاشياً عما يشبه الإستهزاء، واختلف أئمتنا في حكم الإجابة بعضهم صرح بوجوبها وصرح بعضهم بإستحبابها ( ثم) دعا المجيب والمؤذن (بالوسيلة) بعد صلاته على النبي عقب الإجابة (فيقول) كما رواه جابر رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من هذه الدعوة التامة والصلاة القائمة آت محمداً الوسيلة

قال حين يسمع النداء (اللهم رب صحيح ومماتنا، ثم يسأل الله عز وجل حاجته رواه الطبراني في كتاب الدعاء، وقال الحاكم: الإسناد فهذا صريح في أنه يقول مثل ما يقول في جميع الكلمات، ولا يقال أن ذلك يشبه الإستهزاء لأنا نقول : لا مانع من صحة اعتبار المجيب بهما أمراً نفسه داعياً إياها محركاً منها السواكن مخاطباً لها حثاً وحضاً على الإجابة بالفعل، ثم يتبرأ من الحول والقوة وقد رأينا من مشايخ السلوك من يجمع بينهما قوله : (والدعاء مستجاب بعد إجابته بمثل ما قال) أي حتى في الحيعلتين ودليله ما في مسند أبي يعلى المتقدم. قوله: (وبررت) عطف تفسير على ما قبله من بر في كلامه إذا صدق وبرّ في يمينه إذا حفظها، وقيل: يقول : صدقت وبالحق نطقت كما في مجمع الأنهر، ولا خفاء في حسن الجمع. قال بعض الفضلاء : ويقول عند قد قامت الصلاة أقامها الله وأدامها هكذا روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ذكره الحلبي وغيره، ومعنى أقامها الله أثبتها وأبقاها قال في شرح المشكاة واشتهر بعد قوله وأدامها زيادة وجعلني من صالحي أهلها وهذا إنما يظهر على قول الصاحبين أن الشروع بعد الفراغ منها إما على قول الإمام أن الشروع الأفضل عند قد قامت الصلاة وأن الأفضل مقارنة المأموم للإمام في التحريمة لا يظهر قوله : (ما شاء الله كان) كان هنا ويكن فيما بعد تامة . قوله : (والمؤذن لتحصل له الفضيلة كذا في الشرح قوله : (بالوسيلة) أي بتحصيلها. قوله : (حين يسمع النداء هذا يقتضي أن الدعاء بها حين يسمع النداء وما سيأتي يقتضي يدعو بها بعد فراغه من الإجابة فإما أن يجمع بينهما، وإما أن يحمل الأول على الثاني، ويكون المراد بقوله حين يسمع الإسراع والمبادرة أو المراد كل الأذان. قوله : (الدعوة) بفتح الدال الدعاء والتامة الكاملة التي لا يدخلها نقص ولا عيب ولا تغيرها ملة، ولا تنسخها شريعة وفي هذه الدعوة أفضل الأقوال، وهو لا إله إلا الله قال العيني : هي إلى قول محمد رسول الله . قوله : (الصلاة) القائمة أي الدائمة الثابتة. قوله : (آت محمداً الوسيلة) هي فعيلة وتجمع على وسائل ووسل وهي كل أمر يكون موصلاً لأمر تبتغيه،
And in the Fajr adhan, the responder says: 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and are righteous) with the first ra' fatha or kasra, or he says: 'ma sha' Allahu kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' (what Allah wills happens, and what He does not will does not happen) when the mu'adhdhin says in the Fajr adhan 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep), avoiding what resembles mockery. And our imams differed regarding the ruling of the response: some clarified its obligation, and some clarified its recommendation. Then the responder and the mu'adhdhin supplicate for the wasilah after sending blessings upon the Prophet after the response. He says, as Jabir narrated from the Prophet: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imi, ati Muhammadan al-wasilah.' He said when he hears the call: 'Allahumma rabba...' and then asks Allah for his need. Reported by al-Tabarani in Kitab al-Du'a, and al-Hakim said the chain is authentic. So this is explicit that he says similar to what the mu'adhdhin says in all words, and it is not said that this resembles mockery, because we say: there is no obstacle to the soundness of the responder considering himself as commanding himself, calling them, moving the silent letters, addressing them with encouragement and urging for actual response, then he disclaims power and strength. And we have seen from some mashayikh of suluk who combine between them. His saying: (and the supplication is answered after his response with similar words) meaning even in the two hay'alah, and its evidence is in the aforementioned Musnad Abi Ya'la. His saying: (wa bararta) is an explanatory conjunction to what precedes, from birr in speech meaning truthful, and birr in oath meaning keeping it. It is said: he says 'sadaqta wa bil-haqqi nataqta' (you spoke truth and with truth you spoke) as in Majma' al-Anhur, and there is no harm in combining. Some virtuous scholars said: and he says at 'qad qamati al-salah', 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha' (may Allah establish it and perpetuate it). This has been reported from the Prophet, mentioned by al-Halabi and others. The meaning of 'aqamaha Allahu' is made it firm and everlasting. It is said in Sharh al-Mishkat that after his saying 'wa adamaha' the addition 'wa ja'alani min salihi ahliha' (and make me of its righteous people) became famous. And this appears only according to the statement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the beginning (of prayer) is after finishing (the iqamah). As for the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa) that the preferred act is to begin at 'qad qamati al-salah' and that the best is for the follower to match the imam in the tahrimah, it does not appear. His saying: (ma sha' Allahu kana) 'kana' here is complete, and 'yakun' later is also complete. His saying: (and the mu'adhdhin) to obtain the virtue, as in the sharh. His saying: (bi al-wasilah) i.e., by obtaining it. His saying: (when he hears the call) this necessitates that the supplication is when he hears the call, and what will come necessitates that he supplicates after finishing the response. So either combine between them, or carry the first upon the second, and the meaning of 'when he hears' is promptness and haste, or it means the entire adhan. His saying: (al-da'wati) with fatha on the dal, meaning supplication. 'al-tammati' the complete, which has no deficiency or defect, no religion changes it, and no sharia abrogates it. In this supplication are the best statements, which is 'la ilaha illa Allah'. Al-Ayni said: it extends to 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'. His saying: (al-salati) 'al-qa'imi' meaning the continuous and established. His saying: (ati Muhammadan al-wasilah) 'al-wasilah' is fa'ilah and plural is wasa'il and wasl; it is every matter that leads to what you seek.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya addresses two specific aspects of responding to the adhan: the response to the Fajr adhan and the supplication for al-wasilah. For the Fajr adhan, when the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep), the responder should not repeat the same phrase but instead say 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and are righteous) or 'ma sha' Allahu kana...' (what Allah wills happens...). This is to avoid mockery, since repeating the exact words could be seen as mimicking the caller's statement that prayer is better than sleep, as if one is telling himself. The passage notes that the Hanafi imams differed on the ruling of responding to the adhan in general: some considered it wajib (obligatory) while others considered it mustahabb (recommended). The relied-upon view is mustahabb. After the response, both the responder and the mu'adhdhin are encouraged to send blessings upon the Prophet and then supplicate for al-wasilah, which is a high station in Paradise granted to the Prophet. The specific du'a is narrated by Jabir: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imi, ati Muhammadan al-wasilah.' The passage discusses the timing of this du'a: some say it is said upon hearing the call, others say after the response. The preferred view is to do it after the response, but one can also combine. There is also discussion about saying 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha' upon hearing 'qad qamati al-salah' in the iqamah, with a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding when to stand for prayer. The passage concludes with commentary on the meanings of the words in the du'a.

Key Terms
إجابة (ijabah): The act of responding to the mu'adhdhin's call.
بررت (bararta): Literally 'you are righteous'; used in response to 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' to affirm the truth of the statement.
صدقت (sadaqta): You have spoken the truth; another response phrase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Repeat the exact phrase.
B) Say 'sadaqta wa bararta'.
C) Say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'.
D) Remain silent.

Key Takeaway
In the Fajr adhan, affirm the mu'adhdhin's statement with 'sadaqta wa bararta' rather than repeating it, and remember that responding to the adhan is a recommended sunnah.

The Du'a for Wasilah After the Adhan
Ruling on du'a for wasilah after adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the du'a for wasilah and determine the preferred timing for it after the adhan.

Core Idea
After the adhan, ask Allah to grant the Prophet the wasilah—a unique station in Paradise.

After the mu'adhdhin finishes the call, both the caller and listener are encouraged to send blessings on the Prophet and then supplicate for al-wasilah. This du'a is a means of honoring the Prophet and seeking his intercession. The lesson also addresses the timing of this supplication.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of wasilah
Wasilah is a high rank in Paradise reserved for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It is the means by which one draws near to Allah.
The du'a asks Allah to grant the Prophet this station.
2
Learn the du'a text and its evidence
The du'a is: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imi, ati Muhammadan al-wasilah.' It is narrated by Jabir and authenticated by al-Hakim.
The du'a is recited after sending blessings on the Prophet.
3
Determine the timing of the du'a
The passage notes a difference: some say it is said upon hearing the adhan, others after the response. The preferred view is to say it after finishing the response to the adhan, but combining both timings is possible.
The phrase 'when he hears the call' may indicate promptness, not necessarily during the adhan.
4
Note the additional phrases in the du'a
The du'a includes asking for one's needs after requesting the wasilah. The passage also mentions that the du'a is answered after the response.
One may also add personal supplications after the wasilah du'a.

This has been reported from the Prophet, mentioned by al-Halabi and others. The meaning of 'aqamaha Allahu' is made it firm and everlasting. It is said in Sharh al-Mishkat that after his saying 'wa adamaha' the addition 'wa ja'alani min salihi ahliha' (and make me of its righteous people) became famous. And this appears only according to the statement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the beginning (of prayer) is after finishing (the iqamah). As for the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa) that the preferred act is to begin at 'qad qamati al-salah' and that the best is for the follower to match the imam in the tahrimah, it does not appear. His saying: (ma sha' Allahu kana) 'kana' here is complete, and 'yakun' later is also complete. His saying: (and the mu'adhdhin) to obtain the virtue, as in the sharh. His saying: (bi al-wasilah) i.e., by obtaining it. His saying: (when he hears the call) this necessitates that the supplication is when he hears the call, and what will come necessitates that he supplicates after finishing the response. So either combine between them, or carry the first upon the second, and the meaning of 'when he hears' is promptness and haste, or it means the entire adhan. His saying: (al-da'wati) with fatha on the dal, meaning supplication. 'al-tammati' the complete, which has no deficiency or defect, no religion changes it, and no sharia abrogates it. In this supplication are the best statements, which is 'la ilaha illa Allah'. Al-Ayni said: it extends to 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'. His saying: (al-salati) 'al-qa'imi' meaning the continuous and established. His saying: (ati Muhammadan al-wasilah) 'al-wasilah' is fa'ilah and plural is wasa'il and wasl; it is every matter that leads to what you seek.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya addresses two specific aspects of responding to the adhan: the response to the Fajr adhan and the supplication for al-wasilah. For the Fajr adhan, when the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep), the responder should not repeat the same phrase but instead say 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and are righteous) or 'ma sha' Allahu kana...' (what Allah wills happens...). This is to avoid mockery, since repeating the exact words could be seen as mimicking the caller's statement that prayer is better than sleep, as if one is telling himself. The passage notes that the Hanafi imams differed on the ruling of responding to the adhan in general: some considered it wajib (obligatory) while others considered it mustahabb (recommended). The relied-upon view is mustahabb. After the response, both the responder and the mu'adhdhin are encouraged to send blessings upon the Prophet and then supplicate for al-wasilah, which is a high station in Paradise granted to the Prophet. The specific du'a is narrated by Jabir: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imi, ati Muhammadan al-wasilah.' The passage discusses the timing of this du'a: some say it is said upon hearing the call, others say after the response. The preferred view is to do it after the response, but one can also combine. There is also discussion about saying 'aqamaha Allahu wa adamaha' upon hearing 'qad qamati al-salah' in the iqamah, with a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding when to stand for prayer. The passage concludes with commentary on the meanings of the words in the du'a.

Key Terms
وسيلة (wasilah): A high station in Paradise that will be granted uniquely to the Prophet Muhammad; the means by which one draws near to Allah.
دعوة تامة (da'wah tammah): The perfect call, referring to the adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct sequence after the adhan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Send salawat, then respond to the adhan, then du'a for wasilah.
B) Respond to the adhan, then send salawat, then du'a for wasilah.
C) Du'a for wasilah, then send salawat, then respond.
D) Only respond to the adhan, no du'a needed.

Key Takeaway
After responding to the adhan, send blessings on the Prophet and ask Allah for the wasilah—a beloved sunnah that honors the Prophet and opens the door for supplications.

The Adhan Supplication and the Reward of Intercession
Explains the wording and reward of the supplication after the adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the supplication after the adhan, identify its proof from the hadith, and explain the meaning of al-wasilah.

Core Idea
Asking Allah for al-wasilah for the Prophet guarantees his intercession on the Day of Judgment.

The adhan is followed by a supplication that carries immense reward. This lesson explores the hadith of Ibn Umar, which instructs the listener to repeat the adhan, send blessings upon the Prophet, and ask Allah for al-wasilah. We will examine the Hanafi ruling on this practice and the deeper meanings of the key terms mentioned in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being described and classify it according to the five categories (fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, mubah). The passage discusses the supplication after the adhan.
The Hanafi school rules it as mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith of Ibn Umar. Note the type of dalil (Sunnah ahad) and its content.
The hadith contains clear imperatives but is interpreted as recommendation due to context and reward.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling. Here, the imperative 'sallu' and 'saloo' indicate command, but the absence of qarina for obligation and the promise of reward point to nadb.
This is a key usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub illa bi-qarinah.
4
Define key terms
Understand the meanings of wasilah, fadilah, al-maqam al-mahmud, and shafa'ah as explained in the commentary.
Wasilah is the highest station in Paradise; al-maqam al-mahmud is the great intercession.
5
Evaluate the practice of rubbing thumbs
Consider the additional practice mentioned in the 'faa'idah'. Note that while it is reported, it is not part of the original hadith and is considered optional.
This is an example of ikhtilaf; the core supplication is agreed upon, but the extra gesture is disputed.
