كتاب الصلاة
والفضيلة وابعثه مقاماً محموداً الذي وعدته حلت له شفاعتي يوم القيامة وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إذا سمعتم المؤذن فقولوا مثل ما يقول ثم صلوا علي صلاة فإنه من صلى علي صلاة صلى الله عليه بها عشراً، ثم سلوا الله لي الوسيلة، فإنها منزلة في الجنة لا تنبغي إلا لعبد مؤمن من عباد الله وأرجو أن أكون أنا فمن سأل لي الوسيلة حلت له شفاعتي يوم القيامة . وحقيقة الوسيلة إلى الله عز وجل مراعاة سبيله بالعلم والعبادة وتجري مكارم الشريعة فهي كالقربة قاله الراغب، وحاصله أنها فعل المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات والمراد هنا منزلة عالية في الجنة فهو مجاز من إطلاق السبب على المسبب قوله : ( والفضيلة). المرتبة الزائدة على سائر الخلق، أو منزلة أخرى، أو تفسير للوسيلة. قال السخاوي في المقاصد الحسنة وزيادة والدرجة الرفيعة كما يفعله من لا خبرة له بالسنة لا أصل لها في الدعاء الوارد ذكره الشهاب في شرح الشفاء قوله : (مقاماً محموداً) مفعول ثان لأبعثه بتضمينه أعط أو على المفعول المطلق أي ابعثه يوم القيامة فأقمه مقاماً محموداً، وضمن بعث معنى أقم، وهو منكر لمناسبة لفظ القرآن أو للتفخيم ووقع في رواية النسائي وابن خزيمة، وغيرهما المقام المحمود بالتعريف والمراد به الشفاعة العظمى، وهو الأشهر، وعليه الأكثر وقيل هو ان يسأل فيعطي ويشفع فيشفع، وليس أحد إلا تحت لوائه . قوله : (الذي وعدته أي في قوله تعالى : عسى أن يبعثك ربك مقاماً محموداً وهو صفة للمقام إن جعل علماً لذلك المقام، وإلا فهو بدل قوله حلت له شفاعتي) حل من باب ضرب أي وجبت بمعنى تحققت وثبتت أو من باب قعد بمعنى نزل واللام في له بمعنى على، والمراد بالشفاعة شفاعة مخصوصة كدخول الجنة مع السابقين ورفع الدرجات، وزيادة العطيات، ولا يختص هذا الفضل بمن قالها مستحضراً لأخلاقه ، بل يكفي فيه مجرد إلا أنه ينبغي أن لا يكون لاهياً لاغياً. ذكره الشهاب في شرح الشفاء، وفائدة هذا الدعاء تحقق مدلوله له عليه الصلاة والسلام الإمتثال أو ترتب الثواب الموعود لقائله. قوله : (صلى الله عليه بها عشراً) أي أنعم عليه بإنعامات عشرة بسبب دعائه له . قوله: (وأرجو أن أكون أنا هو هذا من الأدب مع الله تعالى والتباعد عن التحكم عليه، أو قاله قبل أن يطلعه الله تعالى على أنه هو.
فائدة: ذكر القهستاني عن كنز العباد أنه يستحب أن يقول عند سماع الأولى من الشهادتين للنبي صلى الله عليك يا رسول الله وعند سماع الثانية قرت عيني بك يا رسول الله اللهم متعني بالسمع والبصر بعد وضع إبهاميه على عينيه فإنه يكون قائداً له في الجنة، وذكر الديلمي في الفردوس من حديث أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً من مسح باطن أنملة السبابتين بعد تقبيلهما عند قول المؤذن أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله، وقال: أشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله رضيت بالله رباً وبالإسلام ديناً وبمحمد نبياً حلت له شفاعتي اهـ وكذا روي عن الخضر عليه السلام وبمثله يعمل في الفضائل . اعلم أن من هذه المنزلة تتفرع جميع الجنات وهي جنة عدن دار المقامة ولها شعبة في كل جنة من الجنان من تلك الشعبة يظهر محمد لأهل تلك الجنة وهي في كل جنة أعظم منزلة فيها جعلنا الله من الفائزين بشفاعته ومجاورته في دار كرامته .
The Book of Prayer. And (he said) al-fadilah, and raise him to a praiseworthy station which You have promised him; his intercession will be lawful for him on the Day of Resurrection. And from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say similar to what he says, then send blessings upon me, for whoever sends blessings upon me once, Allah sends ten blessings upon him. Then ask Allah for al-wasilah for me, for it is a station in Paradise which is not appropriate except for a believing servant of Allah's servants, and I hope that I will be that one. Whoever asks for al-wasilah for me, my intercession will be lawful for him on the Day of Resurrection.' The reality of wasilah to Allah is observing His path with knowledge and worship and following the noble aspects of the Shariah, so it is like a means of closeness, as al-Raghib said. Its summary is doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden. What is meant here is a high station in Paradise; it is a metaphor of calling the cause by the effect. His statement (al-fadilah): the extra rank above all creation, or another station, or an interpretation of wasilah. Al-Sakhawi said in al-Maqasid al-Hasana that the addition 'and the high degree' as done by those with no knowledge of the sunnah has no basis in the reported supplication, as mentioned by al-Shihab in Sharh al-Shifa'. His statement (praiseworthy station) is a second object of 'ab'athu' with the implication of 'give', or an absolute object, meaning raise him on the Day of Resurrection and establish him in a praiseworthy station. 'Ba'atha' is given the meaning of 'aqama'. It is indefinite for harmony with the Quranic wording or for glorification. In the narration of al-Nasa'i and Ibn Khuzaymah and others, it occurs as 'al-maqam al-mahmud' with definite article, meaning the great intercession, which is the most famous and the majority view. It is also said that he will be asked and given, and he will intercede and his intercession will be accepted, and no one will be except under his banner. His statement (which You have promised him) i.e., in His saying: 'It may be that your Lord will raise you to a praiseworthy station' (17:79). It is an adjective for 'station' if it is made a proper noun for that station, otherwise it is a substitute. His statement 'his intercession will be lawful for him': 'halla' from the pattern of daraba meaning wajaba (obligated) meaning it is confirmed and established, or from the pattern of qa'ada meaning nazala (descended). The lam in 'lahu' has the meaning of 'ala'. What is meant by intercession is a specific intercession, such as entering Paradise with the foremost and raising of ranks and increase of gifts. This virtue is not specific to one who says it while mindful of his character; rather, mere uttering suffices, but it is appropriate that he not be heedless or engaged in idle talk, as mentioned by al-Shihab in Sharh al-Shifa'. The benefit of this supplication is the realization of its meaning for him (peace be upon him) by obedience or the attainment of the promised reward for the one who says it. His statement (Allah sends ten blessings upon him) meaning He bestows upon him ten favors due to his supplication for him. His statement (And I hope that I will be that one) this is from politeness towards Allah and avoiding presumption against Him, or he said it before Allah informed him that he is that one. Benefit: Al-Qahistani mentioned from Kanz al-'Ibad that it is recommended to say upon hearing the first of the two testifications for the Prophet: 'Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah' and upon hearing the second: 'My eyes are delighted with you, O Messenger of Allah, O Allah, benefit me with hearing and sight' after placing his two thumbs on his eyes, for he will be a guide for him in Paradise. Al-Daylami mentioned in al-Firdaws from the hadith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) raised: 'Whoever wipes the inner side of the tips of the index fingers after kissing them when the mu'adhdhin says "I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah" and says: "I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, I am pleased with Allah as Lord, with Islam as religion, and with Muhammad as Prophet", his intercession will be lawful for him.' Likewise it is narrated from al-Khidr (peace be upon him), and similar practice is done in virtuous matters. Know that from this station all the gardens branch out, and it is the Garden of Eden, the abode of staying, and it has a branch in every garden of paradise; from that branch Muhammad appears to the people of that garden. It is in every garden the greatest station therein. May Allah make us among those who attain his intercession and his neighborhood in the abode of His generosity.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi is an expansion on the hadith regarding the recommended supplication after the adhan. The author first cites the hadith of Ibn Umar which instructs the listener to repeat the adhan, send blessings on the Prophet, and then ask Allah for al-wasilah. The commentary then defines 'wasilah' and 'fadilah', clarifying that wasilah is a high station in Paradise, and that the mere utterance of the supplication suffices to secure the promised intercession, though one should avoid heedlessness. A 'faa'idah' (benefit) is added, mentioning a specific practice of wiping the index fingers and saying a phrase upon hearing the shahadah from the mu'adhdhin, which is also reported to attain intercession. The author concludes with a reminder that the Prophet's station is the greatest in Paradise. The ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to say this supplication, and the Hanafi school accepts the hadith as sound evidence for this practice.

Key Terms
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): Literally a means of closeness; here it refers to the highest station in Paradise reserved for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
الفضيلة (al-fadilah): An added rank or virtue above all creation; sometimes interpreted as a separate station or as synonymous with al-wasilah.
المقام المحمود (al-maqam al-mahmud): The praiseworthy station, interpreted here as the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) on the Day of Resurrection.
الشفاعة (al-shafa'ah): Intercession, specifically the Prophet's intercession on the Day of Resurrection for his ummah, including entering Paradise and raising ranks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Distinguishing Shart from Rukn in Salah
Lexical and legal definitions of shart and rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shart (condition) and rukn (pillar) according to the Hanafi definitions, applying examples from salah.

Core Idea
A condition is external to the act; a pillar is internal — both invalidate when omitted, but only the pillar is part of the essence.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) of prayer. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal definitions from Maraqi al-Falah and its hashia, clarifying that while both are necessary for validity, they occupy different conceptual spaces: one outside the act, the other within its essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key terms
Locate the definitions of shart and rukn in the source. Note the plural forms (shurut vs. arkan) and the linguistic roots.
Shart comes from 'sharata' meaning to bind; rukn from 'rukn' meaning strong side.
2
Understand the legal definition of shart
The text says: 'In the Shariah, it is that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to its essence.' So a condition is necessary but outside the act. Give an example like wudu for prayer.
Contrast with sabab (cause) and 'illa (effective cause) mentioned later.
3
Understand the legal definition of rukn
The text says a rukn is internal to the act, like bowing in prayer. If omitted, the act is invalid because an integral part is missing.
The word rukn implies strength and support; the act leans on it.
4
Distinguish from 'illa
The text differentiates between what is inside (rukn), what is outside but effective ('illa, like a contract making sex permissible), and what is outside and not effective (pure shart). Note that shart is not a cause.
This threefold classification (rukn, 'illa, shart) is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the distinction to prayer
List typical shurut of salah (e.g., wudu, facing qibla, covering awrah) and arkan (e.g., qiyam, ruku, sujud). Verify each fits the definition: conditions are external prerequisites, pillars are internal actions.
Use the Hanafi list: shurut al-salah are 6 (or 4 in some texts); arkan are 6 (including qira'ah as wajib, not rukn, but that's another lesson).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها
جمعنا بينهما للتيقظ لما تصح به الصلاة الشروط جمع شرط بسكون الراء والاشراط جمع شرط بفتحها وهما العلامة وفي الشريعة هو ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهيته، والأركان جمع ركن وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى، وفي الاصطلاح
أن محمداً عبده ورسوله رضيت بالله رباً وبالإسلام ديناً وبمحمد نبياً حلت له شفاعتي اهـ وكذا روي عن الخضر عليه السلام وبمثله يعمل في الفضائل قوله : (تتفرع جميع الجنات) يحتمل أن المعنى أنه الأصل لكل جنة فباقي دورها تبع لها قوله : دار المقامة) بيان لجنة عدن قال ابن كثير : الوسيلة أقرب منازل الجنة إلى العرش وأعلاها، وأشرفها ويدل عليه ما رواه الإمام أحمد عن أبي سعيد الخدري مرفوعاً الوسيلة درجة عند الله ليس فوقها درجة فأسألوا الله أن يؤتيني الوسيلة قوله : (بشفاعته) المراد شفاعة مخصوصة كرفع الدرجات. قوله: ( ومجاورته) المجاورة لكل شخص بما يناسبه والله تعالى أعلم .
باب شروط الصلاة
قوله : (للتيقظ) أي للتنبه. قوله : (جمع شرط) وهو ثلاثة أنواع عقلي كالقدوم للنجار، وشرعي كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق كذا في الشرح قوله: (وهما العلامة مسلم في الثاني ومنه قوله تعالى : فقد جاء أشراطها أي علاماتها ومنه الحاكم سمي صاحب شرطة بالضم ، والجمع شرط (۱) كرطبة ورطب أي صاحب علامة لأن له علامة تميزه والشرط على لفظ الجمع أعوان السلطان لأنهم جعلوا لأنفسهم علامات يعرفون بها، وأما الأول فأصله مصدر شرط کنصر، وضرب واستعمل لغة في إلزام الشيء والتزامه في بيع، ونحوه والشريطة بمعناه هذا ما يدل عليه عبارت أهل اللغة قوله: (وفي الشريعة الخ) اعلم إن ماله تعلق بالشيء أما أن يكون داخلاً فيه أو لا الأول الركن كالركوع في الصلاة، والثاني إن كان مؤثراً فيه بحسب الظاهر فهو العلة كعقد النكاح المحلل للوطء، وإن لم يكن مؤثراً فيه فإن
(۱) قوله كرطبة ورطب الأولى كغرفة وغرف وكرطبة لغة قليلة اهـ كتبه مصححه .
Chapter of the Conditions of Prayer and Its Pillars. We combined them for alertness as to what prayer is valid with. Conditions (shurut) is the plural of shart with sukun on the ra, and al-ashrat is the plural of shart with fatha on the ra, and both mean 'sign'. In the Shariah, it is that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to its essence. Pillars (arkan) is the plural of rukn, which in language is the strongest side, and in terminology... (intervening text: 'That Muhammad is His slave and Messenger...' etc.) Chapter of the Conditions of Prayer. His statement (for alertness) i.e., for wakefulness. His statement (conditions) and they are three types: rational like the coming of the carpenter, legal like purification for prayer, and contractual like the conditional divorce attached to entry, as in the Sharh. His statement (and both mean 'sign') is accepted in the second meaning. From it is His statement: 'Indeed the signs of the Hour have come' (47:18). From it is the ruler called the 'sahib al-shurta' (head of police), and the plural is shurat like rutab and ratb, i.e., the owner of a sign because he has a distinguishing sign. And 'shart' in the sense of plural refers to the ruler's assistants because they have made for themselves signs by which they are known. As for the first, its origin is the masdar of sharata, and it is used linguistically to mean binding something and adhering to it in sale and the like; and shartah (condition) has the same meaning. This is what the statements of the linguists indicate. His statement (and in the Shariah, etc.): Know that whatever has connection to a thing either enters into it or does not. The first is the rukn, like bowing in prayer. The second: if it is effective upon it manifestly, it is the cause ('illa) like the marriage contract that makes intercourse permissible. If it is not effective upon it, then... (footnote omitted).
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi begins the chapter on the conditions and pillars of prayer. The author states that he combined both topics for the sake of alertness. He then defines the terms. 'Shart' (condition) linguistically means a sign, and legally it is something upon which the existence of an act depends but is external to its essence. For example, wudu is a condition for prayer; prayer is not valid without it, but wudu is not part of the prayer. 'Rukn' (pillar) linguistically means the strong side, and legally it is something that is internal to the act, such as bowing (ruku') in prayer. If a pillar is omitted, the act is invalid; if a condition is omitted, the act is also invalid, but the condition is outside the act. The passage also discusses the linguistic aspects, including the plural forms and the three types of conditions: rational, legal, and contractual. The legal definition emphasizes that a condition is that without which the thing does not exist, but it is outside its essence. This distinction is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh. Note: The text includes an interpolation of commentary from the previous topic about wasilah, which is not part of this chapter. The intended lesson is the definition of shurut and arkan.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): In this text, shart (condition) is defined as that upon which the existence of something depends, and it is external to its essence. Examples: purification for prayer.
الركن (al-rukn): In this text, rukn (pillar) is defined as that which is internal to the act. Example: bowing (ruku') in prayer.
العلامة (al-'alamah): Sign; a linguistic meaning of shart.
العلة (al-'illa): Cause; something that is effective upon the act manifestly, like the marriage contract making intercourse permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what distinguishes a shart from a rukn?
A) Shart is optional; rukn is obligatory
B) Shart is external to the act; rukn is internal
C) Shart is based on reason; rukn on revelation
D) Shart is a cause; rukn is an effect

Key Takeaway
A shart is an external prerequisite for an act's validity, while a rukn is an internal integral component; both are essential but conceptually distinct.

Shart and Rukn: Key Distinctions in Prayer Validity
Defines shart and rukn, then lists first conditions with legal analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart and rukn in Hanafi law, distinguish between them, and state the first condition (tahara) with its legal basis.

Core Idea
A condition is external and prerequisite; a pillar is integral and essential. Both are obligatory for prayer validity.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah opens the chapter on prayer conditions by clarifying two fundamental legal concepts: shart (condition) and rukn (pillar). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assessing what makes prayer valid. The author then begins listing the conditions, starting with the most important: purity (tahara) from hadath.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish shart and rukn
Identify the key features: shart is external and prerequisite, rukn is integral and part of the essence. Both are obligatory but conceptually different.
Hanafis are unique in maintaining this strict separation; other schools may blur the lines.
2
Locate the 27 elements
Note the author's statement that 27 things are necessary for prayer validity, though some simplify to 12 (6 conditions + 6 pillars). Understand this as a comprehensive list.
The 27 are not all enumerated here; the text only begins with the first condition.
3
Analyze the definition of hadath
Examine the dual definition: linguistically 'an occurring thing'; legally 'a shari' prevention that resides in the limbs until removed'.
This definition is foundational for understanding the requirement of wudu and ghusl.
4
Recognize classification of conditions
The passage classifies conditions into four types based on when they are required (initiation, continuity, etc.). Purity is a condition of both initiation and continuity.
This classification helps in determining at which point a missing condition invalidates the prayer.

باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها
جمعنا بينهما للتيقظ لما تصح به الصلاة الشروط جمع شرط بسكون الراء والاشراط جمع شرط بفتحها وهما العلامة وفي الشريعة هو ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهيته، والأركان جمع ركن وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى، وفي الاصطلاح الجزء الذاتي الذي تتركب الماهية منه، ومن غيره وقد أردنا تنبيه العابد فقلنا : لا بد لصحة من سبعة وعشرين شيئاً ولا حصر فيها ومن اقتصر على ذكر الشروط الستة الخارجة الصلاة، وعلى الستة الأركان الداخلة فيها أراد التقريب وإلا فالمصلي يحتاج إلى ما ذكرناه بزيادة فأردنا به بيان ما إليه الحاجة من شرط صحة الشروع، والدوام على صحتها وكلها فروض وعبر بلفظ الشيء الصادق بالشرط والركن فمن الشروط الطهارة من الحدث) الأصغر والأكبر والحيض والنفاس لآية الوضوء والحدث لغة الشيء الحادث وشرعاً مانعية شرعية تقوم بالأعضاء إلى غاية وصول المزيل لها (و) منها (طهارة الجسد والثوب والمكان)
كان مفضياً إليه في الجملة فهو السبب كالوقت لوجوب الصلاة وإن لم يكن مفضياً إليه فإن توقف الشيء عليه فهو الشرط كالطهارة للصلاة وإن لم يتوقف عليه الشيء سمي علامة كالأذان للصلاة ذكره الحموي. قوله: (وهو) في اللغة الجانب الأقوى قال تعالى : (أو آوي إلى ركن شدید) [هود: ۱۱] أي عز ومنعة قوله : (الجزء الذاتي ويطلق الفرد عليه كما يطلق على الشرط. قوله : (أراد التقريب) أي تقريب الحفظ على المتعلم. قوله : (بزيادة) الباء بمعنى مع، وسيأتي له ذكر الزيادة شرحاً قوله : (من شرط صحة الشروع، والدوام على صحتها) اعلم أن الشروط من حيث هي أربعة أقسام : شرط إنعقاد لا غير كالنية، والتحريمة، والوقت والخطبة للجمعة وشرط إنعقاد ودوام كالطهارة وستر العورة، وإستقبال القبلة وشرط بقاء لا غير أي ما يشترط وجوده داخل الصلاة، وهو نوعان ما يشترط فيه التعيين كترتيب ما لم يشرع مكرراً، والثاني ما لا . يشترط فيه التعيين، وهو نوعان أيضاً : وجودي وعدمي، فالوجودي كالقراءة فإنها وإن كانت ركناً، إلا أنها ركن في نفسها شرط لغيرها لوجودها في كل الأركان تقديراً، ولذا لم يجز استخلاف الأمي، ولو بعد أداء فرض القراءة كما في الدر، والعدمي كعدم تقدم المقتدي على إمامه، وعدم محاذاة مشتهاة في صلاة مشتركة، وعدم تذكر صاحب الترتيب فائتة، والقسم الرابع شرط خروج، وهو القعدة الأخيرة. قوله: (فمن الشروط الطهارة) قدمها على سائر الشروط لأنها أهم إذ هي مفتاح الصلاة، ولأنها أول مسؤول عنه . في القبر . قوله : (والحيض والنفاس) لا حاجة إلى ذكرهما لأن المراد بالحدث الأكبر ما أوجب الغسل، ويحتمل أنه أراد به هنا خصوص الجنابة قوله : (والحدث لغة الشيء الحادث قال في القاموس : الحدث محركة الإبداء، وقال قبله : حدث حدوثاً وحداثة نقيض قدم وتضم داله إذا ذكر مع قدم اهـ وهذا يفيد أن إطلاقه على الشيء الحادث من إطلاق المصدر على إسم الفاعل . قوله: (وشرعاً ماتعية شرعية) المانعية الكون ،مانعاً وهذا لا بد له من موصوف يصح إسناده إليه بحيث يقال : معنى كون البول حدثاً أنه مانعية شرعية أي كون مانعاً الخ والمصنف ذكره مجرداً عن الموصوف فلو قال وشرعا مانع شرعي يقوم الخ أي مانع عما يباح إلا برافعه لكان أوضح، وفي شرح الخطيب لأبي شجاع أنه في الشرع يطلق على أمر إعتباري يقوم بالأعضاء يمنع من
Chapter of the Conditions of Prayer and Its Pillars. We have combined them for awareness of what makes prayer valid. 'Al-shurut' is the plural of 'shart' with sukun on the ra', and 'al-ashrat' is the plural of 'shart' with fatha; both mean 'sign'. In the Shari'ah, it is that upon whose existence something depends, and it is outside its essence. 'Al-arkan' is plural of 'rukn', which in language means 'the strongest side', and in terminology it is the essential part from which the essence is composed, and from other than it. And we intended to alert the worshiper, so we said: For validity, twenty-seven things are necessary, and there is no limit to them. And whoever restricts himself to mentioning the six external conditions of prayer and the six internal pillars intends simplification; otherwise, the worshiper needs what we have mentioned with addition. So we intended by it to explain what is needed in terms of conditions for the validity of commencement and continuity of its validity, and all of them are obligations (furood). And he expressed with the word 'thing' which applies to both condition and pillar. So among the conditions is purity (tahara) from minor and major hadath, and from menstruation and post-natal bleeding, based on the verse of wudu. 'Al-hadath' linguistically means 'the occurring thing', and legally it is a shari' prevention that resides in the limbs until the arrival of that which removes it. And among them is purity of the body, garment, and place. If it leads to it in general, it is the cause (sabab) like time for the obligation of prayer; if it does not lead to it, but the thing depends on it, it is the condition (shart) like purity for prayer; if the thing does not depend on it, it is called a sign (alamah) like the adhan for prayer. Al-Hamawi mentioned it. His statement: (and it) in language is 'the strongest side'; Allah said: 'or take refuge in a strong pillar' [Hud 11:80] meaning might and protection. His statement: (the essential part) and the individual is called by it just as it is called by the condition. His statement: (he intended simplification) i.e. to simplify memorization for the student. His statement: (with addition) the 'ba' means 'with', and he will mention the addition later in the commentary. His statement: (from the conditions of validity of commencement and continuity of its validity) – know that conditions, in terms of their nature, are of four types: a condition of initiation only, like intention, takbir, time, and the khutbah for Friday; a condition of initiation and continuity, like purity, covering the 'awrah, and facing the qiblah; a condition of continuation only, i.e. what is required to exist inside the prayer, and it is of two types: that which requires specific designation like the order of what is not repeated, and the second is that which does not require specific designation, also of two types: existential and non-existential. The existential is like recitation, for although it is a pillar, it is a pillar in itself but a condition for others due to its existence in all pillars in estimation; therefore it is not permissible to appoint an illiterate person as an imam, even after performing the obligation of recitation as in al-Durr. The non-existential is like the follower not preceding his imam, and not facing a person's private part in a joint prayer, and the owner of al-tartib not forgetting a missed prayer. The fourth type is a condition of exit, which is the last sitting. His statement: (so from the conditions is purity) – he gave it precedence over other conditions because it is the most important, as it is the key to prayer, and because it is the first thing asked about in the grave. His statement: (and menstruation and post-natal bleeding) – there is no need to mention them because by major hadath is meant what necessitates ghusl, and it is possible that he intended here specifically janabah. His statement: (and al-hadath linguistically is the occurring thing) – he said in al-Qamus: 'al-hadath' (with fatha on ha and dal) means 'the beginning', and before that he said: 'hadatha huduthan wa hadathah is the opposite of qidam, and its dal is doubled when mentioned with qidam'. This tells that applying it to the occurring thing is applying the masdar to the ism al-fa'il. His statement: (and legally it is a shari' prevention) – the prevention is being a preventer, and this must have a described thing to which it is attributed such that it is said: the meaning of urine being hadath is that it is a shari' prevention, i.e. being a preventer, etc. The author mentioned it devoid of the described thing; if he had said 'and legally it is a shari' preventer that resides...' meaning a preventer from what is permissible except with its remover, it would be clearer. In the commentary of al-Khatib on Abi Shuja', it is said that legally it is applied to an imaginary matter that resides in the limbs and prevents from...
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on the conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) of prayer from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah. The author explains why he combined both topics: to alert the worshiper about what makes prayer valid. He defines 'shart' linguistically as a sign and legally as something external to the essence of an act upon which the act depends. 'Rukn' linguistically means the strongest side and legally is the essential part from which the essence is composed. The author then clarifies that for prayer to be valid, twenty-seven elements are necessary, but some scholars simplify by listing six external conditions and six internal pillars. He states that all of these are obligations (furood). He then begins listing the conditions, starting with purity (tahara) from hadath (minor and major), menstruation, and post-natal bleeding, citing the verse of wudu. He defines hadath linguistically as an occurring thing and legally as a shari' prevention residing in the limbs until removal. Next he mentions purity of the body, garment, and place. He then digresses into a classification of conditions: conditions of initiation only (like intention), conditions of initiation and continuity (like purity), conditions of continuity only (existential and non-existential), and conditions of exit (the last sitting). He explains why purity is given precedence: it is the key to prayer and the first thing asked about in the grave. He also discusses the redundancy of mentioning menstruation and post-natal bleeding separately and comments on the definition of hadath from the Qamus, noting the author's imprecise wording. This passage is a dense lexical and juristic analysis aimed at precise legal understanding.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): A condition: something external to the essence of an act upon which the act depends for validity (e.g., purity for prayer).
الركن (al-rukn): A pillar: an integral part of the act (e.g., bowing in prayer), the omission of which invalidates the act entirely.
الحدث (al-hadath): A state of ritual impurity (minor or major) that prevents performance of acts requiring purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many things are necessary for the validity of prayer?
A) Six
B) Twelve
C) Twenty-seven
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Shart (external condition) and rukn (internal pillar) are both obligatory, but they differ in nature: shart must be present before/alongside the act, while rukn is part of the act itself.

The 27 Essential Items for Prayer and the Four Types of Conditions
Expansion on the 27 required items and classification of conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of conditions for prayer and explain why purification is a condition for both formation and continuation.

Core Idea
A valid prayer requires 27 items—conditions and pillars—and conditions are classified by when they must be present: formation, continuation, or exit.

This lesson clarifies the essential components of prayer according to the Hanafi school. The classical texts often mention six conditions and six pillars for brevity, but the full set includes twenty-seven items. We will explore the distinction between conditions and pillars, the four types of conditions, and the proof for the primary condition of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the total required items
The text states that twenty-seven things are necessary for the validity of prayer. Note that the common mention of six conditions and six pillars is only for ease of memorization.
The number 27 includes both external conditions and internal pillars.
2
Distinguish shart from rukn
A shart (condition) is external to the act, while a rukn (pillar) is an integral part. The text defines rukn as the essential part constituting the reality, and shart as something on which prayer depends but is not part of it.
In Hanafi usul, missing a pillar invalidates the prayer, while missing a condition prevents validity from the start.
3
Classify conditions into four types
Conditions are divided into: (1) for formation only (e.g., intention, takbir), (2) for both formation and continuation (e.g., purification, covering awrah), (3) for continuation only (existential like recitation, non-existential like not advancing ahead of imam), and (4) for exit (final sitting).
This taxonomy helps in understanding when each condition must be present.
4
Analyze the proof for taharah
The proof for purification from hadath is the verse of wudu (Quran 5:6). The imperative form indicates obligation. Hadath is defined as a legal preventive quality residing in the limbs until removed.
Purification is given precedence because it is the key to prayer and the first thing asked about in the grave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
الصلاة عن الجزء الذاتي الذي تتركب الماهية منه، ومن غيره وقد أردنا تنبيه العابد فقلنا : لا بد لصحة من سبعة وعشرين شيئاً ولا حصر فيها ومن اقتصر على ذكر الشروط الستة الخارجة الصلاة، وعلى الستة الأركان الداخلة فيها أراد التقريب وإلا فالمصلي يحتاج إلى ما ذكرناه بزيادة فأردنا به بيان ما إليه الحاجة من شرط صحة الشروع، والدوام على صحتها وكلها فروض وعبر بلفظ الشيء الصادق بالشرط والركن فمن الشروط الطهارة من الحدث) الأصغر والأكبر والحيض والنفاس لآية الوضوء والحدث لغة الشيء الحادث وشرعاً مانعية شرعية تقوم بالأعضاء إلى غاية وصول المزيل لها (و) منها (طهارة الجسد والثوب والمكان)

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the introductory statement of the matn about the necessary items for prayer. The commentator clarifies that the original text mentions twenty-seven things necessary for prayer, and the author's mention of six conditions and six pillars is for ease of memorization. He then defines key terms: a rukn (pillar) is the essential part constituting the reality; a shart (condition) is what prayer depends on but is not part of it. He further classifies conditions into four types: (1) conditions for valid formation (e.g., intention, takbir, time for obligation), (2) conditions both for formation and continuation (purity, covering awrah, facing qibla), (3) conditions for continuation only (existential like recitation which is also a pillar, and non-existential like not advancing ahead of imam), and (4) condition for exiting prayer (final sitting). The passage then focuses on the first condition, taharah (purification), explaining its importance and providing the proof from the verse of wudu (Quran 5:6). It defines hadath linguistically and legally: a legal preventive quality residing in the limbs. The commentary also notes that menses and postpartum bleeding are included in major hadath but the author mentioned them separately for clarity.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition external to the act of prayer that must be present for its validity, e.g., taharah.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer, without which the prayer is invalid, e.g., recitation.
حدث (hadath): A legal preventive quality that resides in the limbs, requiring purification before prayer; includes minor and major types.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many things are necessary for the validity of prayer according to the original text being commented upon?
A) 6 conditions and 6 pillars
B) 27 items
C) 4 types of conditions
D) 12 items

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires 27 items for prayer, classified into conditions and pillars, with purification from hadath as the most important condition.

Purity of Place and Carrying Impurity in Prayer: Hanafi Conditions and Exceptions
Details conditions for purity of the place of prayer and exceptions for carrying impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for purity of the place of prayer and identify when carrying impurity invalidates prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Purity of the place of prayer is a condition; carrying impurity during prayer is only a problem if the impurity moves with you.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on the foundational rules of purity during salah. It clarifies what makes a place pure enough for prayer and when an impurity on your person or clothing is excused. We will work through the specific cases he presents to understand the Hanafi position on these critical details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition for valid prayer
The passage states that the condition is purity from non-excused impurity. This means the place of prayer (feet, forehead, etc.) must be free from any impurity that is not forgiven by the shari'ah.
Non-excused impurity: for light impurity (e.g., urine), less than a quarter of the limb is excused; for heavy impurity (e.g., blood), less than a dirham is excused.
2
Understand exceptions for carrying impurity
The text discusses scenarios where impurity is attached to the worshiper or something they hold: rope with impure object, impure tent, child, bird. Prayer is invalid only if the impurity moves with the worshiper's movement, making him a 'carrier'.
If the impurity is stationary relative to the worshiper, it is not considered carrying.
3
Analyze the criteria for excused impurity
Only impurity above the thresholds (quarter for light, dirham for heavy) invalidates prayer. The passage mentions these thresholds in the commentary.
The text references 'its explanation preceded' referring to earlier knowledge of these thresholds.
4
Delineate the cases of valid and invalid prayer
Apply the condition: if a thin cloth is spread over wet impurity and the smell is detectable, prayer is invalid. If thick cloth prevents smell and sight, prayer is valid. Also: holding a rope – if impure end moves, invalid; otherwise valid. Impure tent touching head: valid if no impurity separates.
The passage also mentions standing on a healthy foot with dislike (karahah) but not invalid.
5
Compare with potential cross-madhhab differences
The Hanafi school is more lenient regarding excused impurity and carrying impurity. The Shafi'i school may require purity of the entire prayer space and may not excuse carrying impurity at all.
This ikhtilaf is noted in the analytical toolbox.

عمامته الذي يصلي عليه فلو بسط شيئاً رقيقاً يصلح ساتراً للعورة وهو ما لا يرى منه الجسد جازت صلاته وإن كانت النجاسة رطبة فألقي عليهما لبداً، أو ثنى ما ليس ثخيناً أو كبسها بالتراب فلم يجد ريح النجاسة جازت صلاته وإذا أمسك حبلاً مربوطاً به نجاسة أو بقي من طرف طاهر ولم يتحرك الطرف النجس بحركته صحت وإلا فلا كما لو أصاب رأسه خيمة نجسة وجلوس صغير يستمسك في حجر المصلى، وطير متنجس على رأسه لا يبطل الصلاة إذا لم تنفصل منه نجاسة مانعة لأن الشرط الطهارة (من) نجس غير معفو عنه) وتقدم بيانه (حتى) أنه يشترط طهارة (موضع القدمين فتبطل الصلاة بنجس مانع تحت أحدهما، أو بجمعه فيهما تقديراً في الأصح وقيامه على قدم صحيح مع الكراهة، وانتقاله مكان عن
عليها ذا
جرم
صحة الصلاة، وعلى الأسباب التي ينتهي بها الظهر، وعلى الأمر المترتب على ذلك اه والأول هو بمعنى قولنا وشرعاً مانع الخ. قوله : (فلو بسط شيئاً رقيقاً يصلح ساتراً الخ) أي ولم تشم منه رائحة النجاسة . قال البرهان الحلبي وكذا الثوب، إذا فرش على النجاسة اليابسة إن كان رقيقاً يشف ما تحته أو توجد منه رائحة النجاسة على تقدير أن لها رائحة لا تجوز الصلاة عليه وإن كان غليظاً بحيث لا يكون كذلك جازت اهـ قوله : ( فألقى عليها البدا) المراد أنه ألقى غليظ يصلح للشق نصفين كحجر، ولبن وخشب كما في البدائع، والخانية، ومنية المصلي وقيد النجاسة بالرطبة لأنها إن كانت يابسة جازت على كل حال لأنها لا تلتزق بالثوب الملقى عليها بعد كونه يصلح ساتراً كذا في الخانية، وفي القهستاني ينبغي أن تكون الصلاة أي على الملقى على النجاسة الرطبة تكره ككراهتها على نحو الإسطبل كما في الخزانة . قوله : فلم يجد ريح النجاسة) أما إذا وجدها لو استشمه لا يجوز كما في الخانية. قوله : (مربوطاً به نجاسة) كسفينة نجسة أو كلب بناء على أنه نجس العين قوله (ولم يتحرك الطرف النجس بحركته) أي المتصل بالنجس فيكون راجعاً إلى المسئلتين، وذلك لأنه بتلك الحركة ينسب إلى حمل النجاسة كما في البحر ،وغيره بخلاف ما لو كانت النجاسة في بعض أطراف البساط حيث تجوز الصلاة على الطاهر منه ولو تحرك الطرف الآخر بحركته لأن البساط بمنزلة الأرض فيشترط فيه طهارة مكان المصلي فقط كما في الخانية. قوله: (خيمة نجسة) مثلها السقف لأنه يعد حاملاً للنجاسة كما ذكره السيد وغيره بخلاف المس كما في القهستاني يعني لو مس نحو حائط نجس بيابس في الصلاة لا يضر لأنه يعد حاملاً للنجاسة. قوله: (وجلوس صغير) أي متنجس يستمسك فإنه لا يعد حاملاً بخلاف ما لا يستمسك، وعليه نجس مانع فإنه تصح معه الصلاة لأنه يعد حاملاً للنجس . قوله : ( وطير) عطف على صغير. قوله : (إذا لم تنفصل منه نجاسة) أي مما ذكر من الصبي والطير . قوله : (لأن الشرط الطهارة) علة لعدم البطلان أي وقد وجدت لأنه لا يعد حاملاً لها قوله : ( وتقدم بيانه) وهو أنه يعفى في غير المغلظة عما دون الربع، وفي المغلظة الدرهم. قوله : (حتى أنه يشترط الخ) تفريع على اشتراط طهارة المكان .
His turban that he prays on. If he spreads a thin cloth that suffices to cover the awrah, i.e., that from which the body is not seen, his prayer is valid. Even if the impurity is wet and he throws onto it a felt piece, or folds what is not thick, or buries it in soil and does not find the smell of impurity, his prayer is valid. If he holds a rope tied to impurity, or remains on a pure side, and the impure side does not move with his movement, it is valid; otherwise it is not, as if his head touches an impure tent, or a small child sitting and clinging to his lap in the prayer place, or a contaminated bird on his head – the prayer is not invalidated if no preventing impurity separates from it, because the condition is purity (from impurity not excused). Its explanation preceded: (even) that purity is required for the place of the feet; so prayer is invalidated by a preventing impurity under one of them, or by its collection in both by estimation in the most correct view, and standing on a healthy foot with dislike, and moving from place to... the health of prayer, and on the causes by which the noon prayer ends, and on the matter resulting from that. The first is in the sense of our saying 'and legally a preventer'. His saying: 'If he spreads a thin cloth that suffices as a cover' i.e., and he does not smell the odor of impurity. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: and similarly a garment, if spread over dry impurity – if it is thin so that what is under it can be seen, or the odor of impurity is found (if it has an odor), prayer is not valid on it; if it is thick such that it is not like that, it is valid. His saying: 'he throws onto it a felt piece' meaning he throws a thick thing that suffices for splitting in half like stone, brick, wood, as in al-Bada'i', al-Khaniyya, and Munyat al-Musalli. He restricted the impurity to wet, because if it is dry, it is valid in any case since it does not stick to the thrown cloth after it suffices as a cover – as in al-Khaniyya. In al-Qahistani: it is preferable that prayer (on the thrown cloth over wet impurity) is disliked as it is disliked on something like a stable (as in al-Khazana). His saying: 'he does not find the odor of impurity' – if he finds it when he sniffs, it is not valid (as in al-Khaniyya). His saying: 'tied to impurity' like an impure ship or dog, based on it being inherently impure. His saying: 'and the impure side does not move with his movement' i.e., the part connected to the impurity, so it refers to both cases. That is because by that movement he is considered to be carrying the impurity, as in al-Bahr and others, contrary to if the impurity is on some edges of the mat, where prayer is valid on the pure part even if the other edge moves with his movement, because the mat is like the ground; only purity of the place of the person praying is required, as in al-Khaniyya. His saying: 'impure tent' – similar is the ceiling, because it is considered to be carrying impurity, as mentioned by al-Sayyid and others, contrary to touching, as in al-Qahistani: if he touches a wall with dry impurity in prayer, it does not harm because he is considered to be carrying the impurity. His saying: 'a small child sitting' i.e., an impure one that clings – he is not considered to be carrying, contrary to one that does not cling – if there is preventing impurity on him, prayer is valid because he is considered to be carrying the impurity. His saying: 'and a bird' is conjuncted to 'small child'. His saying: 'if no impurity separates from them' i.e., from the mentioned child and bird. His saying: 'because the condition is purity' is the cause for non-invalidity: i.e., it is present because he is not considered to be carrying it. His saying: 'and its explanation preceded' that in non-major impurities, less than a quarter is excused, and in major impurities, a dirham. His saying: 'even that it is required' is a branch on the requirement of purity of place.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe detailing the rulings on the purity of the place of prayer. It begins by discussing a person praying on a turban: if he spreads a thin cloth that covers the awrah and does not show the body, prayer is valid. Similarly, if impurity is wet and he places a thick felt piece or folds a thick cloth or covers it with soil so that no smell or trace remains, prayer is valid. The commentary then addresses cases of carrying impurity: if one holds a rope tied to an impure object (e.g., an impure ship or dog), prayer is valid only if the impure end does not move with his movement; otherwise, it is invalid because he is considered to be carrying the impurity. Similarly, if an impure tent touches his head or an impure child sits in his lap, prayer is not invalidated as long as no preventing impurity separates from them, because the core condition is purity, and he is not considered a carrier of the impurity if it is clung to him. The passage clarifies that the place of the feet must be pure; if a preventing impurity is under one foot or both, prayer is invalid unless it is excused (less than a quarter for light impurity, less than a dirham for major). It also notes that standing on a healthy foot is disliked. The commentary cites multiple sources (al-Bada'i', al-Khaniyya, Munyat al-Musalli, al-Bahr, al-Qahistani, etc.) to substantiate these rulings.

Key Terms
مكان (makan): The place where the person prays; includes ground, mat, or any surface directly in contact.
حامل النجاسة (hamil al-najasah): One who physically carries an impurity not attached to their body; considered a carrier only if the impurity moves with them.
نجس غير معفو عنه (najis ghayr ma'fu 'anhu): Impurity that is not excused by the shari'ah (above a quarter or dirham).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prayer is invalid regardless of movement
B) Prayer is valid if the impure end does not move with the person's movement
C) Prayer is valid only if the rope is thick
D) Prayer is invalid because the person is carrying impurity

Key Takeaway
Purity of the place of prayer is a condition; carrying impurity during prayer only invalidates if the impurity moves with you or separates onto your person.

Conditions of Prayer: Purity of Place for Prostration Limbs and Covering Awrah
Commentary on conditions of prayer regarding purity of body parts and covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purity of place for the forehead, hands, and knees during prostration and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding invalidation.

Core Idea
Contact with impurity on any prostration limb invalidates prayer, even if placing that limb is not obligatory.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi clarifies a critical refinement in Hanafi fiqh: the requirement of purity for the place of prostration extends not only to the forehead but also to the hands and knees. He resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute, establishing that even though placing the hands and knees is not fard (obligatory), once they contact impurity, the prayer is invalidated. This lesson unpacks the reasoning (talil) behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
List the three conditions discussed: purity of place for hands and knees, purity of place for forehead, and covering awrah.
These are shurut (conditions) for prayer validity.
2
Analyze the dispute on hands and knees
Note the conflicting opinions: some said purity not required because placement is not fard. The correct view (al-mukhtar) requires purity. Understand the proof: prostration on seven limbs and analogy to carrying impurity.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Apply the reasoning (talil)
Explain the principle: contact with impurity is equivalent to carrying it, which invalidates prayer irrespective of whether the limb's placement is obligatory.
This is the key argument of Abu Yusuf and the chosen view.
4
Resolve the dispute for the forehead
The more sound narration from Abu Hanifa (and the view of the two Sahibayn) requires purity. Even on the weaker opinion, once the forehead is placed on impurity, it invalidates.
Because contact with impurity nullifies the act, as with hands and knees.
5
Contrast with covering awrah
Covering awrah is obligatory by consensus (ijma). Purity of place is more emphatic than purity of garment because place is unavoidable.
This shows the relative importance of different conditions.

طاهر لنجس ولم يمكث به مقدار ركن لا تبطل به وإن مكث قدره بطلت على المختار (و) منها طهارة موضع اليدين والركبتين على الصحيح لافتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم واختاره الفقيه أبو الليث، وأنكر ما قيل من عدم افتراض طهارة موضعها ولأن رواية جواز مع نجاسة موضع الكفين والركبتين شاذة (و) منها طهارة موضع الجبهة على الأصح من الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وهو قولهما رحمهم الله ليتحقق السجود عليها لأن
الصلاة
قوله: (أو بجمعه) معطوف على محذوف معلوم من المقام تقديره بنجس مانع بإنفراده تحت أحدهما. قوله : ( تقديراً) أي بالحرز والظن قوله لا تبطل به الصلاة لأن المكث اليسير على النجس القليل كالمكث الكثير مع النجس القليل معفو عنه، وحكم الانكشاف مع الزمن كحكم المكث مع النجس أفاده الشرح . قوله : (وإن مكث قدره) أي وإن لم يؤده. قوله : (على المختار) هو قول أبي يوسف، وقال محمد : لا تفسد إلا إذا أداه بالفعل. قوله : (على الصحيح) صححه الحلبي، وصاحب العيون. قوله : (الإفتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم) ظاهره أنه إذا لم يضع اليدين أو الركبتين أو إحداهما (۱) أن تكون الصلاة فاسدة وليس كذلك، بل العلة في الفساد أن وضع العضو على النجاسة بمنزلة حملها، فيفسد وإن كان الموضع غير فرض قال في الخانية : إذا كانت النجاسة في موضع السجود، أو الركبتين، أو اليدين فإنها تجمع، وتمنع ولا يجعل كأنه لم يضع ذلك العضو بخلاف ما لو صلى رافعاً إحدى قدميه فإنه يجوز، ولو وضع القدم على نجاسة لا يجوز، ولا يجعل كأنه لم يضع اهـ. قال الكمال : وهذا يفيد أنّ عدم إشتراط طهارة مكان اليدين والركبتين محله إذا لم يضعهما أما إذا وضعهما، أو وضع إحداهما اشترطت فليحفظ اهـ . قال الحلبي : فعلم أنه لا فرق بين الركبتين واليدين، وبين موضع السجود، والقدمين في أنّ النجاسة المانعة في مواضعها مفسدة للصلاة، وهو الصحيح لأن إتصال العضو بالنجاسة بمنزلة حملها، وإن كان وضع ذلك العضو ليس بفرض اهـ، هذه النقول تدل على أن وضعها ليس فرضاً، ولكنها إذا وضعت إشترطت طهارة مواضعها، فليتأمل. بقي الكلام فيما إذا وضع ما يكره وضعه كالذراعين هل يفترض طهارة موضعهما الظاهر نعم لأنه بوضعهما على النجاسة يعد حاملاً لها قوله: (واختاره الفقيه أبو الليث) الذي ذكره بعد في هذا الباب أنّ الذي إختاره الفقيه وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف القدمين فليتأمل قوله : (وأنكر ما قيل) لا يلزم من إنكاره ذلك قوله بإفتراض وضعها. قوله (شاذة) ذكر ذلك صاحب العيون، وهذا لا ينافي إن وضعهما غير واجب أي غير فرض في ظاهر الرواية كما ذكره صاحب البحر .
(1) قوله أن تكون الخ لعل الأولى حذف أن تأمل؟ مصححه .

للصلاة
الفرض، وإن كان يتأدى بمقدار الأرنبة على القول المرجوح يصير الوضع معدوماً حكماً بوجوده على النجس ولو أعاده على طاهر في ظاهر الرواية ولا يمنع نجاسة في محل أنفه مع طهارة باقي المحال بالاتفاق لأن الأنف أقل من الدرهم ويصير كأنه اقتصر على الجبهة مع الكراهة، وطهارة المكان ألزم من الثوب المشروط نصاً بالدلالة إذ لا وجود بدون مكان، وقد توجد بدون ثوب، ولا يضر وقوع ثوبه على نجاسة لا تعلق به حال ده (و) منها (ستر العورة) للإجماع على افتراضه ولو في ظلمة والشرط سترها من جوانبه على الصحيح ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه في قول عامة المشايخ (و) لا يضر لو
سجوده

Book of Prayer. Page 209. ... pure from impurity and if it does not remain for the duration of a rukn, prayer is not invalidated; if it remains for that duration, it is invalidated according to the chosen view. And among them (conditions): purity of the place of the hands and knees according to the correct view, because prostration is prescribed on seven limbs; and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose it, and he rejected what was said about the non-obligation of purity of their place, and because the narration permitting impurity on the place of the palms and knees is anomalous. And among them: purity of the place of the forehead according to the more sound of the two narrations from Abu Hanifah, and it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), may Allah have mercy on them, so that prostration is realized upon it, because... (continues with commentary). ... And among them: covering the private parts (awrah) due to consensus on its obligation even in darkness, and the condition is to cover it from its sides according to the correct view, and it does not harm if one sees it from his collar according to the general body of scholars.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah, explaining several conditions of prayer. The author discusses three key conditions: purity of the place of hands and knees, purity of the place of the forehead, and covering the awrah. For hands and knees, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that purity is required, and if one places these limbs on impurity for the duration of a rukn, the prayer is invalidated. This is based on the principle that contact with impurity is equivalent to carrying it. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf (al-mukhtar), invalidation occurs even if the limb remains without active movement, while Muhammad requires actual performance of the rukn on impurity. For the forehead, purity is required even on the weaker opinion that placing the forehead is not fard, because contact with impurity is still like carrying it. The author clarifies that even if a limb's placement is not obligatory, once it is placed, purity becomes necessary. Covering the awrah is obligatory by consensus, and it suffices even with water, leaves, or mud; darkness does not exempt. The commentary also notes that purity of the place is more emphatically required than purity of the garment, as the place is unavoidable.

Key Terms
طهارة المكان (taharat al-makan): The condition that the place where the worshipper prays, specifically the spot where the forehead, hands, and knees touch, be free from physical impurity (najis).
ستر العورة (satr al-awrah): The obligation to cover the private parts of the body during prayer, which is established by consensus (ijma).
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred ruling among conflicting opinions within the Hanafi school, often indicating the mufta bihi (operative view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (al-mukhtar) in the Hanafi school, what invalidates prayer regarding impurity on the hands and knees?
A) Only if the impurity is visible.
B) If the hands or knees remain on impurity for the duration of a rukn.
C) Only if the hands are placed on impurity, not knees.
D) It never invalidates because placement is not fard.

Key Takeaway
Purity of the place of prostration is required for all seven limbs; contact with impurity invalidates prayer even if the limb's placement is not obligatory.

Salah — Prayer

Facing the Qibla: Obligation and Practical Determination
Commentary on the condition of qibla in prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla for both the mushahid (one who sees the Ka'bah) and the gha'ib (absent person), and apply the tarjih regarding intention of the qibla.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is fard; for the mushahid it is exact, for the gha'ib direction suffices.

Facing the qibla is one of the essential conditions (shurut) for the validity of prayer. This lesson clarifies its definition, the evidence for its obligation, and the important distinction between someone who sees the Ka'bah directly and someone who does not. We also examine a notable intra-Hanafi dispute: is the absent person required to intend the exact spot? The correct (sahih) position is that the direction is sufficient, making the prayer valid without a specific intention of the 'ayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text defines facing the qibla as a condition (shart) for prayer. Determine that it is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) based on consensus (ijma).
The Quranic verse (2:144) and hadith are cited as primary proofs.
2
Distinguish between mushahid and gha'ib
For a person in Mecca who sees the Ka'bah (mushahid), the obligation is to face its exact spot (ayn). For everyone else (gha'ib), the direction (jihah) is sufficient. This is a concession (tawsi'ah) from Shari'ah.
The direction is determined by ijtihad, not by exact astronomical alignment.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Jurjani held that even the gha'ib must intend the exact spot of the Ka'bah. However, the majority (al-ammah) and the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that intention of the exact spot is not required; facing the direction suffices.
Al-Tahtawi declares the majority view as 'al-sahih' (the correct one).
4
Apply the tarjih
Understand that the mufta bihi position does not require niyyah (intention) of the qibla as a separate condition. The condition is actual facing, not the act of seeking it.
This is based on the principle that means (wasā'il) do not require separate intention.
5
Determine qibla in practice
In cities and towns, rely on established mihrabs set by the Companions and Followers. If no mihrab is available, ask a trustworthy local (even if sinful, if truthful).
Ijtihad is permissible when no authority is present.

Source Text

(And from them is) facing the qibla. 'Istiqbal' is from 'qabaltu' meaning I faced, and the 'sin' and 'ta' are not for seeking because the condition is facing. Language. His statement: (Due to consensus on its obligation) meaning in prayer. ... His statement: (Facing the qibla) with kasrah on the qaf, linguistically absolute direction. Al-Jawhari said: one says 'from where is your qibla?' i.e., your direction, and 'what is the qibla of his speech?' i.e., direction. Legally, as in al-Qahistani, it is the direction towards which the people of the seven earths to the seven heavens pray, facing the Ka'bah i.e., its direction. This name has become predominant for this direction until it became a proper noun, and it is called 'mihrab' because facing it fights the soul and shaytan. At the beginning of Islam it was towards Bayt al-Maqdis, but the Prophet in Mecca did not face the Ka'bah directly but placed it between him and Bayt al-Maqdis as corrected. ... His statement: (For the Meccan who sees the Ka'bah, his obligation is to hit its very spot. (For other than the seer, the obligation is) hitting its direction. So the west is the qibla for the people of the east, and vice versa, and the south is the qibla for the people of the north. Thus the direction is like the exact spot, as a concession for people. ... His statement: (This is the correct view). Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani said the obligation is hitting the exact spot for the absent person as well through ijtihad, because there is no differentiation in the text. ... His statement: (Intention of qibla is not a condition) because it is a means, and means do not require intention like wudu; the condition is its occurrence, not its seeking. ... They said: its direction is known by evidence; the evidence in cities and villages are the mihrabs set up by the Companions and Followers, so we must follow them in facing those set mihrabs; if not, then ask the locals, even one who is sinful, if he tells the truth.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of facing the qibla in prayer. It defines 'qibla' linguistically and legally. Legally, it is the direction of the Ka'bah from any point on earth. The passage notes that initially the qibla was towards Jerusalem, but later changed to the Ka'bah. For a person in Mecca who sees the Ka'bah, it is obligatory to face it exactly. For others, it suffices to face its direction, determined by ijtihad or by following established mihrabs. There is a difference of opinion: some, like al-Jurjani, hold that even the absent person must face the exact spot via intention, but the correct (sahih) view is that the direction is sufficient. Intention of the qibla is not a condition because it is a means; what matters is actually facing it. The passage also addresses how to determine the qibla: by mihrabs set by reliable authorities, or by asking locals. This reflects the Hanafi position that obligation varies with ability.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qibla): The condition of facing the direction of the Ka'bah during prayer; for those who see the Ka'bah, it requires exact alignment; for others, the general direction suffices.
جهة القبلة (jihah al-qibla): The direction of the Ka'bah; a concession for those far away, so they are not required to face the exact spot.
مشاهد (mushahid): One who sees the Ka'bah with his own eyes; must face its exact spot.
غائب (gha'ib): One who does not see the Ka'bah; only required to face its direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person who is far from Mecca and does not see the Ka'bah?
A) He must face the exact spot of the Ka'bah by intention.
B) He must face the general direction of the Ka'bah.
C) He does not need to face any direction if he is ignorant.
D) He must face a mihrab in any mosque.

Key Takeaway
For the gha'ib (absent), facing the general direction of the Ka'bah (jihah) is sufficient and intention of the exact spot is not required.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Facing the Qibla for Those Who See and Do Not See the Ka'ba
States the ruling on qibla with definition of exact vs. directional facing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qibla obligation for those who see and do not see the Ka'ba, and distinguish between facing the exact location ('ayn) and facing the direction (jiha).

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is wajib: exact for those who see the Ka'ba, directional for those who don't.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the obligation to face the qibla differs depending on whether you can see the Ka'ba or not. Understanding this distinction resolves common confusion about the requirement of exactness and ensures the validity of prayer for millions of Muslims worldwide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Facing the qibla is a condition (shart) for prayer, wajib by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. The intended reference is the ground of the Ka'ba, not the building itself.
2
Distinguish between witness and non-witness
For the Meccan who sees the Ka'ba (mushahid), the obligation is to face the exact 'ayn (location) because certainty is possible. For others (ghayr mushahid), including those in Mecca obstructed by a building, the obligation is to face the direction (jiha).
This distinction is based on ability: certainty vs. probability.
3
Define 'jiha' (direction)
Direction means being aligned exactly (tahqiq) or approximately (taqrib) with the Ka'ba or its airspace. Approximate alignment is valid as long as some part of the face remains facing the Ka'ba.
Approximate facing is not a complete deviation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some early Hanafis (e.g., Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani) held that the non-witness must also face the 'ayn through ijtihad. However, the correct (sahih) position, as stated by Al-Tahtawi, is that direction suffices.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text

لا طلبها، وهو شرط بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، والمراد منها بقعتها لا البناء حتى لو نوى بناء الكعبة لا يجوز إلا أن يريد به جهة الكعبة وإن نوى المحراب لا يجوز (فللمكي المشاهد) للكعبة فرضه إصابة عينها اتفاقاً لقدرته عليه يقيناً (و) الفرض (لغير المشاهد) إصابة (جهتها) أي الكعبة هو الصحيح ونية القبلة ليست بشرط والتوجه إليها يغنيه عن النية هو الأصح وجهتها هي التي إذا توجه إليها الإنسان يكون مسامتاً للكعبة، أو لهوائها تحقيقاً، أو تقريباً ومعنى التحقيق أنه لو فرض خط من تلقاء وجهه على زاوية قائمة إلى الأفق يكون ماراً على الكعبة أو هوائها ومعنى التقريب أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية بأن يبقى شيء من سطح الوجه مسامتاً لها أو لهوائها ولغير المشاهد إصابة جهتها البعيد والقريب سواء (ولو) بمكة) وحال بينه وبين الكعبة بناء أو غيره
It does not require seeking it (i.e., the qibla), and it is a condition by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. The intended meaning is its ground (the location of the Ka'ba), not the building, so if one intends the building of the Ka'ba, it is not permissible unless he intends thereby the direction of the Ka'ba. And if he intends the prayer niche (mihrab), it is not permissible. For the Meccan who sees the Ka'ba, his obligation is to hit its exact location ('ayn) by agreement, because he is able to do so with certainty. And the obligation for the one who does not see it (non-witness) is to hit its direction (jiha), i.e., of the Ka'ba; that is the correct position. Intention of the qibla is not a condition, and facing it suffices him from intending, that is the most correct view. Its direction is that towards which if a person faces, he will be aligned exactly or approximately with the Ka'ba or its airspace. The meaning of exact alignment is that if a line is imagined from in front of his face at a right angle to the horizon, it would pass over the Ka'ba or its airspace. The meaning of approximate alignment is that the line deviates from the Ka'ba or its airspace in such a deviation that the alignment is not completely negated, such that some part of the surface of his face remains aligned with it or its airspace. And for the non-witness, hitting its direction is sufficient, whether far or near, and even if he is in Mecca and a building or something else intervenes between him and the Ka'ba.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi explains the ruling on facing the qibla in prayer. The author begins by stating that facing the qibla is a condition for prayer, established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. He clarifies that what is meant is facing the ground of the Ka'ba, not the building itself; thus, intending the building (as an object) is invalid unless it is taken as the direction. Similarly, intending the prayer niche (mihrab) is not sufficient in itself. Then he distinguishes two cases: for someone in Mecca who can see the Ka'ba, the obligation is to face the exact 'ayn (location) of the Ka'ba, because they can be certain. For anyone else (non-witness, including those in Mecca obstructed by a building), the obligation is to face the direction (jiha) of the Ka'ba. This is the correct Hanafi position. The text notes that intending the qibla is not a separate condition; the actual act of facing suffices. The definition of 'direction' is then given: it means being aligned exactly (muhadha) with the Ka'ba or its airspace, or approximately aligned such that some part of the face still faces it. For non-witnesses, facing the direction is sufficient whether they are near or far, even if inside Mecca but with an obstruction. This is a critical refinement over the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, providing detailed legal definitions.

Key Terms
العين (al-'ayn): The exact location of the Ka'ba itself, as opposed to its direction.
الجهة (al-jiha): The direction of the Ka'ba, which for non-witnesses is sufficient for prayer validity.
المقابلة (al-muqabala): Facing or alignment with the qibla; it can be exact (tahqiq) or approximate (taqrib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct interpretation of 'shatra' (شطر) in Quran 2:144 according to the Hanafi school?
A) It requires facing the exact building of the Ka'ba for everyone.
B) It indicates direction (jiha), which for non-witnesses does not require exact 'ayn.
C) It requires facing the mihrab of the mosque.
D) It is abrogated by later verses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires exact facing only for those who can see the Ka'ba; for all others, facing the direction is sufficient, based on the Quranic word 'shatra' and the principle of capability.

Methods for Determining the Qibla Direction
Explains practical methods to determine qibla using mihrabs, locals, stars, and sun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for determining qibla direction using mihrabs, celestial signs, and practical marking, and identify the authoritative evidence (dalil) for each method.

Core Idea
For the qibla, follow the upright mihrabs of the Salaf, or ask a trustworthy local; if that fails, use stars or the sun with predefined bearings.

Determining the qibla is wajib for the validity of prayer. The Hanafi school provides multiple reliable methods, from following established mihrabs to using celestial navigation and practical marking techniques. This lesson walks through the evidence and step-by-step techniques as expanded by al-Tahtawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy of evidence
Note that the text first mentions the primary evidence for inhabited areas: mihrabs erected by the Sahaba and Tabi'un. If none, then asking trustworthy locals. For wilderness, the evidence is the stars.
This hierarchy shows the priority: tradition and community over individual guesswork.
2
Examine the hadith from 'Umar (r.a.)
The text cites the narration 'Learn from the stars that which you may guide yourselves to the qibla.' Understand its thubut (zanni) and dalala (zanni) and why it is used as a recommendation.
The command is interpreted as permissibility and recommendation, not obligation.
3
Apply the body-marker method
The text describes using the sun or stars at fixed times relative to a known mihrab. You must mark the sun's position on your body (e.g., eye, back) at sunrise, noon, and sunset, then replicate in a new location.
This method preserves the bearing without instruments.
4
Analyze the definitions of musamata (alignment)
The passage distinguishes exact alignment (muhadha) with the Ka'ba or its airspace from approximate alignment (taqrib) where some part of the face still faces the qibla. Understand when each applies.
Hanafis accept approximate alignment as sufficient.
5
Recognize regional variations for the Pole Star
The text gives specific placements of the Pole Star relative to the body for different regions: behind right ear for Iraq, left shoulder for Egypt, etc. This shows the qibla direction varies by geography.
These instructions are based on traditional astronomical knowledge.

Source Text

وقت الأستواء، ووقت الغروب، فإذا أراد القبلة بعد سفره، أو في بيته فليجعل الشمس في ذلك الوقت قبالة المحل المخصوص يكن مستقبلاً، فإن جعل له خطاً في الأرض أو كوة في حائط، فهو قبلته ما دام في ذلك المكان وكذلك يفعل بالنجوم وغيرها في وقت معين كوقت العشاء، ويختص بإقليم مصر إذا وقف ليلاً مستقبل الجدي ضاماً رجليه وحرك رجله اليمني إلى جهة يمينه بقدر طاقته، ثم نفل الأخرى إليها كان مستقبلاً، وكذا لو فعل ذلك بعد وقوفه على خط نصف النهار بأن يجعل المشرق عن يمينه والمغرب عن يساره ويستقبل ظله وقت الإستواء، ثم يحرك رجله اليمني كذلك يكون مستقبلاً أيضاً. قوله: (يكون مسامتاً) أي محاذياً قوله (للكعبة أو لهوائها هذا إذا وقعت المحاذاة على العين، وقوله : للكعبة أي فيما إذا كان في محل يساوي المحل الذي به القبلة، وقوله : أو لهوائها هو فيما إذا كان محله أعلى من محلها، ومثله ما إذا كان أسفل، وقوله : أو تقريباً، إذا هكذا في النسخ وفيه حذف نون الرفع من غير ناصب ولا جازم وهو لغة قللة كما لا يخفي كتبه مصححه .
As for its direction, they said: its direction is known by evidence. The evidence in cities and villages is the mihrabs that the Sahaba and Tabi'un erected; thus upon us is to follow them in facing those erected mihrabs. If there are none, then asking the residents, i.e., the people of that locality, even if one is a sinner, if one trusts him. As for seas and deserts, the evidence for the qibla is the stars. It has been narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Learn from the stars that which you may guide yourselves to the qibla.' That is like the Pole Star (al-Qutb), a small star in the Little Dipper (Banat Na'sh al-Sughra), between al-Farqadan and al-Jady. If the person standing places it behind his right ear, he will be facing the qibla if he is in the region of Kufa, Baghdad, Hamadan, Qazwin, Tabaristan, Jurjan, and what adjoins them up to the River of Syria. One in Egypt places it on his left shoulder, and one in Iraq on his right shoulder, and he will be facing the door of the Ka'ba. One in Yemen faces opposite the one facing, adjacent to his left side, and one in Syria behind him. It is recommended for one who is ignorant of the proofs of the qibla and wants to travel, for example, to lands where the qibla does not differ, and he has no one knowledgeable with him, or he wants to set a qibla in his house for example, that he should face a correct mihrab from the mihrabs of his town at a fixed time, like sunrise for example, and mark the sun at that time on a part of his body, like his eye or his back. Then he does likewise at the time of noon (istiwa') and at sunset. Then when he wants the qibla after his travel or in his house, he places the sun at that time opposite that specific part, and he will be facing. If he marks a line on the ground or a niche in the wall, that will be his qibla as long as he is in that place. Similarly, he does with stars and other things at a fixed time like the time of 'Isha. And it is specific to the region of Egypt: if he stands at night facing al-Jady, pressing his legs together, and moves his right foot to his right side as much as he can, then moves the other foot to it, he will be facing. Similarly, if he does that after standing on the meridian line, making the east to his right and the west to his left, and faces his shadow at the time of noon (istiwa'), then moves his right foot likewise, he will also be facing. His saying: (is aligned) i.e., in line with. His saying: (with the Ka'ba or its airspace) this is when alignment falls on the 'ayn. His saying: (with the Ka'ba) i.e., when he is at a level equal to the place of the qibla. His saying: (or its airspace) is when his place is higher than its place, and similarly when lower. His saying: (or approximately) when alignment falls on the direction, for the one facing the direction, his facing may wholly fall on the 'ayn or not, and he has mentioned the two possible types. His saying: (such that some part of the surface of the face remains) even if that is a small part, and this is its form. (Footnote: His saying 'ma tahhtadu' (what you guide) is like this in the manuscripts; it has the omission of the nun of the indicative mood without a nassib or jazim, and it is a rare dialect.)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi expands on the means to determine the qibla direction for prayer. The author explains that the direction is known through evidence (dalil). In settled areas (cities and villages), the primary evidence is the mihrabs (prayer niches) that the companions and their successors erected in mosques; these are reliable and must be followed. If no mihrab exists, one should ask the trustworthy locals, even if they are sinners, as long as their information is believed. In seas and deserts, the evidence is the stars, specifically the Pole Star (al-Qutb). The author cites a tradition from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab encouraging learning star positions for qibla guidance. Detailed instructions are given for different regions: for example, someone in Iraq places the Pole Star behind his right ear, someone in Egypt on his left shoulder, etc. For those ignorant of celestial signs, practical methods are provided: before a journey, one can mark the position of the sun relative to a known correct mihrab at specific times (sunrise, noon, sunset). Later, in a new location, by placing the sun at the same bearing relative to his body, he can determine the qibla. Similar methods using stars (e.g., at 'Isha time) and shadow at noon (for Egypt) are described. The passage concludes by clarifying the definitions of alignment (musamat): exact alignment (muhadha) with the Ka'ba or its airspace, and approximate alignment (taqrib) when some part of the face still faces it. This is an expansion of the matn, providing practical guidance for the common person.

Key Terms
المحاريب (al-maharib): Prayer niches in mosques that indicate the qibla direction, traditionally aligned by the Sahaba and Tabi'un.
القطب (al-qutb): The Pole Star, used as a navigational star for determining the qibla in the northern hemisphere.
المسامتة (al-musamata): Alignment with the qibla, either exactly (tahqiq) or approximately (taqrib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Exact and Approximate Facing of the Qibla
Definition of haqiqatan and taqriban facing with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define haqiqatan and taqriban facing of the qibla and determine the validity of a worshiper's alignment in prayer.

Core Idea
Approximate facing is valid as long as some part of the face remains aligned with the Kaaba or its airspace.

In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi legal definition of facing the qibla. The passage distinguishes between exact (haqiqatan) and approximate (taqriban) facing, with commentary clarifying the role of elevation and alignment of the face's surface. Understanding this distinction is essential for validating one's prayer posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Locate the terms haqiqatan and taqriban in the Arabic text. Note that the author first defines exact facing as a line from the face passing over the Kaaba or its airspace, then defines approximate facing as a deviation that does not completely negate alignment.
Look for the phrases: 'أن يكون ماراً على الكعبة أو هوائها' and 'أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة ... انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية'.
2
Understand the role of airspace (hawa')
The commentator explains that mention of 'airspace' applies when the worshiper is not at the same elevation as the Kaaba. If higher or lower, alignment is with the airspace above or below the Kaaba.
See: 'قوله : أو لهوائها هو فيما إذا كان محله أعلى من محلها، ومثله ما إذا كان أسفل'.
3
Define the minimum requirement for approximate facing
The text states that approximate facing requires at least some part of the surface of the face to be opposite the Kaaba or its airspace. Even a small portion suffices.
Key phrase: 'بأن يبقى شيء من سطح الوجه'.
4
Apply the ruling for one who does not see the Kaaba
For a worshiper who is not in direct sight of the Kaaba (ghair mushahid), distant and near are equal; both must face the direction. Even in Mecca, if a building or mountain blocks the view, the ruling is like that of an absent person, requiring taharr (effort to determine direction).
See: 'ولغير المشاهد إصابة جهتها البعيد والقريب سواء' and 'وحال بينه وبين الكعبة بناء أو جبل على الصحيح'.
5
Identify the corrupting deviation
The passage quotes al-Fatawa that a deviation that moves the face from the east to the west is invalidating (mufsid). This sets the outer limit of permissible deviation.
Phrase: 'الإنحراف المفسد أن يجاوز المشارق إلى المغارب'.
