أو تقريباً ومعنى التحقيق أنه لو فرض خط من تلقاء وجهه على زاوية قائمة إلى الأفق يكون ماراً على الكعبة أو هوائها ومعنى التقريب أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية بأن يبقى شيء من سطح الوجه مسامتاً لها أو لهوائها ولغير المشاهد إصابة جهتها البعيد والقريب سواء (ولو) بمكة) وحال بينه وبين الكعبة بناء أو جبل على الصحيح) كما في الدراية والتجنيس (و) من الشروط (الوقت) للفرائض الخمس مستقبل الكعبة المشرفة مستقبل مستقبل هذا مسامت لها أو هذا مسامت للكعبة هذا مسامت للكعبة لهوائها تقريباً أو لهوائها تحقيقاً أو لهوائها تقريباً وبعض دائرة الوجه وبعض الدائرة يصيب عين الكعبة يصيب عين الكعبة . يمنع وفي الفتاوي الإنحراف المفسد أن يجاوز المشارق إلى المغارب اهـ. قوله: (يكون مسامتاً) أي محاذياً قوله (للكعبة أو لهوائها هذا إذا وقعت المحاذاة على العين، وقوله : للكعبة أي فيما إذا كان في محل يساوي المحل الذي به القبلة، وقوله : أو لهوائها هو فيما إذا كان محله أعلى من محلها، ومثله ما إذا كان أسفل، وقوله : أو تقريباً، إذا وقعت المحاذاة للجهة فإنّ مستقبل الجهة يحتمل أن يقع إستقباله بتمامه على العين، أولا وقد بين النوعين المحتملين. قوله : بأن يبقى شيء من سطح الوجه، ولو كان ذلك جزاً يسيراً، وهذه صورته

(1) قوله ما تهتدوا هكذا في النسخ وفيه حذف نون الرفع من غير ناصب ولا جازم وهو لغة قللة كما لا يخفي كتبه مصححه .
Or approximately, and the meaning of exact (tahqiq) is that if a line is assumed from opposite his face at a right angle to the horizon, it would pass over the Kaaba or its airspace. The meaning of approximate (taqrib) is that it deviates from the Kaaba or its airspace in a deviation that does not completely remove the facing, such that something of the surface of the face remains aligned with it or its airspace. For one who does not see (the Kaaba), hitting its direction, the distant and the near are equal (even in Mecca) and if there is a building or mountain between him and the Kaaba, the correct view (is that his ruling is like the absent). As in al-Diraya and al-Tajnis. And among the conditions (is the time) for the five prayers. Facing the noble Kaaba, facing, facing: this is aligned with it or its airspace approximately, or its airspace exactly, or its airspace approximately. And part of the face's circle and part of the circle hits the eye of the Kaaba, hits the eye of the Kaaba. It prevents. And in al-Fatawa, the corrupting deviation is to exceed the east to the west, end. His saying: (is aligned) i.e., opposite. His saying: (to the Kaaba or its airspace) this is when the alignment occurs on the eye. His saying: (to the Kaaba) i.e., when he is in a place equal to the place where the qibla is. His saying: (or its airspace) is when his place is higher than its place, and similarly if it is lower. His saying: (or approximately) is when the alignment is to the direction, for the one facing the direction may possibly have his facing entirely on the eye or not, and he has explained the two possibilities. His saying: (that something of the surface of the face remains) even if that part is small. And this is its diagram. (1) His saying: 'ma tahatadu' is like this in the manuscripts, and in it the nun of the indicative mood is omitted without a nasiKh or jazim, and it is a rare dialect as is not hidden, written by its corrector.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a definition with commentary on the legal concept of facing the qibla in prayer. The author distinguishes between exact facing (haqiqatan) and approximate facing (taqriban). Exact facing means that a line extending straight from the worshiper's face at a right angle to the horizon would pass directly over the Kaaba itself or its airspace above it. Approximate facing means that the line deviates from the Kaaba but not so much that the worshiper is no longer considered facing it at all; as long as some part of the face is still aligned with the Kaaba or its airspace, the facing is valid. The commentator explains that the wording 'aligned with the Kaaba' applies when the worshiper is at the same level as the Kaaba, while 'aligned with its airspace' applies when the worshiper is higher or lower. The requirement for one who does not see the Kaaba (ghair mushahid) is to face its direction; both the distant and the near are equal in this, and even in Mecca if a building or mountain blocks the view, the ruling is like that of an absent person (ghaib), meaning he may exert effort (taharr) to determine the direction. The commentary then clarifies that the alignment considered is of the surface of the face, not just a point. The diagrams attempt to illustrate the two types of facing. A textual note points out a rare grammatical form in a hadith about stars.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Exact facing: a line from the face passes directly over the Kaaba or its airspace.
تقريب (taqrib): Approximate facing: deviation from the Kaaba but not enough to negate facing; some part of the face remains aligned.
مسامتة (musamat): Alignment: the condition where the worshiper's face is directly opposite the Kaaba or its airspace, even if only partially.
هواء الكعبة (hawa' al-Ka'bah): The airspace above the Kaaba: used for facing when the worshiper is at a higher or lower elevation than the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The worshiper faces exactly towards the Kaaba.
B) The worshiper faces any direction that is generally known as qibla.
C) The worshiper deviates from the Kaaba but some part of the face remains aligned with it or its airspace.
D) The worshiper prays without determining the qibla and it is accepted.

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla is wajib; the Hanafi school accepts approximate facing as long as some part of the face aligns with the Kaaba or its airspace.

Invalidating Deviation from Qibla
Ruling defining what constitutes invalidating deviation from qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define invalidating deviation (al-inhiraf al-mufsid) according to the Hanafi school and apply it to determine when prayer becomes batil.

Core Idea
Turning beyond the east-west arc invalidates prayer; slight deviations do not.

Many worshippers worry about facing the exact qibla. This concise ruling from the later Hanafi fatwa collections clarifies the threshold: only a complete turn from the general direction of east to west invalidates the prayer. Understanding this prevents unnecessary doubt and ensures valid salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its authority
Note that this ruling is from al-Fatawa, a later collection, not the primary Zahir al-Riwayah texts. The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin, meaning it is the operative position for fatwa.
Later collections often refine earlier rulings.
2
Understand the geographic arc
The text defines the arc between the points of sunrise (mashariq) and sunset (magharib). In the Hanafi view, the qibla in a given region is within a wide arc between east and west. Deviation means turning so far that one exits that arc entirely.
This arc is not a precise degree; it is a general orientation.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Imagine a prayer in a mosque that is not exactly qibla-aligned. If the worshipper turns such that he faces away from the general east-west corridor, his prayer becomes invalid. A slight turn to adjust does not exit the arc.
The key is exiting the arc, not missing the exact line.
4
Contrast with other schools
Other madhhabs have stricter thresholds (e.g., some require facing exactly towards the Kaaba). The Hanafi position offers more flexibility, reflecting the principle of 'ma'ruf' (accepted custom) in determining direction.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; each school has its proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوي الإنحراف المفسد أن يجاوز المشارق إلى المغارب اهـ.
And in al-Fatawa: the invalidating deviation is that he exceeds the eastern [points] to the western [points].
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Fatawa collections clarifying the measure of deviation from the qibla that makes prayer invalid. 'Exceeding the easts to the wests' means turning so far that one faces away from the general arc between east and west, effectively turning his back to the qibla direction. This is considered an invalidating deviation.

Key Terms
الإنحراف المفسد (al-inhiraf al-mufsid): The deviation from qibla that invalidates the prayer, defined as exceeding from the direction of east to the direction of west.
المشارق والمغارب (al-mashariq wa al-magharib): The points of sunrise and sunset; used to define the acceptable arc for qibla direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Facing slightly away from the exact direction
B) Exceeding the east to the west arc
C) Turning 45 degrees to the left
D) Any deviation at all

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only a deviation that exits the wide east-west arc invalidates prayer; slight turns are permissible.

Ijtihad vs Certainty for Qibla in Mecca
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijtihad vs. certainty for qibla with natural obstacles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on ijtihad for qibla when certainty is attainable and explain the practical consequence (iʿādah) if the wrong direction is chosen.

Core Idea
If certainty is possible, ijtihad is invalid — certainty overrides probability.

When a person in Mecca is prevented from seeing the Kaaba by a natural obstacle like a mountain, should he rely on ijtihad to determine the qibla direction, or must he climb to achieve certainty? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the author of Maʿraj al-Dirāyah and al-Muḥaqqiq al-Kamāl, with the latter arguing that ijtihad is not sufficient when climbing is possible. The dispute hinges on the epistemological principle that certain knowledge (yaqīn) takes precedence over probable estimation (al-ẓann).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the distinction: a man-made barrier (building) vs. a natural barrier (mountain). For buildings, the person is treated as a gha'ib (absent) and must use ijtihad. For a mountain, the author of Maʿraj allows ijtihad but recommends climbing. Al-Muḥaqqiq al-Kamāl objects to ijtihad entirely when climbing is possible.
This distinction is based on whether the obstacle is removable or not.
2
Understand al-Muḥaqqiq al-Kamāl's argument
He argues that resorting to speculative evidence (dalīl ẓannī) while certain evidence (dalīl qaṭʿī) is available is impermissible. Therefore, the person must climb to achieve certainty; otherwise, if he prays and later discovers he was wrong, he must repeat the prayer.
The principle 'al-akhbār fawq al-taḥarrī' from al-Hidāyah is cited: textual evidence (which gives certainty) is above ijtihad.
3
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If the person does not climb and prays using ijtihad, according to the first view his prayer is valid but he has missed the better (afḍal). According to the second view, his prayer is invalid (he must repeat if he later learns he was wrong).
This directly affects the validity of the prayer performed with ijtihad when certainty was possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وحال بينه وبين الكعبة بناء، أو جبل قال في معراج الدراية ومن كان بمكة وبينه، وبين الكعبة حائل المشاهدة كأبنية، فالأصح أن حكمه حكم الغائب، ولو كان الحائل أصلياً كالجبل فله أن يجتهد والأولى أن يصعد على الجبل حتى تكون صلاته إلى الكعبة يقيناً اهـ قال المحقق الكمال: وعندي في جواز التحري مع إمكان صعوده أي صعود المكي الجبل إشكال لأن المصير إلى الدليل الظني، وترك القاطع مع إمكانه لا يجوز فلا يكفيه الإجتهاد حتى لو اجتهد، وصلى، ثم تبين خطوه فعليه الإعادة، وقد قال في الهداية الأخبار فوق التحري، فإذا امتنع المصير إلى الظني لا مكان ظني أقوى منه فكيف يترك اليقين مع إمكانه، ويكتفي بالظن.
He said: (And there is between him and the Kaaba an obstacle, a building or a mountain.) He said in Ma'raj al-Diraya: 'Whoever is in Mecca and between him and the Kaaba there is a visible barrier like buildings, then the correct view is that his ruling is the ruling of one who is absent. And if the barrier is natural like a mountain, then he may perform ijtihad, but it is better that he climb the mountain so that his prayer is definitely towards the Kaaba.' Al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal said: 'In my view, there is a problem in allowing ijtihad while climbing is possible, because resorting to a speculative evidence while abandoning certain evidence when possible is not permissible, so ijtihad is not sufficient for him. Even if he did ijtihad and prayed, then it became clear that he was mistaken, he must repeat. And it was said in al-Hidayah: "Hadith are above ijtihad." So if resorting to the speculative is prevented when a stronger speculative is possible, then how can certainty be abandoned when it is possible and be satisfied with probability?'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person in Mecca who cannot see the Kaaba due to an obstacle. The author of Ma'raj al-Diraya distinguishes between man-made obstacles (building) and natural obstacles (mountain). For a building, the person is like a traveler (gha'ib) and must perform ijtihad to determine the direction. For a mountain, ijtihad is allowed but climbing is better to achieve certainty. Al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal objects that if climbing is possible, ijtihad should not be allowed because certainty is possible. He bases this on the principle that one cannot abandon certainty for probability when certainty is accessible. He cites al-Hidayah stating that hadith are above ijtihad, meaning textual evidence (which gives certainty) takes precedence over personal reasoning. Therefore, he argues that the person must climb the mountain to be certain.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Ijtihad or estimation to determine the direction of qibla when one is uncertain.
الغائب (al-ghā'ib): A person who is absent from Mecca and cannot see the Kaaba, thus must use ijtihad for qibla.
الحائل الأصلي (al-ḥā'il al-aṣlī): A natural barrier (like a mountain) that is not man-made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal, what is the problem with allowing ijtihad for qibla when climbing a mountain is possible?
A) Climbing is too difficult
B) Ijtihad is only for travelers
C) Resorting to speculation while certainty is possible is not allowed
D) The mountain may collapse

Key Takeaway
When certainty is attainable, it must be sought; ijtihad (probability) cannot substitute it.

Time as a Condition for Prayer: Certainty and Doubt
Ruling with proof on the condition of time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the condition of time for prayer, explain why certainty of entry is required, and apply the consequence when doubt leads to incorrect belief.

Core Idea
Time is a condition for prayer; without decisive intention of its entry, the prayer is invalid even if the time had actually entered.

In this passage, the author affirms that time is a condition for the obligatory prayers, proven by the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. He notes a peculiarity: some authoritative Hanafi texts list the prayer times but do not include time among the conditions in the chapter on conditions. The passage then clarifies that one must be certain that the time has entered before praying, because the intention must be decisive. If someone prays believing the time has not entered, but it later becomes clear that it had, the prayer is invalid, because his mistaken belief was based on a valid legal basis (his ijtihad) and does not become valid retroactively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? What is the status of time? Time is a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer. Without it, the prayer is invalid.
The passage also notes that time functions as a cause (sabab), container (zarf), and condition for obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? He states 'By the Book, the Sunnah, and Ijma.' The Quranic evidence is 4:103, which says prayer is 'booked in times' (kitaban mawquta). The Sunnah includes the hadith of Jibril teaching the times.
The dalil is qati in both transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the requirement of certainty
What is the condition regarding intention? One must believe (i'tiqad) that the time has entered. This ensures the intention is decisive (jazim). The doubter is not decisive.
The text uses 'yaqin' style certainty, not just strong probability.
4
Apply the consequence of doubt
If someone prays while thinking the time has not entered, but it had entered, the prayer is invalid. Why? Because he judged his prayer to be corrupt based on a valid legal reasoning (his ijtihad or doubt). That judgment cannot be overturned by later revelation.
The person is also subject to fear for his religion, implying sin or disbelief if he thought it permissible to pray before time.
5
Note the omission in some texts
Why do some Hanafi works not list time as a condition in the chapter on conditions? The author does not know the secret, but time is still considered a condition. This is a subtle intra-madhhab observation.
The omission does not affect the ruling; it is a structural choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وقد نص على اشتراطه في عدة من المعتمدات، وقد ترك ذكر الوقت في باب شروط الصلاة في عدة من المعتمدات كالقدوري، والمختار والهداية والكنز مع بيانهم الأوقات، ولا أعلم سر عدم ذكرهم له، وإن كان يتصف بأنه سبب للأداء، وظرف للمؤدى وشرط للوجوب كما هو مقرر في محله (و) ويشترط (اعتقاد دخوله) لتكون عبادته بنية جازمة لأنّ الشاك ليس بجازم حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته بناه على دليل شرعي، وهو تحريه لا ينقلب جائزاً إذا ظهر خلافه، ويخاف عليه في دينه
By the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. And it is explicitly stated that it is a condition in several authoritative works. And they omitted mentioning the time in the chapter of conditions of prayer in several authoritative works like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz while they mentioned the times. And I do not know the secret of their not mentioning it, although it is described as a cause for performance, a container for what is performed, and a condition for obligation as established in its place. And it is required to believe in its entry so that his worship is with a decisive intention because the doubter is not decisive. Even if he prayed while thinking that the time had not entered, then it became clear that it had entered, it does not suffice him, because when he judged that his prayer was corrupt, he built that on a legal proof, and his ijtihad does not become permissible when the opposite appears, and he is feared for his religion.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage establishes that time is a condition (shart) for the obligatory prayers, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. The author notes that some Hanafi works (e.g., al-Quduri, al-Hidayah) did not list time as a condition in the chapter on conditions of prayer, but rather described the times separately. The author expresses puzzlement at this, as time functions as a cause (sabab) for the obligation, a container (zarf) for the act, and a condition for obligation. The passage then addresses the need to be certain ('i'tiqad dukhul) of the entry of time, because otherwise the intention is not decisive (jazim). If someone prays while under the impression that time has not entered, but it actually had, the prayer is not valid, because he built his judgment (that the prayer was invalid) on a valid legal basis (his ijtihad), and that judgment does not become permissible retroactively when the reality is opposite. Such a person is feared for his religion (i.e., he may fall into kufr if he thought it was permissible to pray before time).

Key Terms
اعتقاد دخوله (i'tiqad dukhulihi): Certain belief that the time for prayer has entered.
جازم (jazim): Decisive, certain, without doubt. The intention must be jazim for the prayer to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Time is a condition for prayer; without a decisive belief that the time has entered, the prayer is invalid even if the time later turns out to have been correct.

The Condition of Intention (Niyyah) in Prayer
Definition and ruling on the necessity of intention in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of intention in Hanafi fiqh and explain why it is a condition (shart) for prayer.

Core Idea
Intention is a decisive will that transforms a habit into worship.

Intention (niyyah) is the inner act that sets worship apart from ordinary actions. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of intention as 'decisive intention' (al-irada al-jāzima) and its role as a condition (shart) for prayer. Understanding this foundational concept clarifies why mere physical motions without resolve do not constitute valid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category of intention

2
Pinpoint the definitional elements

The text also mentions linguistic interpretation as 'determination' (ʿazm).
3
Understand the scope of intention
The commentary clarifies that intention covers actions of the limbs and the heart, including both performing and refraining from actions.
This shows niyyah is not limited to physical acts but includes internal resolve.
4
Apply the condition
Explain why intention is required: to differentiate worship (ʿibāda) from habit (ʿāda) and to ensure sincerity (ikhlāṣ) towards Allah.

This passage states that intention (niyyah) is a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer. It is defined as 'decisive intention' (al-irada al-jazima), which linguistically means determination ('azm). The purpose of intention is to distinguish an act of worship from a mere habit and to ensure sincerity (ikhlas). The hashiya elaborates: intention in the sharh is defined as the aim of obedience and seeking nearness to Allah in performing an action, covering both physical and heart actions, including both doing and refraining.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Decisive intention to perform an act of worship, aiming to obey Allah and seek nearness.

Time as a Condition for Obligatory Prayers
Critical commentary affirming time as condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for time as a condition (shart) for obligatory prayers and explain why its omission in some Hanafi texts does not negate its requirement.

Core Idea
Time is an essential condition for prayer, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, even if not always listed explicitly.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement by al-Tahtawi regarding the status of time (waqt) in the conditions of prayer. Although several authoritative Hanafi texts omit time from their formal lists of conditions, al-Tahtawi affirms that time is firmly established as a condition by the primary sources. Understanding this apparent discrepancy sharpens our ability to navigate between textual silence and operative legal principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal claim
What is al-Tahtawi's claim about time in relation to prayer? Identify the three roles he assigns to time: cause (sabab), container (zarf), and condition (shart).
2
Locate the evidence
He states that time is proven by 'the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.' Identify which specific Quranic verse and hadith are commonly cited for this ruling.
Refer to the dalil_block for guidance.
3
Analyze the omission
Al-Tahtawi notes that works like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz omit time from the conditions chapter. Why might this be? Consider that they do mention prayer times elsewhere, implying time is so fundamental it need not be repeated.
4
Understand the legal distinctions
Distinguish between the three functions of time: sabab (cause of obligation), zarf (temporal container), and shart (condition). How does each affect the ruling?
A shart must exist for validity; its absence invalidates. A sabab triggers obligation. A zarf is the time window.
5
Apply the ruling
Given that time is a condition, what is the ruling on a prayer performed before its time? Use the Hanafi framework to determine validity.
The prayer would be invalid (batil) because a condition is missing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وقد نص على اشتراطه في عدة من المعتمدات، وقد ترك ذكر الوقت في باب شروط الصلاة في عدة من المعتمدات كالقدوري، والمختار والهداية والكنز مع بيانهم الأوقات، ولا أعلم سر عدم ذكرهم له، وإن كان يتصف بأنه . سبب للأداء، وظرف للمؤدى وشرط للوجوب كما هو مقرر في محله
By the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. It has been explicitly made a condition in several reliable works, and the mention of time has been omitted in the chapter on conditions of prayer in several reliable works such as al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz, while they nonetheless mention the times. I do not know the reason for their omission, although it is characterized as being a cause for performance, a container for the performed act, and a condition for obligation, as established in its proper place.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) that establishes the condition of time (waqt) for obligatory prayers. The author begins by affirming that the requirement of time is proven by the three primary sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunnah, and scholarly consensus. He then notes a peculiarity: several authoritative Hanafi works—including al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz—do not explicitly list time as a condition in the chapter on the conditions of prayer, even though they do specify the prayer times. The author confesses ignorance of the reason for this omission, but explains that time functions in three ways regarding prayer: it is a cause that triggers obligation, a temporal container within which the prayer is performed, and a condition that must exist for the obligation to be binding. This follows the standard Hanafi legal framework where a condition (shart) is something whose absence prevents the ruling, but whose presence does not necessitate it. The omission in those texts may indicate reliance on the understanding that time is so fundamental it requires no mention, or that it is considered a condition of the obligation rather than the validity of the act.

Key Terms
وقت (waqt): The prescribed time period within which a prayer must be performed for its obligation to be valid.
شرط (shart): A condition that must exist for the prayer to be valid or obligatory; its absence invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Time is a condition (shart) for obligatory prayers, firmly established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, even if not always explicitly listed in every Hanafi text.

The Ruling on Doubt in Entry of Prayer Time
Requirement of belief in time entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling if a person prays while doubting the entry of time and later discovers it had entered.

Core Idea
Doubt in time entry invalidates prayer even if time genuinely entered.

The Hanafi school requires that the intention for prayer be decisive (jazm). This decisiveness is only possible if one has firm belief or at least dominant speculation that the time has entered. The text illustrates this with a scenario: if someone prays thinking the time has not entered, but it later becomes clear it had entered, the prayer is invalid. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Find the phrase 'اعتقاد دخوله' (belief in its entry) and note that it is required for the prayer to be valid.
2
Understand the rationale
The text says 'لتكون عبادته بنية جازمة' (so that his worship is with a decisive intention). The condition ensures the intention is decisive, because a doubter is not decisive.
Jazm (decisiveness) is key.
3
Analyze the example
The text gives an example: 'حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه' (if he prays while thinking the time had not entered, then it becomes clear it had, it is not sufficient). Note the ruling.
The subjective belief at the time matters, not objective reality.
4
Examine the reasoning
The text explains that he built his judgment on a legal proof (تحريه) and his speculation does not become permissible when the opposite appears.
This is based on the principle that acts are judged by intentions and dominant considerations.
5
Consider the severity
The text warns that it is feared for him in his religion (ويخاف عليه في دينه) because such negligence can lead to disbelief.
The gravity underscores the importance of certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) ويشترط (اعتقاد دخوله) لتكون عبادته بنية جازمة لأنّ الشاك ليس بجازم حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته بناه على دليل شرعي، وهو تحريه لا ينقلب جائزاً إذا ظهر خلافه، ويخاف عليه في دينه (و) قوله : (لتكون عبادته بنية جازمة) أفاد بذلك أن المراد بإعتقاد دخوله جزمه به لأنّ جزم النية إنما يكون به ولا يكفي غلبة الظن بالدخول، وينظر مع قولهم أن غلبة الظن في الفروع تقوم مقام اليقين، ويحتمل أن المراد بالإعتقاد، والجزم ما يعم غلبة الظن ويدل له التعليل بقولهم لأن الشاك الخ، فالمضر أحد شيئين إما إعتقاد عدم الدخول، وإما الشك. قوله : (حتى لو صلى الخ) هذا أولى بالحكم مما فرع عليه لأنه جزم بعدم الدخول، وهو أولى بالمنع من التردد بين الدخول، وعدمه. قوله: (لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته الخ) نظيره من صلى في ثوب وعنده أنه نجس، فإذا هو طاهر فإنه لا تصح صلاته لما ذكر، وهذا التعليل إنما يظهر فيمن عرف الحكم أما لو كان عنده أنه يظهر اللهم إلا أن يقال إنّ هذا الإعتقاد فاسد بمنزلة العدم، فينزل شرعاً في هذا الحكم منزلة العارف، فتفسد به صلاته زجراً له .بتقصيره قوله : ويخاف عليه في دينه) أي يخشى عليه الوقوع في الكفر أما إذا اعتقد حل ذلك فالأمر ظاهر، وإن اعتقد حرمته فيجره ذلك إلى غيره من وضع الأشياء في غير موضعها كالصلاة بالنجاسة، وإلى غير القبلة، وقد وقع خلاف في كفر من فعل ذلك
And it is required (belief in its entry) so that his worship is with a decisive intention, because the doubter is not decisive. So if he prays while thinking the time had not entered, then it becomes clear that it had entered, it is not sufficient for him, because when he judged his prayer invalid, he built that on a legal proof, and his speculation does not become permissible when the opposite appears. And it is feared for him in his religion. And his saying: 'so that his worship is with a decisive intention' indicates that what is meant by belief in its entry is certainty of it, because decisiveness of intention is only through it, and mere dominant speculation is not sufficient. And it is considered alongside their saying that dominant speculation in subsidiary matters stands in place of certainty. It is possible that what is meant by belief and decisiveness includes dominant speculation, and the evidence for that is their reasoning: 'because the doubter...' So what is harmful is one of two: either the belief that it has not entered, or doubt. His saying: 'so if he prays...' This is more deserving of the ruling than what he derived from it, because he was certain of non-entry, and that is more deserving of prohibition than hesitation between entry and non-entry. His saying: 'because when he judged his prayer invalid...' Its analogue is one who prays in a garment while he thinks it is najis, then it turns out to be pure, then his prayer is not valid for the reason mentioned. And this reasoning is only apparent one who knows the ruling. As for one who thinks it appears, unless it is said that this belief is corrupt and is like non-existence, so legally in this ruling he is treated as a knower, so his prayer is invalidated as a deterrent due to his negligence. His saying: 'and it is feared for him in his religion' means it is feared that he falls into disbelief. For if he believed it is permissible, the matter is clear. If he believed it is forbidden, it leads to other things like placing things in other than their proper places, such as praying with najasah or facing other than the qiblah. And there is disagreement regarding disbelief of one who does that.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement that addresses the condition of believing with certainty that the time for prayer has entered. The author explains that mere intellectual knowledge is insufficient; one must have a firm conviction (jazm) that the time has commenced. This is because intention (niyyah) requires decisiveness, and doubt undermines that. The text provides an example: if someone prays under the impression that the time has not entered, but later discovers it actually had, their prayer is invalid. This is because their own supposition (their 'research') led them to deem it invalid, and their incorrect belief does not retroactively validate the prayer. The author then engages with a potential objection: the Hanafi principle that dominant speculation (ghalabat al-zann) suffices in subsidiary matters. He reconciles this by suggesting that 'belief' and 'decisiveness' here may encompass dominant speculation, as the harmful element is either certainty of non-entry or doubt. The stricter view is that even dominant speculation is insufficient, but the author leans towards including it. The analogy of a pure garment mistakenly believed to be impure illustrates the principle: the judgment is based on the person's state at the time, not the objective reality. The passage concludes with a warning about the severity of such negligence, potentially leading to disbelief if one treats the prayer as permissible despite doubts, following a line of reasoning that equates this to putting things in wrong places.

Key Terms
اعتقاد دخول الوقت (i'tiqad dukhul al-waqt): The firm belief or dominant speculation that the prescribed time for prayer has begun.
جزم (jazm): Decisive certainty without any doubt; the required state for a valid intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person prays while doubting the entry of time and later discovers the time had entered?
A) The prayer is valid because the time actually entered
B) The prayer is invalid because the doubter lacks decisive intention
C) The prayer is valid only if he had dominant speculation
D) The prayer is invalid only if he was certain it had not entered

Key Takeaway
Prayer requires decisive intention; doubt in time entry invalidates it regardless of actual time.

Reconciling Jazm and Ghalabat al-Zann in Entry of Time
Reconciliation of certainty and dominant speculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Al-Tahtawi reconciles the requirement of jazm with the Hanafi principle that ghalabat al-zann suffices in subsidiary matters.

Core Idea
Ghalabat al-zann can suffice for 'belief' in time entry, reconciling strict and lenient views.

The passage presents a tension: the requirement of jazm (decisiveness) for intention versus the Hanafi principle that ghalabat al-zann (dominant speculation) stands in place of certainty in subsidiary matters. The author resolves this by suggesting that 'belief' and 'decisiveness' may include dominant speculation, as the harmful element is either certainty of non-entry or doubt. This lesson explores that reconciliation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tension
The text first states that belief in entry is required for jazm, and mere ghalabat al-zann is not sufficient. Then it notes that the Hanafi principle holds that ghalabat al-zann in furu' (subsidiary matters) replaces certainty.
This creates an apparent contradiction.
2
Analyze the author's solution
The author says: 'ويحتمل أن المراد بالإعتقاد، والجزم ما يعم غلبة الظن' (It is possible that what is meant by belief and decisiveness includes dominant speculation).
The author broadens the terms to include dominant speculation.
3
Examine the evidence
The author cites the reasoning: 'لأن الشاك الخ' (because the doubter...). The harmful element is either certainty of non-entry or doubt, not dominant speculation.
This supports inclusion of ghalabat al-zann.
4
Understand the implication
The text then gives the example of certainty of non-entry as more deserving of prohibition than doubt, implying that doubt (but not dominant speculation) is harmful.
This aligns with the reconciliation.
5
Articulate the mufta bihi
Based on this, the relied-upon position is that ghalabat al-zann is sufficient for the condition of belief in time entry, though absolute certainty is preferable.

Analogy of Najis Garment to Time Entry Doubt
Analogy to najis garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling from the analogy of praying in a garment believed to be najis to similar cases of subjective belief.

Core Idea
Subjective belief about impurity invalidates prayer even if reality is pure.

The passage extends its reasoning by analogy: just as praying while thinking a garment is najis invalidates the prayer even if it turns out pure, so does praying while doubting the time. This analogy reinforces that the ruling is based on the person's belief at the time of action. This lesson explores the analogy and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original example
The text presents an analogy: 'نظيره من صلى في ثوب وعنده أنه نجس، فإذا هو طاهر فإنه لا تصح صلاته' (Its analogue is one who prays in a garment while he thinks it is najis, then it turns out to be pure, then his prayer is not valid).
2
Understand the basis
The reasoning is that the person built his prayer on a corrupt belief (belief of impurity), which is treated as non-existence. In legal terms, he is considered as a knower (عارف) because of his negligence.
The corrupt belief is analogous to certainty of non-entry of time.
3
Connect to time entry
The text uses this analogy to support the ruling on time: both cases show that subjective negative belief invalidates the act, even if objective reality is positive.
4
Apply the analogy
If someone prays while believing the garment is najis (though it is pure), the prayer is invalid. Similarly, if someone prays while believing time has not entered (though it had), the prayer is invalid.
The common element is the corrupt belief at the time.
5
Consider the exception
The text notes that this reasoning applies to one who knows the ruling. For a ignorant person, it might be different unless the corrupt belief itself is treated as non-existence.
This highlights the role of knowledge in culpability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Intention as a Condition for Prayer: Distinguishing Worship and Achieving Sincerity
Defining intention, its purposes, and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of intention (niyyah), explain its two purposes (distinguishing worship from habit and distinguishing types of worship), and list the conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention is the decisive will that distinguishes worship from habit and one act of worship from another; it suffices at the start and extends over the entire act.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi defines intention (niyyah) as a necessary condition for prayer and other acts of worship. It explains how intention differentiates fasting from diet and distinguishes obligatory from supererogatory prayers. The text also addresses sincerity (ikhlas) and the impact of riya' (ostentation) on the validity and reward of worship, concluding with the conditions required for a valid intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of Intention
Locate the author's definition: intention is 'al-irada al-jazima' (decisive will). Understand that it is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn), for the validity of worship.
Contrast with other schools that may consider intention a pillar.
2
Analyze the Two Purposes of Intention
The text states intention serves to distinguish worship from habitual acts (e.g., fasting vs. dieting) and to distinguish between different types of worship (e.g., fard vs. nafl prayer). Provide examples from the passage.
Note that without intention, the act remains a mere physical action.
3
Understand the Ruling on Riya' (Ostentation)
The passage distinguishes between initial sincerity and later riya'. In obligatory acts, if one begins with sincerity and later riya' mixes in, the obligation is fulfilled but reward may be reduced. True riya' (praying only when seen) nullifies reward entirely.
This is a Hanafi position; other schools may rule differently.
4
Determine the Timing of Intention
The relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is that intention is required only at the beginning of the act and extends over the entire act. This is sufficient; repeating intention in each part is not necessary.
This applies to acts composed of multiple actions, like prayer.
5
List the Conditions for a Valid Intention
From the text: the person must be Muslim, have discernment (tamyiz), know what is intended, and ensure no contradiction between intention and intended act.
For those unable to form intention in the heart, verbal expression suffices.

(و) تشترط (النية) وهي الإرادة الجازمة لتتميز العبادة عن العادة ويتحقق الإخلاص فيها الله سبحانه وتعالى (و) قوله: (لتتميز العبادة عن العادة) أو يتميز بعض العبادة عن بعض الأمثال الأول الإمساك عن المفطرات فإنه يكون لعدم الحاجة إليه، أو للحمية فلا يمتاز الصوم عنه إلا بالنية، ومثال الثاني في الصلاة مثلاً فإنها تكون فرضاً وواجباً، ونفلاً فشرعت فيها النية ليتميز بعضها عن بعض، وفي المجتبي وغيره من عجز عن إحضار القلب في النية، أو يشك في النية يكفيه اللسان كذا في الشرح . قوله : ( ويتحقق الإخلاص فيها أي في الصلاة، والإخلاص بينك سر وبين ربك لا يطلع عليه ملك فيكتبه ولا شيطان فيفسده ولا هوى فيميله ذكره الحموي، وذلك بأن تريده تعالى بطاعته ولا تريد سواه، وفي الخلاصة : لا رياء في الفرائض اهـ وفي البزازية شرع بالإخلاص، ثم خالطه الرياء، فالعبرة للسابق ولا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوط الواجب اهـ وحقيقة الرياء هو أنه إن خلا عن الناس لا يصلي، وإن كان عند الناس يصلي، فهذا لا ثواب له لأنه أشرك بعبادة ربه، ولو أحسنها لأجلهم فله ثواب الأصل لا الإحسان، ثم إنه إن جمع بين عبادات الوسائل في النية صح كما لو اغتسل الجنابة، وعيد وجمعة إجتمعت ونال ثواب الكل، وكما لو توضأ لنوم، وبعد غيبة وأكل لحم جزور، وكذا يصح لو نوى نافلتين أو أكثر كما لو نوى تحية مسجد، وسنة وضوء، وضحى، وكسوف، والمعتمد أن العبادات ذات الأفعال يكتفي بالنية في أوّلها، ولا يحتاج إليها في كل جزء إكتفاء بإنسحابها عليها، ويشترط لها الإسلام والتمييز والعلم بالمنوى، وأن لا يأتي بمناف بين النية، والمنوي .
And it is required (intention), which is decisive will, to distinguish worship from habit and to achieve sincerity for Allah, the Exalted. And his saying: 'to distinguish worship from habit' or to distinguish some acts of worship from others. The first example is refraining from that which breaks the fast, for it may be due to lack of need or diet, so fasting is not distinguished from that except by intention. The second example is in prayer, for it may be obligatory, necessary, or supererogatory, so intention was legislated to distinguish them from each other. In al-Mujtaba and others: whoever is unable to bring his heart to intention, or doubts his intention, his tongue suffices him, as mentioned in the Sharh. His saying: 'and to achieve sincerity' meaning in prayer. Sincerity is a secret between you and your Lord, no angel can write it, no devil can corrupt it, no desire can sway it. Al-Hamawi mentioned it, and that is by intending Him and obeying Him and not intending other than Him. In al-Khulasah: there is no riya' in obligatory acts. In al-Bazzaziyyah: one begins with sincerity, then riya' mixes with it; consideration is given to the first, and there is no riya' in obligatory acts regarding the nullification of obligation. The reality of riya' is that one does not pray when alone, but prays when people are present; such a person has no reward because he committed shirk in worshiping his Lord. If he beautifies it for their sake, he has the reward of the original act, not the beautification. Then, if one combines acts of worship that are means (wasa'il) in the intention, it is valid, as if he performs ghusl for janabah, Eid, Jumu'ah all together, he attains reward for all; and likewise if he performs wudu' for sleep, after backbiting, and eating camel meat. Similarly, it is valid if he intends two or more supererogatory prayers, such as intending tahiyyat al-masjid, sunnah of wudu', duha, and kusuf. The relied-upon view is that acts of worship consisting of actions suffice with intention at the beginning, and one does not need it in every part, relying on the intention's extension. Conditions for intention include Islam, discernment (tamyiz), knowledge of what is intended, and that one does not bring something contrary between the intention and the intended.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement that defines intention (niyyah) as a condition for prayer and other acts of worship. The author explains that intention serves two main purposes: distinguishing worship from ordinary habits, and distinguishing one type of worship from another. For example, refraining from food could be fasting or just dieting; only intention differentiates. Similarly, intention differentiates between obligatory, necessary, and supererogatory prayers. The author then addresses sincerity (ikhlas), citing that riya' (ostentation) in obligatory acts is not considered to nullify the obligation if it follows initial sincerity, though it may reduce reward. True riya' is described as praying only when people are watching. The discussion also covers combining multiple intentions in a single act: it is valid if the acts are means (wasa'il), like ghusl for multiple purposes, or multiple supererogatory prayers in one prayer. The relied-upon view is that intention is needed only at the beginning of the act, not throughout, as it extends over the entire act. Finally, conditions for valid intention are listed: Islam (the person must be Muslim), tamyiz (discernment, i.e., age of reason), knowledge of what one intends, and no contradiction between the intention and the intended act.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Decisive will (irada jazima) that distinguishes worship from habit and differentiates between types of worship.
رياء (riya'): Performing worship for the sake of people rather than Allah; it nullifies reward but may not invalidate the obligation if it follows initial sincerity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon view regarding the timing of intention in acts of worship consisting of actions?
A) Intention is required at every part of the act
B) Intention is required only at the beginning, and it extends over the entire act
C) Intention must be verbalized throughout the act
D) Intention is not required if the act is obligatory

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for the validity of prayer; it suffices at the beginning and extends over the entire act, with conditions including Islam, discernment, knowledge, and harmony with the intended act.

The Tahrimah Dispute: Condition or Pillar?
Critical refinement of an intra-Hanafi dispute on the tahrimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nature of the opening takbir (tahrimah) and apply the thamarah to determine prayer validity when conditions are rectified during the takbir.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but a pillar according to Imam Muhammad—with real consequences for prayer validity.

The opening takbir (tahrimah) is the act that transitions a person from outside prayer to within prayer. But is it a condition (shart) that must be fulfilled, or a pillar (rukn) that constitutes the prayer's essence? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad, and shows how the differing views affect the validity of prayer when conditions are corrected mid-takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
Recognize that the tahrimah (opening takbir) is the subject of an intra-Hanafi dispute: Is it a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn)? The base text declares it a condition, aligning with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The two shaykhs are Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Imam Muhammad differs.
2
Examine the proof from Quran
The verse 'wa dhakara isma rabbihi fasalla' (87:15) is cited. The conjunction 'and' (wa) implies the two acts are separate, so mentioning the name of the Lord is not part of the prayer itself, making the takbir external to prayer's essence.
This dalil supports the condition view.
3
Understand the opposing proof
Imam Muhammad argues that tahrimah is an obligatory dhikr performed while standing, analogous to qira'ah (recitation), which is a pillar. Hence, it should be a pillar.
Al-Shafi'i shares this view.
4
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence)
Consider a person who begins the takbir while carrying najis, facing away from qiblah, or with awrah uncovered, but rectifies these before completing the takbir. According to the two shaykhs, the prayer is valid because conditions can be fulfilled during the takbir; according to Muhammad, it is invalid because the pillar (tahrimah) was invalid from the start.
This is the key test case for the dispute.
5
Explore the ruling on building prayers
The passage discusses building a supererogatory prayer on the tahrimah of an obligatory prayer—permissible (with dislike) according to the two shaykhs, but prohibited by those who deem tahrimah a pillar. Building an obligatory prayer on another's tahrimah is prohibited by the majority.
This demonstrates how the condition/pillar classification extends to other rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويشترط التحريمة ) هو قول الشيخين لقوله تعالى وذكر اسم ربه فصلی، فإنه عطف الصلاة عليها العطف يقتضي المغايرة، وليس من عطف الكل على الجزء فإنه إنما يكون لنكتة بلاغية وهي غير ظاهرة هنا قوله وليست ركناً) أشار به إلى خلاف محمد فإنه يقول بركنيتها لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام، فكانت ركناً كالقراءة، وتظهر الثمرة فيما إذا كان حاملاً لنجاسة مانعة، فألقاها عند فراغه منها أو كان منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها، أو مكشوف العورة فسترها بعمل يسير أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال، ثم ظهر عند الفراغ، فعندهما تجوز صلاته لوجود الأركان مستجمعة للشروط، وتقدم الشرط جائز بالإجماع، وعبارة البرهان، وإنما اشترط لها ما اشترط للصلاة لا باعتبار ركنيتها، بل باعتبار إتصالها بالقيام الذي هو ركنها، وقد منع ذلك الزيلعي وعند محمد، والشافعي لا تجوز لأنها ركن، وقد أداه المنافي، أو قبل الوقت وجاز بناء النفل على تحريمة الفرض مع الكراهة عندهما لأن النفل مطلقاً صلاة، والفرض صلاة مخصوصة ففي الفرض معنى النفل، وزيادة لأن الخاص يتضمن العام، فكان العقد على الفرض متضمناً للعقد على النقل، ولأنّ الشرط لا يشترط تحصيله لكل صلاة كالطهارة، بل يصح شرط الفرض للنفل، ولا يجوز عند القائل بالركنية، وأما بناء الفرض على تحريمة فرض آخر، أو على تحريمة نقل فظاهر المذهب، والجمهور منعه، وأما بناء النقل
His saying: 'And the tahrimah is required' that is the saying of the two shaykhs [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf] based on the verse 'And he mentions the name of his Lord and prays' because the conjunctive 'and' joining prayer to mentioning the name implies difference, and it is not from the category of joining the whole to the part, as that would require a rhetorical nuance which is not apparent here. His saying: 'and it is not a pillar' indicates the disagreement with Muhammad, who says it is a pillar because it is an obligatory remembrance in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation. The practical result appears in the case where one is carrying a prohibiting impurity and discards it at the end of the takbir, or is turning away from the qiblah and then faces it, or has exposed awrah and covers it with a minor action, or begins the takbir before the moment of zawal and then it appears afterward. According to the two shaykhs, his prayer is valid because the pillars exist fulfilling the conditions, and it is permissible to advance a condition by consensus. The statement of al-Burhan: 'Indeed it is only made a condition what is made a condition for prayer, not by considering it a pillar, but by considering its connection to standing, which is its pillar.' Al-Zayla'i rejected that. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, it is not valid because it is a pillar, and he performed an invalidating act, or before the time. And it is permissible to build a supererogatory prayer on the tahrimah of an obligatory prayer with dislike according to the two shaykhs, because supererogatory in absolute terms is prayer, and obligatory is a specific prayer, so in the obligatory there is the meaning of supererogatory and more, because the specific includes the general. Thus the contract on the obligatory includes the contract on the supererogatory. And because a condition is not required to be fulfilled for every prayer like purification; rather, the condition of obligatory is valid for supererogatory. And it is not permissible according to the one who holds pillar-hood. As for building an obligatory prayer on the tahrimah of another obligatory, or on the tahrimah of a supererogatory, the apparent madhhab and the majority prohibit it. And as for building supererogatory...
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement that presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nature of the opening takbir (tahrimah). The base text states that tahrimah is a condition (shart). The author attributes this view to 'the two shaykhs' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and supports it with a Quranic verse: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (87:15), arguing that the conjunction 'and' implies two separate acts, so mentioning Allah's name is distinct from the prayer itself, hence tahrimah is not part of the prayer's essence but a condition. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that tahrimah is a pillar (rukn) because it is an obligatory dhikr performed while standing, analogous to recitation (qira'ah), which is a pillar. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is significant: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone begins the takbir while carrying najis, facing away from qiblah, or with awrah uncovered, but rectifies these before the takbir ends, the prayer is valid because the pillars (like qiyam) are fulfilled, and conditions can be advanced by consensus. They consider the takbir's own conditions (like purity, facing qiblah, covering awrah) as conditions of the takbir only because it connects to the pillar of standing, not because it itself is a pillar. Al-Zayla'i rejected this reasoning. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, the prayer would be invalid because tahrimah is a pillar, and performing the takbir before fulfilling its conditions invalidates it. The passage also discusses building one prayer on another's tahrimah: it is permissible (though disliked) to build a supererogatory prayer on the tahrimah of an obligatory one according to the two shaykhs, because the specific (obligatory) includes the general (supererogatory). Those who consider tahrimah a pillar prohibit this. The apparent madhhab prohibits building an obligatory prayer on another's tahrimah.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer and renders prohibited (muharram) actions outside the prayer.
ثمرة (thamarah): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; in this case, the validity of prayer when conditions are met after starting the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person begins the opening takbir while facing away from the qiblah but immediately turns to face it before completing the takbir, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) The prayer is valid because conditions can be perfected during the takbir
B) The prayer is invalid because tahrimah is a pillar that requires facing qiblah at its inception
C) The prayer is valid only if the turn is done without excessive movement
D) The prayer is invalid because the entire takbir must be done facing the qiblah

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is a condition according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, allowing flexibility for conditions to be perfected during the takbir—a ruling with significant practical impact on everyday prayer.

The Condition of Intention Concurrency with the Opening Takbir (Tahrimah)
Specifies the first condition for validity of opening takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of intention concurrency (actual and legal) required for the opening takbir and identify which acts break the connection.

Core Idea
Intention must accompany the opening takbir; actual concurrency is best, but legal concurrency via prior intention suffices if no severing act occurs.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya refines the first condition for a valid opening takbir (tahrimah): the intention must be concurrent. The author explains that this concurrency can be actual (at the same moment) or legal (through a prior intention maintained without interruption). He clarifies that walking to prayer or performing wudu does not break the connection, while eating, drinking, and speech do. The passage also provides evidence from the Quran ('And your Lord, magnify Him') and the hadith ('The key to prayer is purification...'), and addresses differing positions within the Hanafi school regarding timing for imam and follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition being explained
Read the opening lines: the first condition for validity of tahrimah is that it 'must be accompanied by intention, either actually or legally, without a separator'. Note that this is a condition (shart) for the opening takbir.
2
Distinguish actual vs legal concurrency
Actual concurrency (muqaranah haqiqiyyah) means intending at the moment of saying Allahu Akbar. Legal concurrency (hukman) means a prior intention that is maintained without a break. Identify examples given: actual—intending concurrently with the takbir; legal—intending during wudu and continuing to prayer without distraction.
The preferred method is actual concurrency, but legal is acceptable.
3
Recognize severing vs non-severing acts
The text lists acts that sever the connection: eating, drinking, speaking. Acts that do NOT sever: walking to prayer, performing wudu. Understand that the latter are part of preparation and do not indicate disinterest.
4
Examine the evidences (dalil)
The author cites the Quranic command 'And your Lord, magnify Him' (Surat al-Ala, 74:3) which the mufassirun agree refers to the opening takbir, and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its forbidden element (tahrimuhu) is the takbir...' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Note that ijma (consensus) is also cited: the command for obligation and the specific mention of takbir as tahrimah.
The hadith is hasan (sound) by al-Tirmidhi's evaluation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on imamah and iqtida
The passage discusses differences on when the imam should form intention for imamah: before starting or only when someone follows. Also, there is difference on whether the follower can advance his intention to follow before the imam's tahrimah. The text favors the view that the imam's intention is valid from the start of leadership, and the follower should intend when the imam stands in place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحة التحريمة إثنا عشر شرطاً ذكرت منها سبعة متناً والباقي شرحاً فالأول من شروط صحة التحريمة أن توجد مقارنة للنية حقيقة أو حكماً بلا فاصل بينها وبين النية بأجنبي يمنع الإتصال للإجماع عليه كالأكل والشرب والكلام فأما المشي للصلاة، والوضوء فليسا مانعين. قوله: (وعليه عامة المشايخ وهو قول المحققين من مشايخنا بدائع، وهو المعتبر من المذهب منية المصلي. قوله: (والهاء لتحقيق الإسمية) أي إنما أتى بالهاء المفسرون على المراد به تكبيرة الإفتتاح وعليه إنعقد الإجماع لأن الأمر للوجوب، وغيرها ليس بواجب فتعينت للمراد تحرزاً عن تعطيل النص. قوله: (والسنة) قال صلى الله عليه وسلم مفتاح الصلاة الطهور، وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم. رواه أبو داود وحسنه الترمذي. قوله: (إثنا عشر شرطاً قد عدها خمسة عشر شرطاً). قوله: (أن توجد مقارنة للنية حقيقة) مثال المقارنة حقيقة أن ينوي مقارناً للشروع بالتكبير، وهو الأفضل بإجماع أصحابنا، وانظر هل تكون تلك المقارنة ولو وجدت بعد ذكر بعض حروف الإسم الكريم أو ذكر كله قبل الفراغ من أكبر والظاهر نعم وحرره. قوله: (أو حكماً) مثال المقارنة الحكمية أن يقدم النية على الشروع قالوا: لو نوى عند الوضوء أنه يصلي الظهر مثلاً، ولم يشتغل بعد النية بعمل يدل على الأعراض كأكل وشرب وكلام ونحوها ثم انتهى إلى محل الصلاة، ولم تحضره النية جازت صلاته بالنية السابقة، ويجوز تقديمها على الوقت كسائر الشروط ما لم يوجد ما يقطعها، ونقل ابن أمير حاج عن أبي هريرة بن هبيرة إشتراط دخول الوقت للنية المتقدمة عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وينبغي أن يكون وقت نية الإمامة عند الشروع وإن لم يقتد به أحد لأنه قد يقتدي به من لا يراه من الملائكة والجن أفاده الحموي، خلافاً لما في الأشباه من أنه ينبغي أن يكون وقت إقتداء أحد به لا قبله. وأما نية المأموم الإقتداء ففي القهستاني، ولا يجوز تقديم نية إقتدائه عن تحريمة الإمام عند بعض أئمة بخارى، وصحح، وقيل ينوي بعد قول الإمام الله قبل قوله أكبر، والذي عليه عامة العلماء أنه ينوي حين وقف الإمام موقف الإمامة وهو أجود كما في النظم اهـ، ويطلب الفرق بين صحة تقديم نية الصلاة وهي فرض دون تقديم نية الإقتداء على هذا الوقت، وهو كذلك، والذي ذكره الشارح في الإمامة جواز تقديمها فالحكم فيهما.
It is stipulated for the validity of the tahrimah twelve conditions, seven of which are mentioned in the matn and the rest in the sharh. The first of the conditions for the validity of the tahrimah is that it must be accompanied by intention, either actually or legally, without a separator between them and the intention that prevents connection, due to consensus. Such as eating, drinking, and speech. As for walking for prayer and ablution, they are not preventers. He said: (And upon it the generality of the mashayikh, and it is the saying of the muhaqqiqun among our mashayikh in al-Badai', and it is the relied-upon in the madhhab in Munyat al-Musalli. He said: (And the ha' is for confirming the nounhood), meaning that the ha' is brought to indicate that what it enters upon is a noun, i.e., for the known word, for if not for this ha', it would be thought that it is the infinitive. It is also possible that it is for exaggeration or for unity, not for femininity. He said: (And it is called takbir for opening) and takbir is added for opening because with it the prayer is opened. He said: (For its prohibition of things permitted outside the prayer) such as eating, drinking, and speech, and attributing prohibition to it is metaphorical because the prohibitor is Allah the Exalted, so prohibition is established by it, not from it. He said: (And it is stipulated by the Book) Allah said: 'And your Lord, magnify Him' the commentators agreed that what is meant by it is the opening takbir, and upon this consensus is formed because the command indicates obligation, and other than it is not obligatory, so it was determined for the intended meaning to avoid disabling the text. He said: (And the Sunnah) the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its forbidden element is the takbir, and its permissible element is the taslim.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and declared sound by al-Tirmidhi. He said: (Twelve conditions, he counted them as fifteen conditions). He said: (That it exists in actual conjunction with the intention) the example of actual conjunction is that one intends concurrently with commencing the takbir, and this is best by consensus of our companions. Consider whether that conjunction is valid even if it occurs after mentioning some letters of the noble name or its entirety before finishing 'Allahu Akbar' – the apparent is yes, and examine it. He said: (Or legally) the example of legal conjunction is that one advances the intention before commencing. They said: if one intended during ablution to pray zuhr, for example, and after the intention did not engage in an act indicating disinterest like eating, drinking, speech, etc., then proceeded to the place of prayer and the intention did not come to him, his prayer is valid with the prior intention. It is permissible to advance it before the time like all conditions as long as nothing interrupts it. Ibn Amir Hajj narrated from Abu Hurayra ibn Hubayra the condition of the entering of the time for the advanced intention from Abu Hanifa. And it should be that the time of the intention for imamah is at the start, even if no one follows him, because he may be followed by those unseen like angels and jinn, as al-Hamawi stated, contrary to what is in al-Ashbah that it should be at the time someone follows him, not before. As for the intention of the follower to follow, in al-Qahastani: it is not permissible to advance his intention to follow before the imam's tahrimah according to some imams of Bukhara, and it is declared sound. It is said: he intends after the imam's saying 'Allah' before his saying 'Akbar'. And the position of the generality of scholars is that he intends when the imam stands in the imam's station, and this is most sound as in al-Nazm. And one seeks the distinction between the permissibility of advancing the intention for prayer, which is obligatory, without advancing the intention to follow at this time, and it is so. And what the sharh mentioned about imamah concerning the permissibility of advancing it, so the ruling in both is...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage from the hashya explains the first condition for the validity of the opening takbir (tahrimah): it must be accompanied by intention (niyyah). The author clarifies that this accompaniment can be either actual (haqiqatan) – meaning the intention occurs at the very moment of uttering the takbir, which is the best and most precautionary approach – or legal (hukman), where the intention is made earlier and continues without interruption by acts that indicate disinterest (like eating, drinking, or speaking). The text emphasizes that even walking toward the prayer or performing ablution does not break the connection, as these are part of the preparation for prayer. The hashya then elaborates on the word 'tahrimah', explaining why the ha' is added, and provides the foundational evidence from the Quran (Surat al-Ala: 'And your Lord, magnify Him') and Sunnah (hadith: 'The key to prayer is purification…'). It also discusses the time for intending imamah for the imam and the follower, noting divergent opinions within the Hanafi school and ultimately siding with the view that the imam's intention occurs at the start of his leadership position.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer, which renders permissible actions (like eating, speaking) forbidden during the prayer.
مقارنة حقيقية (muqaranah haqiqiyyah): The intention is formed simultaneously with the commencement of the takbir.
نية (niyyah): The intention to perform a specific prayer, made in the heart at or before the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following acts does NOT break the legal concurrency (hukman) of intention?
A) Eating
B) Drinking
C) Walking to the prayer area
D) Speaking

Key Takeaway
The first condition for a valid opening takbir is that intention must accompany it, either actually or legally, without any act that severs connection—walking and wudu do not sever, while eating, drinking, and speech do.

Conditions for the Opening Takbir: Standing and Intention Timing
Explains second and third conditions for valid opening takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of the opening takbir and apply the rule regarding standing posture when catching the imam in bowing.

Core Idea
The opening takbir requires standing (or near-standing) and immediate intention; delay or improper posture invalidates it.

The opening takbir (tahrimah) is the entry into prayer. For it to be valid, certain conditions must be met at the moment of takbir. This lesson explains the second and third conditions: proper standing posture and the timing of intention. It also clarifies what happens when a latecomer catches the imam bowing — a scenario that tests the boundaries of these conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for valid tahrimah
From the passage, list the conditions that must be satisfied at the moment of the opening takbir. They include a specific posture (standing or near-standing) and timely intention.
The passage also starts a fourth condition about audible pronunciation.
2
Analyze the standing requirement
The condition does not require fully erect standing; a slight bend is acceptable as long as the person is closer to standing than to bowing. This is the threshold.
Contrast with other schools that may demand full uprightness.
3
Apply the rule to the mas'ala of catching the imam in ruku'
If a latecomer straightens up after the imam has bowed, his posture determines whether his takbir counts as the opening takbir. If closer to standing, it is valid; if closer to bowing, it is not valid as the opening takbir.
The intention to make it a bowing takbir is irrelevant – the posture dictates the ruling.
4
Explain the ruling on delaying intention
The intention must be present at the time of the takbir (concurrent or legally prior). Delaying it until after the takbir invalidates the initiation. This is because prayer is indivisible; unlike fasting, there is no hardship that justifies delay.
Best practice is to have intention exactly concurrent with the takbir to avoid differing opinions.
5
Note the fourth condition (partial)
The passage begins to mention that the takbir must be pronounced audibly enough for the person to hear himself. This condition ensures that the takbir is actually uttered.
The text cuts off partway through this condition.

So they are not preventers. (And) the second of the conditions for the validity of the tahrimah is performing the tahrimah while standing, or slightly bent, before his bending occurs, that which is closer to bowing. He said in al-Burhan: If someone catches the imam bowing and then straightens his back, then says the takbir – if he is closer to standing, the initiation is valid, even if he intended by it the takbir for bowing, his intention is void because the one catching the imam in bowing does not need to say two takbirs, contrary to some. If he is closer to bowing, the initiation is not valid. (And) the third of them is not delaying the intention after the tahrimah, because prayer is an act of worship that is indivisible; as long as he does not intend it, it does not occur as worship. There is no hardship in not delaying it, unlike fasting. And it includes both conjunction and precedence, but actual conjunction is better for precaution, to exit from disagreement, and performing it after the entrance of the time, observing the pillar. Commentary
This section continues the discussion of conditions for the opening takbir. The second condition is that the takbir must be performed while standing (for those obligated to stand) or slightly bent, as long as the bend is closer to standing than to bowing. The ruling is illustrated with the example of someone joining the imam while he is bowing: if after straightening up he is closer to standing, his takbir is valid as the opening takbir; if closer to bowing, the initiation is invalid, and he would intend it as the bowing takbir instead. The third condition is that the intention must not be delayed after the takbir. The reasoning is that prayer is a single, indivisible act of worship; without intention from the start, the initial part would lack worship. Unlike fasting, where intention can be delayed until before noon due to hardship, there is no such excuse in prayer. The best practice is to have intention concurrent with the takbir (actual conjunction) to avoid differing opinions. The text also mentions a fourth condition (incomplete in this passage): the takbir must be pronounced audibly enough for one to hear oneself.

Key Terms
قيام (qiyam): Standing posture; for the opening takbir, it includes both full standing and a slight bend closer to standing than to bowing.
تأخير النية (ta'khir al-niyyah): Delaying the intention until after the opening takbir; this is not permitted in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must repeat the takbir after standing

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is valid only if performed while standing (or near-standing) and with intention concurrent or prior; delay or improper posture prevents the prayer from commencing.
