Conditions for the Opening Takbir (Takbirat al-Ihram)
Explains four conditions for valid opening takbir: standing, intention timing, and audibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for the validity of the opening takbir, including standing posture, timing of intention, and audibility, and explain why intention must not be delayed and why self-hearing is required.

Core Idea
Opening takbir requires standing, immediate intention, and self-audible utterance; otherwise, prayer does not commence.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details three key conditions for the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram): standing while saying it, not delaying the intention, and uttering it audibly enough for oneself to hear. It addresses intra-Hanafi disagreements on the degree of audibility and refutes the analogy to fasting regarding intention timing. Understanding these conditions ensures the prayer's commencement is legally valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, extract the second, third, and fourth conditions for the validity of the opening takbir: standing, not delaying intention, and audibility.
The first condition is not covered in this excerpt.
2
Analyze the standing condition
The worshipper must be standing or slightly leaning forward, but not bending to the extent that his posture is closer to bowing. The example of a latecomer catching the imam in bowing clarifies the threshold.
If closer to bowing, the takbir does not commence prayer; the latecomer should straighten first.
3
Examine the intention timing
Intention must precede or be simultaneous with the takbir. Delaying it invalidates the prayer because prayer is indivisible; analogy to fasting is rejected as there is no hardship in prayer.
The best is simultaneous intention to exit disagreement.
4
Understand the audibility requirement
The takbir must be uttered such that the worshipper hears himself (if not deaf). The majority view is that soft recitation (mukhāfatah) means hearing oneself; al-Hinduwānī required also others nearby, and al-Karkhī held that mere letter correction suffices.
The correct view is that a voice is necessary; the mute is exempt.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a person who begins the takbir while bent so low that his hands could touch his knees—invalid. Or a person who says the takbir silently without moving lips audibly—invalid. Or one who intends after completing the takbir—invalid.
These conditions apply to all verbal acts like tashahhud, dhikr, and divorce as mentioned in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فليسا مانعين (و) الثاني من شروط صحة التحريمة الإتيان) بالتحريمة قائماً) أو منحنياً قليلاً (قبل) وجود (انحنائه) بما هو أقرب (للركوع) قال في البرهان : لو أدرك الإمام راكعاً فحتى ظهره، ثم كبر إن كان إلى القيام أقرب صح الشروع ولو أراد به تكبير الركوع وتلغو نيته لأنّ مدرك الإمام في الركوع لا يحتاج إلى تكبير مرتين خلافاً لبعضهم وإن كان إلى الركوع أقرب لا يصح الشروع (و) الثالث منها عدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة) لأن الصلاة عبادة، لا تتجزأ فما لم ينوها لا تقع عبادة ولا حرج في عدم تأخيرها بخلاف الصوم، وهو صادق بالمقارنة وبالتقدم والأفضل المقارنة الحقيقية للاحتياط خروجاً من الخلاف وإيجادها بعد دخول القوت مراعاة للركنية (و) الرابع منها (النطق بالتحريمة بحيث يسمع نفسه) بدون صمم ولا يلزم الأخرس تحريك لسانه على الصحيح، وغير الأخرس يشترط سماعه نطقه (على الأصح كما قاله شمس الأئمة الحلواني وأكثر المشايخ على أن الصحيح أن الجهر يسمع غيره والمخافتة أن يسمع نفسه، وقال الهندواني لا تجزيه ما لم تسمع أذناه ومن بقربه فالسماع شرط فيما يتعلق بالنطق باللسان التحريمة والقراءة السرية والتشهد والأذكار والتسمية على الذبيحة ووجوب سجدة التلاوة والعتاق، والطلاق والإستثناء واليمين والنذر والإسلام والإيمان حتى لو أجرى الطلاق على قلبه، وحرك لسانه من غير يسمع لا يقع وإن صحح الحروف، وقال الكرخي القراءة تصحيح الحروف وإن لم يكن صوت بحيث يسمع والصحيح خلافه قال المحقق الكمال بن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى اعلم أن القراءة، وإن كانت فعل اللسان لكن فعله الذي هو كلام والكلام بالحروف تلفظ . وقال الكرخي مقابل قول الحلواني، وقول الأكثرين في تفسير المخافتة فالمخافتة عنده تصحيح الحروف
So they are not preventers. (And) the second of the conditions for the validity of the opening takbir is performing the opening takbir while standing or slightly leaning forward before his leaning occurs in a manner closer to bowing. Al-Burhan said: If he catches the imam bowing and straightens his back, then says the takbir, if he is closer to standing, the commencement is valid, even if he intended it as the takbir for bowing and his intention is invalid because the one catching the imam in bowing does not need two takbirs, contrary to some. If he is closer to bowing, commencement is not valid. (And) the third of them is not delaying the intention after the opening takbir because prayer is an indivisible worship; if he does not intend it, it does not occur as worship. There is no hardship in not delaying it, unlike fasting. It is true with simultaneity and precedence. The best is true simultaneity for caution, to exit from disagreement, and its occurrence after the entrance of the time to observe its pillar nature. (And) the fourth of them is uttering the opening takbir such that he hears himself without deafness. The mute is not required to move his tongue according to the correct view. For the non-mute, hearing his own utterance is required according to the most correct view, as stated by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and most shaykhs, that the correct view is that loud recitation makes others hear and soft recitation makes himself hear. Al-Hinduwani said: It is not valid unless his ears and those near him hear. So hearing is a condition for what pertains to utterance by the tongue: the opening takbir, silent recitation, tashahhud, remembrances, saying Bismillah over the slaughter, the obligation of the prostration of recitation, emancipation, divorce, exception, oath, vow, Islam, and faith. Even if he performed divorce in his heart and moved his tongue without being heard, it does not occur even if he corrects the letters. Al-Karkhi said: Recitation is correcting the letters even if there is no voice that can be heard. The correct view is otherwise. The investigator Kamal ibn al-Humam said: Know that recitation, although it is an action of the tongue, its action is speech, and speech is with letters uttered. Al-Karkhi's view opposes that of al-Halwani and the majority in interpreting soft recitation; according to him, soft recitation is correcting the letters.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah) on the conditions for the validity of the opening takbīr (takbīrat al-ihrām) in prayer. The text discusses four conditions, with emphasis on the second, third, and fourth. 

**Second condition: Standing (qiyām) while saying the takbīr.** The worshipper must be standing or slightly leaning forward, but not bent to the extent that his posture is closer to bowing than to standing. The text cites al-Burhān: if a latecomer catches the imam in rukūʿ and straightens his back, saying the takbīr, then if his posture is closer to standing, his commencement is valid; if closer to bowing, it is not. Even if he intended the takbīr for bowing, his intention is disregarded because one catching the imam in bowing does not need two takbīrs, contrary to some scholars.

**Third condition: The intention (niyyah) must not be delayed after the takbīr.** Prayer is indivisible; without intention, the act is not worship. Unlike fasting, there is no hardship in not delaying the intention, so it must be simultaneous with or precede the takbīr, but the best is true simultaneity to avoid disagreement and to observe the pillar nature of intention.

**Fourth condition: The takbīr must be uttered audibly such that the worshipper hears himself.** This is the relied-upon view. The mute is exempt from tongue movement. The majority (including Shams al-A'imma al-Halwānī) hold that loud recitation makes others hear, while soft recitation makes oneself hear. Al-Hinduwānī required that both one's own ears and those nearby hear, but this is not the relied position. The condition of hearing oneself applies to all verbal acts: the takbīr, silent recitation, tashahhud, dhikr, tasmiyah over slaughter, obligation of sajdat al-tilāwah, emancipation, divorce, exception, oath, vow, Islam, and faith. For example, if one pronounces divorce in his heart and moves his tongue without being heard, it does not occur, even if the letters are correct. Al-Karkhī held that recitation is merely correcting the letters, even without a voice, but the correct view is otherwise, as stated by Kamāl ibn al-Humām.

Key Terms
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbīr (takbīrat al-ihrām) that commences the prayer.
نية (niyyah): Intention to perform the specific prayer; must be present at the beginning of the prayer.
مخافتة (mukhāfatah): Soft recitation (silent or low voice) that the worshipper can hear himself.
صمم (ṣamam): Deafness; a condition that exempts one from audibility requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid because he said the takbīr.
B) The prayer is invalid because his posture is closer to bowing than standing.
C) It is valid if he intended the takbīr for bowing.
D) It is valid only if he is a latecomer catching the imam in bowing.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbīr is valid only if performed while standing (or close to it), with intention present from the start, and uttered audibly enough for oneself to hear; otherwise the prayer does not begin.

The Condition of Audibility in Quiet Recitation (Mukhafatah) in Prayer
Explains the condition of hearing oneself in prayer recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement to hear oneself in quiet recitation and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its definition.

Core Idea
Quiet recitation in prayer requires the reciter to hear himself; mere letter-correction without sound is invalid.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of certain utterances in prayer: that the reciter must hear his own voice. The source passage presents the majority Hanafi view (Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and most mashayikh) that quiet recitation (mukhafatah) is defined as making oneself heard, and contrasts it with alternative views from al-Hindwani and al-Karkhi. The rational proof establishes that speech requires sound; without it, the act is mere indication and not valid recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that the passage concerns the validity of utterances in prayer: the opening takbir, silent recitation, tashahhud, remembrances, etc. The ruling is that hearing oneself (isma' nafsih) is a condition for their validity.
This applies to both quiet and loud recitation: for loud, others must hear; for quiet, the reciter must hear himself.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
The text declares that the correct view (al-sahih) is the one held by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and most scholars: mukhafatah means the reciter hears himself.
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the two opposing views: al-Hindwani requires the reciter and those nearby to hear; al-Karkhi says correcting letters suffices even without sound. Note the sources of these views.
The text explicitly rejects al-Karkhi's view as unsound.
4
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
Follow Ibn al-Humam's analysis: speech is composed of letters (huruf), each letter is a quality of sound, and sound requires breath and articulation. Without sound, no letter, thus no speech. Therefore, moving the tongue without sound is not recitation.
This is a 'dalil aqli' (rational proof) based on the nature of kalam.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Conclude that if a person merely moves his tongue without any audible sound, his prayer is invalid according to the majority. He must produce sound that he can hear (even if faint).
Exceptions: the mute is excused; obstacles like loud background noise may be accommodated if potential audibility exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة حقيقته أن صمم ولا يلزم الأخرس تحريك لسانه على الصحيح، وغير الأخرس يشترط سماعه نطقه (على الأصح كما قاله شمس الأئمة الحلواني وأكثر المشايخ على أن الصحيح أن الجهر يسمع غيره والمخافتة أن يسمع نفسه، وقال الهندواني لا تجزيه ما لم تسمع أذناه ومن بقربه فالسماع شرط فيما يتعلق بالنطق باللسان التحريمة والقراءة السرية والتشهد والأذكار والتسمية على الذبيحة ووجوب سجدة التلاوة والعتاق، والطلاق والإستثناء واليمين والنذر والإسلام والإيمان حتى لو أجرى الطلاق على قلبه، وحرك لسانه من غير يسمع لا يقع وإن صحح الحروف، وقال الكرخي القراءة تصحيح الحروف وإن لم يكن صوت بحيث يسمع والصحيح خلافه قال صمم) أما لو كان به أو كانت جلبة أصوات فالشرط أن يكون بحيث لو أزيل المانع لأمكن السماع، ولا يسمع نفسه حقيقة في تلك الحالة كما لا يشترط إسماع غيره إلا في العقود كبيع وهبة ونكاح فلا بد من إسماع غيره أيضاً كما في القهستاني قوله : (ولا يلزم الأخرس تحريك لسانه وكذا الامي بل يكتفيان بمجرد النية على الصحيح، فينبغي أن يشترط لها القيام لقيامها مقام التحريمة وأن تقديمها على الشروع لا يصح كالتحريمة، ولم أره لهم نهر . قوله : (وأكثر المشايخ) مبتدأ، وقوله : على أنّ الخ خبرة، وليس معطوفاً على الحلواني، والألم يحسن ذكر على قوله: (وقال الهندواني الخ) ظاهر ما هنا أن الهندواني لم يقل بقوله أكثر المشايخ، والذي في كبيره أن ما عليه أكثر المشايخ هو قول الهندواني إلا أنه قال وزاد في المجتبى في النقل عن الهندواني أنه لا يجزيه ما لم تسمع أذناه ومن بقربه اهـ ونقل في الذخيرة عن شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن الأصح هذا اهـ قلت: الظاهر أنّ ما زاده في المجتبى يرجع إلى ما قبله لأن الغالب أنه إذا أسمع أذنيه أن يسمع من بقربه ممن يكون ملاصقاً، ولا يكاد ينفك ذلك. قوله : (فالسماع (شرط) تفريع على الأصح الذي في المصنف، وعلى قول أكثر المشايخ في تفسير المخافتة، والمراد أنه شرط لتحصيل المنطوق به إن كان فرضاً أو واجباً أو سنة. قوله: (التحريمة) وما عطف عليه بدل من ما في قوله فيما يتعلق قوله : (ووجوب سجدة التلاوة) الأولى حذف وجوب، وسجدة لأن الكلام في المنطوق به قوله: (والإيمان) بكسر الهمزة أورد عليه أنه التصديق القلبي، ولا لفظ فيه إلا أن يكون مبنياً على أنه قول، وعمل. قوله : (حتى لو أجرى) إنما ذكره لأنه محل الوهم فإذا لم يجزه على قلبه، والمسئلة بحالها فعدم الوقوع أولى قوله : (يسمع) بالبناء للمجهول والجملة محلها جر صفة لتلفظ . قوله: (وقال الكرخي مقابل قول الحلواني، وقول الأكثرين في تفسير المخافتة فالمخافتة عنده تصحيح الحروف، ويجري في كل ما يتعلق بالنطق باللسان قوله : (الذي هو كلام أي لا مجرد الحركة قوله: (والكلام بالحروف) مبتدأ وخبر أي لا يتحقق الكلام إلا بالحروف، والحاصل أن المراتب ثلاثة حرف وصوت ونفس وكل أخص من الذي بعده قوله: (والحرف كيفية تعرض للصوت لأنه هو الصوت المعتمد على المخارج فالكيفية هي إعتماد الصوت على المخارج، وفيه أن الحرف هو الصوت المعتمد لا الإعتماد قوله: (وهو أخص من النفس) الفاء لأن النفس هو الهواء مطلقاً اعتمد أولاً قوله : (فإنّ النفس المعروض بالقرع) أي هو الهواء الذي عرض عليه القرع يعني أن القرع بالعضلات يعرض على النفس، والصوت هو مجموع النفس مع القرع ومن المعلوم أن المعروض قد يتحقق بدون عارضه كتحقق الإنسان بدون صفة الكتابة، والمعروض، والعارض أخص من المعروض وحده كإنسان وضاحك فإنّ الإنسان فقط أعم من الإنسان الضاحك والقرع يتحقق بالعضلات قوله: (عارض للصوت)، والصوت عرض يقوم بمحل يخرج من داخل الرئة إلى خارجها مع النفس مستطيلاً ممتداً متصلاً بمقطع من مقاطع حروف الحلق واللسان والشفتين قوله: (فمجرد الخ) هو روح العلة . قوله : بلا صوت) أي بل بالنفس الذي هو مطلق الهواء. قوله : (إيماء) أي إشارة إليها والذي يومي بالشيء لا يكون آتياً بحقيقته كالمومي بالصلاة فإنه لم يأت بحقيقة الركوع، والسجود. قوله: (بعضلات المخارج) | العضلات جمع العضلة، وكسفينة كل عصبة معها لحم غليظ كذا في القاموس، والمخارج جمع مخرج محل خروج الحروف ، كذا في الأزهرية فالإضافة من إضافة العام إلى الخاص . قوله : (لا حروف) عطف على إيماء أي لا حروف حقيقة، فلا كلام أي إذا انتفت الحروف انتفى الكلام أي وهو لا بد منه فإنه المطلوب شرعاً، وإذا انتفى الكلام إنتفت القراءة، فلا تصح الصلاة قوله : (ومن متعلقات القلب النية قال في الشرح : تنبيه في إشتراط النطق بالتحريمة إشارة إلى أنه لا يشترط النطق بالنية لأنها من متعلقات القلب التي لا يشترط لها النطق، وقد أجمع العلماء على أنه لو نوى بقلبه، ولم يتكلم بنيته فإنه يجوز اهـ. قوله : (بالنية) متعلق بمحذوف أي يثبت بالنية قوله : ( ولا عن أحد من الصحابة والتابعين) زاد ابن أمير حاج ولا عن الأئمة الأربعة قوله : ( وهذه بدعة) قال في البحر : فتحرر من هذه الأقوال
The Book of Prayer. Its reality is that deafness? And the mute is not required to move his tongue according to the correct view. And for the non-mute, it is required that he hear his own pronunciation (according to the most correct view, as stated by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and the majority of scholars: the correct view is that loud recitation (jahr) means making others hear, and quiet recitation (mukhafatah) means making oneself hear). Al-Hindwani said: It does not suffice unless his ears and those near him hear. So hearing is a condition for what pertains to pronunciation with the tongue: the opening takbir, silent recitation, the tashahhud, remembrances, saying the name over the slaughtered animal, the obligation of prostration of recitation, manumission, divorce, exceptions, oaths, vows, Islam, faith. Even if he passes divorce through his heart and moves his tongue without being heard, it does not occur even if he corrects the letters. Al-Karkhi said: Recitation is correcting the letters even if there is no sound that can be heard. The correct view is contrary to this. The investigator Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Know that recitation, though it is an action of the tongue, his action that is speech is with letters. ... (continues with detailed commentary).
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah. It discusses a fundamental ruling: for non-mute individuals, valid pronunciation in prayer requires that one hear oneself speak. This applies to the opening takbir, silent recitation, tashahhud, and other utterances. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Hindwani requires that both one's own ears and those nearby hear, while al-Halwani and the majority hold that hearing oneself is sufficient. Al-Karkhi goes further, saying that merely correcting the letters without any sound suffices, but the text declares the correct view (al-sahih) to be the opposite. The commentary by Ibn al-Humam then analyzes the nature of speech, establishing three levels: letter (harf), sound (sawt), and breath (nafas). A letter is a quality that attaches to sound, so without sound, there is no letter and thus no speech. Therefore, recitation without audible sound is invalid, and the prayer is not valid. Finally, the passage notes that intention (niyya) is from the heart and does not require pronunciation, and that verbalizing the intention is a bid'a (innovation). The overall ruling is that hearing oneself is a condition for the validity of utterances that are fard, wajib, or sunnah in prayer.

Key Terms
المخافتة (al-mukhafatah): Quiet recitation in prayer: defined by the majority as the one reciting hearing himself, as opposed to jahr (making others hear).
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation: making others hear.
تصحيح الحروف (tashih al-huruf): Correcting the letters (articulating them correctly) without necessarily producing sound. Al-Karkhi's view that this suffices for valid recitation.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Mere indication or gesture, as opposed to actual speech. Used in the proof to distinguish soundless mouth movements from real recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (as stated in this passage), what is the minimum requirement for valid mukhafatah (quiet recitation) in prayer?
A) Only the intention and moving the tongue without sound
B) The reciter must hear his own voice
C) Both the reciter and those near him must hear the voice
D) It is not required to produce any sound at all

Key Takeaway
Quiet recitation in prayer requires the reciter to hear his own voice; mere mouth movements without sound do not constitute valid recitation.

Definition of Letter and Its Effect on Prayer Validity
Defining the components of speech and ruling on prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three levels of speech (nafs, sawt, harf) and apply the ruling that prayer recitation requires actual letters formed by sound.

Core Idea
For valid prayer recitation, a letter without sound is no letter at all.

In this lesson, we dissect the Hanafi linguistic analysis of speech as composed of breath, sound, and letter. The commentator al-Tahtawi clarifies that a letter (harf) is a quality that occurs to sound, not to breath alone. This distinction has a direct legal consequence: in prayer, recitation must consist of genuine letters produced by sound. Mere movement of the articulation muscles without sound invalidates the prayer because no real speech (kalām) occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components of speech
The text defines breath (nafs) as absolute air, sound (sawt) as air after striking, and letter (harf) as the quality that occurs to sound. Recognize each level and note that each is more specific than the one before.
Breath is the raw material, sound is breath with striking, letter is sound with articulation.
2
Understand the relationship: each is more specific
The commentator states that harf is a quality (kayfiyyah) that occurs to sound, and sound is more specific than breath. The analogy of a laughing man illustrates this: man (breath) alone is more general than laughing man (sound+letter).
The letter does not exist without sound, and sound does not exist without breath.
3
Connect to prayer validity: essential components
The ruling is that valid prayer requires recitation (qirā'ah), which is a pillar. Recitation is only realized when actual letters (huruf) are produced. Without sound, the movements are mere indications (īmā'), not real letters, so no speech occurs.
The text explicitly states: 'lā taṣiḥḥ al-ṣalāh' (prayer is invalid) if letters are not produced.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a person who moves their lips and tongue during prayer but makes no audible sound. According to this lesson, their recitation is invalid because they have not produced actual letters, only indications. Therefore, the prayer is batil.
This applies whether the person prays alone or follows an imam; recitation must be audible to oneself.
5
Note the Hanafi position and possible dissent
The Hanafi school requires actual sound for letters. Some other schools might accept mere movement, but the Hanafi ruling is that the prayer is invalid without sound. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The basis is that the Pillar of recitation (qirā'ah) is defined as speech (kalām), and speech requires letters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحرف كيفية تعرض للصوت، وهو أخص من النفس فإنّ النفس المعروض بالقرع فالحرف عارض للصوت لا للنفس فمجرد تصحيحها أي الحروف بلا صوت إيماء إلى الحروف بعضلات المخارج لا حروف فلا كلام اهـ. قوله : (الذي هو كلام) أي لا مجرد الحركة قوله: (والكلام بالحروف) مبتدأ وخبر أي لا يتحقق الكلام إلا بالحروف، والحاصل أن المراتب ثلاثة حرف وصوت ونفس وكل أخص من الذي بعده قوله: (والحرف كيفية تعرض للصوت لأنه هو الصوت المعتمد على المخارج فالكيفية هي إعتماد الصوت على المخارج، وفيه أن الحرف هو الصوت المعتمد لا الإعتماد قوله: (وهو أخص من النفس) فإن النفس هو الهواء مطلقاً اعتمد أولاً قوله : (فإنّ النفس المعروض بالقرع) أي هو الهواء الذي عرض عليه القرع يعني أن القرع بالعضلات يعرض على النفس، والصوت هو مجموع النفس مع القرع ومن المعلوم أن المعروض قد يتحقق بدون عارضه كتحقق الإنسان بدون صفة الكتابة، والمعروض، والعارض أخص من المعروض وحده كإنسان وضاحك فإنّ الإنسان فقط أعم من الإنسان الضاحك والقرع يتحقق بالعضلات قوله: (عارض للصوت)، والصوت عرض يقوم بمحل يخرج من داخل الرئة إلى خارجها مع النفس مستطيلاً ممتداً متصلاً بمقطع من مقاطع حروف الحلق واللسان والشفتين قوله: (فمجرد الخ) هو روح العلة . قوله : بلا صوت) أي بل بالنفس الذي هو مطلق الهواء. قوله : (إيماء) أي إشارة إليها والذي يومي بالشيء لا يكون آتياً بحقيقته كالمومي بالصلاة فإنه لم يأت بحقيقة الركوع، والسجود. قوله: (بعضلات المخارج) العضلات جمع العضلة، وهي كل عصبة معها لحم غليظ كذا في القاموس، والمخارج جمع مخرج محل خروج الحروف، كذا في الأزهرية فالإضافة من إضافة العام إلى الخاص . قوله : (لا حروف) عطف على إيماء أي لا حروف حقيقة، فلا كلام أي إذا انتفت الحروف انتفى الكلام أي وهو لا بد منه فإنه المطلوب شرعاً، وإذا انتفى الكلام انتفت القراءة، فلا تصح الصلاة
And the letter (harf) is a quality that occurs to sound, and it is more specific than the breath (nafs). For the breath is that which is subject to the striking (al-qar'), so the letter is an accident of sound, not of the breath. So mere correction of the letters (i.e., without sound) is an indication of the letters by the muscles of the articulation points, not actual letters, so there is no speech. End. He said: (which is speech) i.e., not mere movement. He said: (and speech is with letters) subject and predicate, i.e., speech is only realized with letters. The summary is that there are three levels: letter, sound, and breath, and each is more specific than the one after it. He said: (and the letter is a quality that occurs to sound) because it is the sound that relies on the articulation points. So the quality is the reliance of sound on the articulation points. In it is that the letter is the sound that relies, not the reliance. He said: (and it is more specific than the breath) so the breath is air absolutely, whether it relies or not. He said: (for the breath is the subject of striking) i.e., it is the air on which the striking occurs, meaning that the striking by the muscles occurs to the breath, and sound is the sum of breath and striking. It is known that the subject may exist without its accident, like the existence of a man without the attribute of writing. And the subject and accident together are more specific than the subject alone, like a man who is laughing: for man alone is more general than a laughing man. And the striking is realized by the muscles. He said: (an accident of sound), and sound is an accident that subsists in a locus, emerging from inside the lung to outside with the breath, elongated, extended, connected to a segment of the segments of the letters of the throat, tongue, and lips. He said: (so mere ...) it is the essence of the cause. He said: (without sound) i.e., rather by the breath, which is absolute air. He said: (an indication) i.e., a sign to them (the letters), and one who indicates by something does not bring the reality of that thing, like one who indicates by prayer, for he does not perform the reality of bowing and prostration. He said: (by the muscles of the articulation points) al-‘adhalāt is the plural of ‘adhalah, which is like safīnah: every sinew with thick flesh, as in al-Qāmūs. al-Makhārij is the plural of makhraj, the place of emergence of letters, as in al-Azhariyyah. So the iḍāfah is a general-to-specific iḍāfah. He said: (not letters) is a conjunct to 'indication', i.e., not real letters. So no speech, i.e., if letters are absent, speech is absent, and it (speech) is indispensable, for it is required by the Law. And if speech is absent, recitation (qirā'ah) is absent, and thus prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling commentary. It defines the technical relationship between breath (nafs), sound (sawt), and letter (harf) in the context of speech for the validity of prayer recitation. The commentator (al-Tahtawi) explains that the letter (harf) is a quality (kayfiyyah) that occurs to sound, not to breath alone. Breath is the raw air, sound is air that undergoes striking (qar‘) by the muscles of the articulation points, and the letter is the specific form that sound takes when it passes through a particular articulation point. The key ruling: if a person merely moves the articulation muscles without producing sound, they are only indicating the letters, not producing them. Hence, no real speech is achieved. In prayer, valid recitation (qirā'ah) requires actual speech (kalām) composed of real letters. Without it, the prayer is invalid (lā taṣiḥḥ al-ṣalāh). The commentator uses analogies (e.g., a man laughing) to illustrate the relationship. The point is that the follower must actually voice the letters; mere mental articulation is insufficient.

Key Terms
حرف (harf): A quality that occurs to sound, making it specific to a particular articulation point. It is the sound after it has been shaped by the makhraj.
صوت (sawt): An accident that subsists in a locus, emerging from the lung with breath, after being struck (qar‘) by the muscles of the articulation points, elongated and connected to a makhraj.
نفس (nafs): Absolute air, the raw material that is the subject (maʻrūḍ) of the striking (qarʻ) that produces sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the consequence if a person in prayer merely indicates the letters with the muscles of the articulation points without producing sound?
A) The recitation is valid if the movements are correct.
B) The prayer is valid but disliked.
C) The prayer is invalid because no actual letters (huruf) are produced.
D) Only the first takbir is affected, the rest of the prayer is fine.

Key Takeaway
For valid prayer recitation, actual letters formed by sound are required; mere muscle movement without sound invalidates the prayer.

Ruling on Vocalizing the Intention (Talfuz bi-l-Niyyah)
Examining the legal status of vocalizing the intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vocalizing the intention and explain why it is not a sunnah, while identifying the exception for gathering resolve.

Core Idea
Intention is an act of the heart; vocalizing it is not required and is a bid'ah unless done silently to strengthen resolve.

Many Muslims habitually whisper their intention before prayer, but what is the actual ruling? This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi examines the legal status of talfuz bi-l-niyyah, drawing on the opinion of Ibn Qayyim and later Hanafi authorities. It clarifies that the intention is purely a matter of the heart, and vocalizing it is neither a sunnah nor obligatory, though it may be permissible in certain circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that intention (niyyah) is an act of the heart, not the tongue, as the passage states 'speech is not a condition for it'.
2
Examine the evidence from Ibn Qayyim
Analyze Ibn Qayyim's claim that no hadith (sound or weak) reports the Prophet (ﷺ) or the Companions vocalizing the intention. This absence of evidence is used to argue that the practice is not part of the Sunnah.
This is a dalil naqli based on non-establishment.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) considered it sunnah (meaning a practice of the scholars, not the Prophet), while others, like Ibn Qayyim, called it a bid'ah. The passage reconciles by labeling it 'bid'ah hasanah' when done to strengthen resolve.
4
Derive the practical ruling (mufta bihi)
The relied-upon position: vocalizing the intention is not required; doing so loudly is makruh tanzihi; silently is permissible (mubah). It is not a sunnah.
Source: Al-Tahtawi cites al-Bahr and al-Fath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن متعلقات القلب النية للإخلاص فلا يشترط لها النطق كالكفر بالنية قال الحافظ ابن قيم الجوزي رحمه الله تعالى لم يثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم طريق صحيح ولا ضعيف إنه كان يقول عند الإفتتاح أصلي كذا ولا عن أحد من الصحابة والتابعين، بل المنقول أنه كان إذا قام إلى الصلاة كبر وهذه بدعة اهـ، وفي الروايات التلفظ بالنية كرهه البعض لأنّ عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه أدب من فعله. قال في الشرح : تنبيه في إشتراط النطق بالتحريمة إشارة إلى أنه لا يشترط النطق بالنية لأنها من متعلقات القلب التي لا يشترط لها النطق، وقد أجمع العلماء على أنه لو نوى بقلبه، ولم يتكلم بنيته فإنه يجوز اهـ. قوله : (بالنية) متعلق بمحذوف أي يثبت بالنية قوله : ( ولا عن أحد من الصحابة والتابعين) زاد ابن أمير حاج ولا عن الأئمة الأربعة قوله : ( وهذه بدعة) قال في البحر : فتحرر من هذه الأقوال فساد التلفظ بالنية وأنه بدعة حسنة عند قصد جمع العزيمة اهـ. قال في الفتح بعد قول الهداية أنه حسن لإجتماع عزيمته اهـ وقد يفهم أنه لا يحسن لغير هذا القصد قوله : (لم يرد بها سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العلامة نوح : وكذا القائل بالاستحباب لعله أراد به الأمر المحبوب في نظر المشايخ لا في نظر الشارع لأن المستحب قسم من السنة اهـ وفي القهستاني وينبغي أن تكون النية بلفظ الماضي، ولو فارسياً لأنه الغالب في الإنشاآت فيقول : نويت صلاة كذا اهـ ملخصاً.
And from the things related to the heart is the intention (niyyah) for sincerity. So speech is not a condition for it, just as unbelief (kufr) can be by intention. Al-Hafiz Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyyah (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It has not been established from the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) by a sound or weak chain that he used to say at the beginning of prayer: 'I pray such and such,' nor from any of the Companions or the Successors. Rather, what is transmitted is that when he stood for prayer, he would say takbir, and this is a bid'ah. In the narrations, some disliked vocalizing the intention because 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) disciplined someone who did it. He said in the Sharh: A note regarding the condition of speech for the opening takbir indicates that speech is not a condition for the intention because it (intention) is from the matters of the heart for which speech is not required. The scholars have agreed that if one intends with his heart and does not speak his intention, it is permissible. He said: (by the intention) is attached to an omitted word, i.e., it is established by intention. He said: (nor from any of the Companions and the Successors) Ibn Amir Haj added: nor from the four Imams. He said: (and this is a bid'ah) He said in al-Bahr: It becomes clear from these statements the invalidity of vocalizing the intention and that it is a good bid'ah (bid'ah hasanah) when intending to gather one's resolve. He said in al-Fath after the statement of al-Hidayah that it is good (hasan) for gathering one's resolve. And it may be understood that it is not good for other than this purpose. He said: (It was not intended as a sunnah of the Prophet) Al-Allamah Nuh said: Similarly, the one who says it is recommended (mustahabb) perhaps meant by it the thing that is beloved in the view of the mashayikh, not in the view of the Lawgiver, because mustahabb is a part of sunnah. And in al-Qahistani: It is appropriate that the intention be in the past tense, even in Persian, because it is common in constructions; so he says: 'I intended such a prayer' — summarized.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute commentary on the ruling of vocalizing the intention (talfuz bi-l-niyyah) in prayer. The commentator presents evidence from Ibn Qayyim that no authentic hadith supports the practice, and that it is a bid'ah. However, later scholars note that it may be considered a 'good bid'ah' (bid'ah hasanah) if done to strengthen resolve. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that vocalizing the intention is not a sunnah and is not required. The practice is disliked (makruh) if done loudly, as 'Umar disciplined someone for it. However, if done silently (mukhāfatan), it is permissible, and some scholars consider it good for gathering one's concentration. The passage emphasizes that intention is an act of the heart, and speech is not a condition. Thus, the correct view is that it is not necessary, but if done silently for a valid reason, it is not blameworthy. The dispute is among Hanafi scholars: some call it sunnah (but mean sunnah of the mashayikh, not of the Prophet), while others label it bid'ah. The fatwa is that it is not recommended, but permissible if done quietly.

Key Terms
تلفظ بالنية (talfuz bi-l-niyyah): Vocalizing the intention, i.e., uttering words like 'I intend to pray such and such' at the beginning of prayer.
بدعة حسنة (bid'ah hasanah): A good innovation, i.e., an innovation that serves a beneficial purpose and is not contrary to the spirit of the Law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone vocalizes the intention loudly at the beginning of prayer?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is a sunnah.
C) It is disliked (makruh), as 'Umar disciplined someone for it.
D) It is recommended (mustahabb) according to all Hanafi scholars.

Key Takeaway
Vocalizing the intention is not a required or recommended part of prayer; it is permissible only when done silently for a valid purpose.

Follower's Intention: Niyyat al-Mutaba'ah in Congregational Prayer
Condition and scope of niyyat al-mutaba'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the follower's intention of following, explain why the correct view allows intending only following, and apply the rule regarding not specifying the imam.

Core Idea
The follower's intention of following is wajib; intending it alone suffices, but mere waiting does not.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) must have an intention of following the imam. This lesson examines a critical refinement within the Hanafi school: what exactly constitutes a valid intention of following? The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies three positions, the preferred view, and important practical advice about naming the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
What is the act? The follower's intention of following (niyyat al-mutaba'ah). What is its ruling? It is a condition (shart) for the validity of congregational prayer, and according to the Hanafi school it is wajib.
Note that conditions are not arkan; omission invalidates without compensation.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the three positions: (1) Intending only following without specifying the prayer suffices (al-aṣaḥḥ). (2) It does not suffice (qīl). (3) Waiting for the imam's takbir suffices (qīl), but the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) says it does not.
The terms 'al-aṣaḥḥ' and 'al-ṣaḥīḥ' indicate preferred views.
3
Analyze the tarjih mechanism
Why does the text prefer the view that intending only following suffices? Because it implies absolute commitment (ittibā‘ muṭlaq). The follower has made himself a follower entirely, and that is sufficient.
Contrast with the view that requires specifying the prayer, which is considered a stricter but less preferred approach.
4
Examine the qiyas on waiting
Why is waiting insufficient? The passage uses a rational argument: waiting is ambiguous (mutaraddid) – it could be for worship or for habit. Without a conscious intention to follow, the follower cannot be considered muqtadi.
This is a qiyas jaliy: waiting is analogized to a case where intention is clearly formed.
5
Apply the rule on not naming the imam
What is the ruling on naming the imam? The follower should not specify the imam by name, because if mistaken, the prayer may be invalid due to the intention not matching reality.
Practical advice: simply intend to follow the imam without naming him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الخامس منها (نية المتابعة) مع نية أصل الصلاة (للمقتدي) أما النية المشتركة فلما تقدم وأما الخاصة وهي نية الاقتداء فلما يلحقه صلاة إمامه لأنه بالالتزام فينوي فرض الوقت والاقتداء بالإمام فيه أو ينوي الشروع في صلاة الإمام ولو نوى الاقتداء لا غير قيل لا يجزيه والأصح أنه يجوز لأنه جعل نفسه تبعاً للإمام مطلقاً والتبعية إنما تتحقق إذا صار مصلياً ما صلاه الإمام وقيل متى انتظر تكبير الإمام كفاه عن نية الاقتداء والصحيح أنه لا مقتدياً. يصير بمجرد الإنتظار لأنه متردد بين كونه للاقتداء أو العادة وينبغي أن لا يعين الإمام خشية بطلان الصلاة بظهوره خلافه ولو ظنه زيداً فإذا هو عمرو
(And) the fifth of them (the conditions? intentions?) is the intention of following (niyyat al-mutāba‘ah) along with the intention of the original prayer (for the follower). As for the common intention (niyyah mushtarakah), it has preceded. As for the specific intention, which is the intention of following (niyyat al-iqtidā‘), it is because he is affected by the prayer of his imam, for it (the prayer) is binding upon him. So he intends the obligatory prayer of the time and following the imam in it, or he intends the commencement of the prayer of the imam (i.e., along with the imam). And if he intends following only (without specifying the prayer), some said it does not suffice him, but the correct view is that it is permissible, because he has made himself a follower of the imam absolutely. And following is only realized when he becomes a performer of what the imam performed. And some said: Whenever he waits for the takbir of the imam, that suffices him for the intention of following. But the correct view is that he does not become a follower merely by waiting, because he is undecided between whether it is for following or from habit. And it is appropriate that he should not specify the imam (by name), for fear of invalidation of his prayer if the imam turns out to be someone else. For example, if he thought the imam was Zayd, but it turned out to be 'Amr.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute commentary on the follower's intention (niyyat al-mutāba‘ah). It addresses the requirement for a person praying behind an imam (muqtadi) to have an intention of following. The common intention (niyyah mushtarakah) is the intention of the prayer itself, which is shared between imam, follower, and individual. The specific intention (niyyah khāṣṣah) is the intention of following (iqtidā‘). The follower must intend both: the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and following the imam in it. If he only intends to follow without specifying the prayer, there is a dispute: some (qīl) say it does not suffice, but the correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that it suffices because he has committed himself to follow the imam absolutely. Being a follower means he performs what the imam performs. Another opinion says that merely waiting for the imam's takbir suffices, but the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) is that it does not, because waiting can be ambiguous. The text also advises that the follower should not specify the imam by name, because if he mistakenly identifies him, the prayer may be invalid. This is a rational legal analysis (dalīl 'aqlī) based on the nature of commitment and the requirement of certainty in intention.

Key Terms
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutāba‘ah): The intention of the follower to follow the imam in prayer, which is a condition for the validity of congregational prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) in this passage, does merely waiting for the imam's takbir make one a follower (muqtadi)?
A) Yes, it suffices.
B) No, because waiting is ambiguous between worship and habit.
C) Yes, if he has a general intention to pray.
D) Only if he also specifies the imam's name.

Key Takeaway
The follower must intentionally commit to follow the imam; a general intention of following suffices, but mere waiting does not, and naming the imam is discouraged.

Conditions of Intention in the Opening Takbir
Critical commentary on three conditions of intention in the tahrimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intention-related conditions for the validity of the opening takbir and apply the Hanafi position on the combination of fard and nafl intentions.

Core Idea
Intention in the takbir requires following the imam, specifying the fard, and specifying the wajib; conflicting intentions are resolved by strength.

The opening takbir (tahrimah) is the gateway to prayer; its validity depends on a correct intention. In this passage, al-Tahtawi clarifies three subtle conditions: the muqtadi must intend to follow the imam, the fard prayer must be specified when multiple prayers overlap, and wajib prayers also require specification. He also addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining fard and nafl intentions, a practical issue for the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
The commentary lists three conditions: (5) intention of following the imam for the muqtadi, (6) specification of the fard prayer, (7) specification of the wajib prayer. Note that these are conditions for the validity of the takbir itself.
The first four conditions are covered earlier in the text.
2
Analyse the condition of following the imam
For the muqtadi, the intention must include both the prayer and following the imam. The text discusses scenarios: intending only to follow is sufficient, but mere waiting for the takbir is not. Specifying the imam by name is not required.
The Hanafi view is distinct from the Shafi'i school.
3
Examine the specification of fard
When a worshipper begins prayer, he must specify which fard he is praying (e.g., Zuhr). If he intends a fard and later mistakenly thinks it is nafl, it remains fard. The number of rak'ahs is not required to be intended.
Jumu'ah must be specified by name, not just 'farḍ al-waqt'.
4
Understand the combination of fard and nafl
If a person intends both a fard and a nafl in the same takbir, Abu Yusuf rules that the fard prevails due to its strength, while Muhammad rules that both are invalid due to conflict. The relied-upon view is Abu Yusuf's.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
5
Apply the specification of wajib
The seventh condition applies to wajib prayers: making up a ruined nafl, vows, Witr, two rak'ahs of Tawaf, and the two Eids. Each requires specific intention because their causes differ.
The condition is necessary to distinguish from other prayers.

And we restricted it to the follower because intention of imamah is not required for men, but for women. (And) the sixth of the conditions of validity of the takbir is: (Specification of the obligatory prayer) at the beginning of entering, such that if he intends an obligatory prayer and enters into it, then forgets and thinks it is voluntary, and completes it on that assumption, then it is a valid obligatory prayer (that fulfills the obligation). Similarly, its opposite becomes voluntary. And intention of the number of rak'ahs is not required. And because of variation, the crowding of obligatory prayers makes specification of what he prays necessary, like Zuhr for example. And if he intends the obligatory prayer of the time, it is valid except in Jumu'ah. And if he combines intention of obligatory and voluntary, it is valid for the obligatory due to its strength according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He does not enter into either of them due to conflict. And if he intends voluntary and funeral prayer, it is voluntary. And if he intends prescribed and funeral, it is prescribed. Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary (hashiyah) by al-Tahtawi on the conditions of the opening takbir (tahrimah) in prayer, specifically the fifth, sixth, and seventh conditions relating to intention (niyyah). The fifth condition is that for a follower (muqtadi), the intention must include the intention to follow the imam (niyyat al-mutaba'ah) in addition to the intention of the prayer itself. The commentary clarifies that the 'common intention' refers to the intention of the original prayer (e.g., intending to pray the obligatory time prayer), while the 'specific intention' is the intention of following the imam. It is necessary because the follower becomes bound by the imam's prayer. The follower must intend both the prayer and following the imam, either by including both in one intention or by intending to enter into the imam's prayer. If he only intends to follow without specifying the prayer, the more correct view is that it is valid because he makes himself a follower absolutely. However, merely waiting for the imam's takbir without an explicit intention is insufficient because the follower remains hesitant. It is recommended not to specify the imam by name, as that might invalidate the prayer if the imam turns out to be someone else; if he mistakenly thinks the imam is Zayd but it is Amr, the prayer remains valid. Intention of imamah is not required for men leading prayer, but it is recommended for women leading women. The sixth condition is specification of the obligatory prayer (ta'yin al-fard). When starting the takbir, the worshipper must intend which specific obligatory prayer he is performing (e.g., Zuhr, Asr). If he initially intends a fard, forgets and thinks it is voluntary but completes it, it counts as that fard. The opposite also applies: if he intends voluntary and later thinks it is fard, it becomes voluntary. Intention of the number of rak'ahs is not required because the obligatory prayers have fixed numbers. However, due to multiple prayers overlapping (tazahum al-furud), specifying which one is necessary. For Jumu'ah, one must intend specifically Jumu'ah, not just 'the obligatory prayer of the time', because the time is for Zuhr according to the Hanafi school. If one combines intention of fard and nafl, according to Abu Yusuf, the stronger (fard) prevails; according to Muhammad, both are invalid due to conflict. If one combines intention of nafl and funeral prayer, it is nafl (stronger), and if he was leading, he must repeat the funeral prayer and also make up the nafl. If one combines intention of a prescribed prayer (maktubah) and funeral, it is maktubah because it is fard 'ayn and a complete prayer. The seventh condition is specification of wajib prayers, which includes make-up of a ruined voluntary, vows, Witr, two rak'ahs of Tawaf, and the two Eid prayers. These require specific intention because their causes differ. The commentary notes that these seven conditions are not all required in every prayer; for example, a nafl prayer does not require specification of fard.

Key Terms
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutaba'ah): The intention of following the imam in prayer, required for the validity of the muqtadi's opening takbir.
تعيين الفرض (ta'yin al-fard): Specifying which obligatory prayer one intends to perform, required when multiple prayers are possible in the time.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The person praying behind an imam, who must intend to follow the imam.
تعيين الواجب (ta'yin al-wajib): Specifying which wajib prayer (e.g., Witr, Eid) one intends, required because their causes differ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muqtadi combines intention of a fard prayer and a nafl prayer in the same takbir, what is the ruling?
A) Both prayers are valid if the muqtadi intended both.
B) Only the nafl is valid because it is more virtuous.
C) Only the fard is valid, according to the relied-upon view (Abu Yusuf).
D) Neither is valid, according to the relied-upon view.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir requires specific intentions for following the imam, specifying the fard (or wajib), and in case of conflict, the stronger obligation prevails.
